- **Deference to seniors**: stable. No measurable decrease across years. Peter, Cap, Jessica Drew, Jefferson, eventually his teachers and college advisors — he defers to all of them past the point of self-interest.
- **Self-deprecating interior monologue**: increases. The narrative captions in the Ahmed solo are notably more self-critical than the Bendis-era captions, even adjusting for writer.
- **Capacity for sustained joy**: improves. Sequences with Ganke, with Gwen, with Billie, with his parents at the dinner table show genuine, unguarded affect in a way the early *USM* almost never permitted. The *waiting-for-the-other-shoe* affect remains, but it now coexists with present-tense pleasure rather than foreclosing it.
- **Sleep architecture**: chronically degraded. No improvement detected across the entire middle period. This is the somatic indicator most resistant to intervention.

---

## J. Summary of the Middle Period

What this stretch produces is a subject who has *survived* far more than he has *integrated*. The wounds — Aaron, Rio, the prophecy, the anomaly verdict, the shadow-clones — have all been borne; none have been fully resolved. The defense structures (compartmentalization, deference, over-functioning, reparation) have hardened from improvisations into character. The powers have been brought under conscious regulation in a way that was not possible at debut; the *self*-concept has not undergone an equivalent integration.


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

## SUBJECT: MORALES, MILES GONZALO — present-tense disposition, ~age 17, Brooklyn-based, operational

---

## 6.1 The Frame of "Recent"

"Recent" in this file means the post-Ahmed window through the Cody Ziglar run on *Miles Morales: Spider-Man* (Vol. 2, 2022–2024), the *Spider-Boy* spin-off (Dan Slott, 2023–present), the *Gang War* crossover (2023–24), the *Ultimate Universe* re-launch's adjacency effects (Hickman, 2023–present — note that this Miles is *not* the Ultimate Miles, but the existence of a parallel Ultimate Peter recursively reactivates predecessor anxieties — see §6.7), continuing *Spider-Verse / Edge of Spider-Verse* appearances, and the *Sinister War / Dark Web* aftermath. Functional age: late high school transitioning to early college. Operational tenure as Spider-Man: approximately four in-universe years, an order of magnitude more than the typical adolescent costumed subject survives.

The defining feature of this era is that the subject is *no longer the new one*. He has aged into mid-tier seniority within the New York hero ecology. This is the single largest unresolved psychological pressure on him at present, because his entire self-concept (see §3, §5) is organized around provisionality and inheritance, and provisionality has a half-life. He is being forced — by the simple passage of time and the arrival of *actually* newer figures (Spider-Boy / Bailey Briggs being the most acute case) — to occupy a position he has spent four years arguing he had not earned.

---

## 6.2 The Ziglar Run — Operational Centerlining

Cody Ziglar's *MM:SM* (2022–24) is the document of record for current-state behavior. Key longitudinal observations:

- **Solo operational base.** Subject is now running his own caseload out of Brooklyn — Sunset Park / Bay Ridge / Red Hook corridor — with minimal Peter Parker overlap. Patrol geography has stabilized: a roughly triangular sweep from the Verrazzano approach northeast through Prospect Park to the Williamsburg waterfront, with a hard preference for rooftops on the Brooklyn side of the East River. He crosses to Manhattan reactively, not proactively. This is a meaningful change from the early *USM* years when he piggybacked on Peter's Manhattan patrol routes; he has built a *territory*, which is a quiet but significant assertion of legitimacy he is not yet aware he has made.

- **Caseload composition.** Smaller-scale, neighborhood-level: muggings, gang escalation, displaced metahuman juveniles, the Assessor (the Roxxon-adjacent biotech antagonist introduced in the run) and his harvested kid-soldiers. He is gravitating toward cases involving exploited adolescents — a near-perfect reaction-formation projection (see §3) of his own clone-arc material onto external rescuees.

- **Introduction of Shift's reabsorption / non-reabsorption.** The clone fragments continue to occupy operational and emotional bandwidth. Shift in particular functions as a live unresolved-self artifact; subject has not killed him, will not let others kill him, refuses to absorb him, and has no working long-term plan. This is diagnostic: when forced to choose between a tidy resolution and an open-ended moral relationship, he chooses the latter every time, at cost to himself.

- **Introduction of younger sister Billie Morales (b. *Spider-Man* Vol. 3 #240, 2020, now ~3–4).** Billie is the single largest behavioral modifier in the recent file. Patrol cadence is now shaped around bedtime stories and weekend mornings. He has been observed cutting fights short to make a 7:30 PM read-aloud. This is not weakness; it is the first time in the canon that he has *organized his hero-time around a non-negotiable family demand* rather than the reverse. Compare *USM* #1–28, where family time was the residual after patrol. The inversion is structurally important.

- **Rabbit (Beyond Corporation antagonist) arc.** Subject is targeted by a corporate-backed assassin specifically engineered to bait the venom-blast — the antagonist's armor harvests bio-electric discharge. This forces him into the operationally novel posture of *suppressing* his most autonomic ability for tactical reasons. He spends an arc effectively fighting one-handed against his own nervous system. Observable consequence: increased reliance on camouflage (the avoidant pole) and on hand-to-hand. Net effect on baseline: he has, by exposure therapy, become measurably better at not discharging under stress. The somatic-anxiety coupling described in §2 is partially loosening.

---

## 6.3 The Bailey Briggs Problem (*Spider-Boy*)

The 2023 introduction of Bailey Briggs — a forgotten sidekick whose existence has been restored to continuity, who calls himself Spider-Boy, who is *younger* than Miles, and who explicitly looks to Miles the way Miles once looked to Peter — is the most psychologically loaded development in the current file.

Surveillance-grade observations on Miles's response pattern:

- **First-meeting affect.** Confusion (cognitive), warmth (interpersonal), and a flash of something the file would code as *displacement-anxiety* — Bailey occupies the structural position (the new kid, the borrowed mantle, the kid who needs blessing from elders) that Miles has organized his entire identity around. Miles is now, against his self-concept, the elder.

- **Behavior under the demand to mentor.** He has been observed doing it badly *on purpose* — undercutting his own authority, deflecting Bailey's deference, framing himself as "still figuring it out." This is the same defense (idealization-upward, deference) deployed in a downward direction. He does not know how to *be* the Peter in someone else's story, because being the Peter would require him to concede that he is no longer the Miles.

- **What he is actually doing for Bailey, watched closely.** Showing up. Answering the phone. Modeling restraint. He is, in operational fact, mentoring well. The discrepancy between performance (competent older-brother) and self-narration ("I have no idea what I'm doing") is itself the entire current-state diagnostic in miniature.

---

## 6.4 The Father Disclosure — Status Update

The single most consequential interpersonal event of the post-2015 era — the eventual revelation to Jefferson Davis that his son is Spider-Man — has by the current window matured into a *stable working relationship* between father and son around the secret. Jefferson knows. Rio knows. The disclosure occurred (across staggered points in the Bendis Vol. 1/Vol. 2 and Saladin Ahmed runs), the Aaron-death-disclosure has been at least partially processed, and the family now operates as an aware unit.

Current observable patterns:

- **Jefferson's role has shifted from antagonist-of-the-secret to logistical accomplice.** He covers for school absences in narrow circumstances; he has a coded set of phrases used over speakerphone when Rio is in the room and unaware of an active situation (rare; she is now mostly read in). The household has, in effect, developed an operational tradecraft.

- **Rio's role is the harder one to read.** She does not endorse the work; she does not forbid it; she has settled into a posture of *witnessed grief in advance* — she behaves around Miles as a person who has decided to love him through a thing she cannot stop and may not survive. The 2015 reality-shift means she does not consciously remember dying in his arms; the subject carries that memory alone. Behavioral tell: he touches her shoulder or hand more often than a 17-year-old typically touches his mother. Documented across multiple writers. He is checking that she is corporeal.

- **Family dinner is sacred.** Sunday dinners at the Morales apartment are the most reliably scheduled event in his life — more reliable than patrol, school, or Champions calls. He has stood up gods for it.

---

## 6.5 The Ganke Relationship — Long-Form Status

Ganke Lee remains the central non-family attachment. Current configuration:

- They are no longer dorm roommates in the Vol. 2 era as they were in *USM*; geographic proximity has loosened. Contact is daily, sometimes hourly, via text. The texting register is heavily abbreviated, meme-saturated, and operationally coded — Ganke is still the *only* person who knew first and the only one who has never wavered.
- Ganke has become, functionally, the subject's auxiliary executive function: reminds him of assignments, of his sister's recital, of the fact that he has not eaten. Surveillance-grade detail: Ganke's phone contains a running half-private spreadsheet (referenced obliquely in dialogue) tracking Miles's known injuries and recovery times. This is care infrastructure built by a teenager for a teenager.
- The relationship has *no romantic subtext, no rivalry, no fracture line.* Across thirteen years of publication it is the most stable dyad in the file. Operationally, it is also his single largest disclosure vulnerability — anyone who fully understands the Miles-Ganke pattern can find Miles through Ganke. He knows this and has not modified the relationship to mitigate.

---

## 6.6 Romantic and Adjacent — Current Standing

The Vol. 2 era has him in a longer, more stable relationship than any prior — Starling (Tiana Toomes, Vulture's granddaughter), introduced in Vol. 3 and carried through Ziglar's run. Pattern observations:

- She knows. He told her. This is the *first* romantic relationship in which the disclosure problem (§5) has been solved at the front end rather than at the breaking point. This is developmental progress and should be logged as such.
- She is morally ambiguous — she has run with criminal-adjacent figures and has her own relationship to a villain-elder (Toomes). The subject has chosen, for the first time, a partner whose moral situation *mirrors his own anxieties* (the criminal uncle, the inherited darkness, the "am I just like him") rather than a partner who functions as a moral anchor. Two readings: (a) he is using the relationship to externalize and work through the shadow material; (b) he is recreating the Aaron dynamic in safer form. Both are true. The relationship is therapeutic and risky in the same gesture.
- Behavioral tell during disagreements with Starling: he goes quiet rather than escalates. He has not learned to fight in a relationship; he has learned to *withdraw and process and return*. The Ganke template is bleeding into the romantic template.

---

## 6.7 Adjacent-Universe Pressure: the New Ultimate Peter

The 2023 Hickman *Ultimate Spider-Man* launch — featuring an adult, married, late-arriving Peter Parker in a separate Ultimate continuity — has no direct in-story contact with the subject at present, but it activates a deep file-historic resonance. The subject *was* the Ultimate Spider-Man. The slot has been refilled, by an adult, in a different universe, without him. The publishing reality and the diegetic reality are bleeding together for in-universe meta-aware Spider-figures (a recurring *Spider-Verse* conceit). Whether or not the subject has on-page acknowledged this, the structural fact — *there is again an Ultimate Spider-Man and it is not me* — is the kind of thing his self-concept will metabolize as further evidence of provisionality. Watch this. Future writers will use it.

---

## 6.8 Gang War / Street-Level Posture

The Zeb Wells *Gang War* event (2023–24) put the subject into sustained contact with Hammerhead, Madame Masque, Tombstone, and the rest of the consolidated New York organized-crime layer. Operational behaviors during the event, in summary:

- He defaulted to *neighborhood defense* over *enemy pursuit.* While other Spider-figures (Peter, Spider-Woman, Jessica) drove toward the kingpin-level antagonists, Miles spent the event on Brooklyn corners, in housing projects, in the specific blocks where his family lives and where Billie's daycare is.
- He coordinated, briefly, with Hobie Brown (the Prowler — note the surname/iconography overlap with Aaron). The relationship is cautious; Miles is uneasy around any "Prowler," for reasons the file makes obvious.
- He did not kill, did not maim, and de-escalated three documented confrontations that other heroes resolved with force. The Champions ethic (§5) held under street-war conditions, which is a real stress test and which he passed.

---

## 6.9 School / Civilian Trajectory

Brooklyn Visions Academy → graduating arc / transition to college in the most recent stories. Academic standing: still high, with documented slippage during peak operational windows. The subject has begun, for the first time, considering college choices that would *take him out of New York* — a deliberation framed entirely around guilt (leaving Brooklyn unprotected; leaving his parents; leaving Billie) rather than around aspiration. He has not chosen. The decision is presently pending and is one of the live narrative threads.

Note the diagnostic: a 17-year-old should be choosing a college around what he wants. He is choosing around what he would be abandoning. The provisional self-concept (§5) extends to his civilian future, not just the cape.

---

## 6.10 The Champions Hiatus

The Champions as a formal unit are presently dormant (post-*Outlawed*, post-Kamala Khan complications, post-Vision-related fallout). The subject has not led a team in the current window. The Young Avengers / Champions cohort is dispersed. He maintains private contact with Kamala (text-frequent), Sam Alexander (intermittent), Amadeus Cho (rare). The absence of the team is felt; he has not sought to reconstitute it, which is in character — he will join a thing, he will hold a thing together, he will not *start* a thing. This remains a developmental edge.

---

## 6.11 Current Somatic and Behavioral Baseline (Granular)

- **Sleep:** approximately 5–6 hours on patrol nights, 7–8 on family nights, recovery debt chronic but compensated by enhanced physiology. Documented bad dreams during *USM* #200 anniversary windows (writers have used this).
- **Diet:** high-volume, irregular. Bodega-dependent. Specific tells: a standing order at a Sunset Park spot (sandwich + iced tea), Pop-Tarts as patrol fuel, his mother's cooking as the recovery meal of record.
- **Music:** running headphones tell. Hip-hop heavy, with documented preference for older NY catalogue (Big Pun, Biggie) alongside contemporary Brooklyn artists. Plays loud enough to leak when he is in a low mood; volume calibration is a usable affect indicator.
- **Phone behavior:** texts in short bursts, uses voice notes with Ganke specifically, screens calls from unknown numbers (operational hygiene), never silences his mother.
- **Clothing (civilian):** hoodie-default, sneakers (kept clean — small vanity, longitudinally stable), backpack always with him and always containing a folded suit. He has not been observed without the suit on his person in any current-era appearance where the location is known. This is operational discipline that has hardened into superstition.
- **Tics:** rubs the back of his neck when uncertain; looks up-and-left during moral deliberation (writer-consistent tell across Bendis, Ahmed, Ziglar); cracks his knuckles before drop-offs from height; mouths the word *okay* to himself before re-entering a fight he disengaged from.
- **Suit:** current iteration is his own design, evolved well past the Peter-Parker-knockoff origin. Black-and-red, mask cut he has refined. He has stopped apologizing for the costume. This is a small but real milestone.

---

## 6.12 The Standing Open Questions (Current State)

What the file cannot yet close on, and which determine his trajectory from here:

1. **Will he grant himself the mantle?** The arc described across the entire workup — substitute-for to *be* — is incomplete. Current evidence suggests he is closer than he was, but the integration is asymptotic, not yet achieved. The Bailey Briggs mirror is the most likely accelerant.

2. **Will he leave New York for college?** A binary with profound consequences. Staying entrenches the neighborhood-protector identity but stalls individuation. Leaving forces a renegotiation of every relationship in the file.

3. **Will Rio's restored life hold, and how will he react if it does not?** He is operating with a buried somatic memory of her death. Any future threat to her will activate trauma far in excess of the proximate event. This is his largest single vulnerability and any sophisticated antagonist will identify it.

4. **Will Shift / the clone material be resolved or remain ambient?** He has chosen open-ended responsibility. The cost is ongoing bandwidth and the constant proximity of a literal "bad Miles" who could be weaponized against him.

5. **Will the disclosure-front in his romantic life hold under stress?** Starling-knowing-from-the-start is a new variable. The pattern has not been pressure-tested by a crisis-grade event.

6. **What happens when Peter Parker is unavailable?** He has not yet had to operate in a Marvel New York without a Peter Parker as a reachable elder. The day he does is the day the inheritance question is forced.

---

## 6.13 Net Current Disposition

A seventeen-year-old in Brooklyn, sleeping in his own bed in his parents' apartment, with a younger sister who calls him by his name, a best friend who tracks his concussions in a spreadsheet, a girlfriend who knows the secret, a father who covers for him, a mother whose hand he touches more than he needs to, a suit folded in his backpack, a patrol route he has built without realizing he built it, a kid in a knockoff costume looking up to him the way he used to look up, an open question about college, an open question about himself, and — for the first window in his published existence — no acute loss in the immediate rearview. He is, presently, *in the calm.* The file's standing prediction: he will not believe he deserves the calm, and will use it to over-prepare for the next loss rather than to integrate the gains. The arc continues. The permission has not yet been granted. He is, on every available metric, doing the work.


## Medical History

# UATU DOSSIER — SUBJECT: MORALES, MILES GONZALO
## SECTION 2 (EXPANDED): MEDICAL HISTORY

---

### 2.1 Constitutional baseline and pre-event profile (birth – age 13)

Subject is a singleton birth, full-term, delivered at a Brooklyn hospital to a Puerto Rican mother (Rio Morales, RN, with intimate working knowledge of clinical environments — relevant later because it explains the family's domestic first-aid competence) and an African-American father (Jefferson Davis, history of orthopedic load injuries consistent with manual labor and an undocumented prior period of street-level violence; subject has, on multiple occasions, observed his father's old scars without commentary, a piece of household data he files away). Apgar, neonatal screen, immunization compliance: presumed unremarkable; subject is consistently depicted at developmentally appropriate height-for-age curves, lean somatotype, mesomorphic adolescent build by age 14, never depicted with childhood obesity, asthma, eczema, or any of the pediatric chronic conditions a charter-school medical record would surface.

No pediatric surgeries on record. No tonsillectomy, no orthopedic interventions, no orthodontia (his dentition is consistently depicted as straight and intact, including after combat dental risk). No allergies of note; he eats peanut products, shellfish (school cafeteria scenes), and standard urban-Latino household cuisine without reaction. Vision and hearing intact pre-bite, intact post-bite, never depicted in corrective lenses. Handedness: right-dominant, with developed bilateral coordination post-transformation that is plausibly trained rather than congenital.

The family carries no documented genetic disease load. Maternal-line Puerto Rican ancestry raises baseline statistical risk for type II diabetes and hypertension downstream; neither has manifested. Paternal-side morbidity is essentially traumatic rather than genetic — Aaron Davis (uncle) died violently in his early forties; Jefferson carries injuries consistent with a former criminal life. Subject has therefore grown up with **somatic evidence in his household that violence is the family's primary health problem.** This is not in any chart, but it is in his head.

### 2.2 The envenomation event (*Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man* #1, age 13)

The transformative medical event of his life occurs in Aaron Davis's Brooklyn apartment when an Oscorp-engineered arachnid (catalogued **Specimen #42**, a sibling-iteration of the spider that altered Peter Parker, carrying a refined OZ-formula payload) bites him on the dorsum of the right hand. Bite is a paired puncture; he scratches it; he does not initially report it to either parent.

The clinical evolution over the subsequent 24–72 hours is exactly what an envenomation chart would record if anyone were taking it:

- **Local reaction:** erythema, mild swelling, persistent itch, no necrosis. He scratches the site repeatedly across the next day (a hand-tic that recurs under stress for months afterward — observable in *USM* #2–#4 — and which appears, decades-of-page-time later, to have extinguished, suggesting full resolution of the wound and probable habituation/extinction of the gesture).
- **Systemic acute reaction:** subject reports feeling "weird," loses consciousness or comes close to it, experiences disorientation in his bedroom. No depicted fever spike, no vomiting, no seizure. He puts himself to bed. There is no medical workup. **This is the first and arguably most consequential undocumented medical event in his life.**
- **Post-acute (24–96 hrs):** emergence of motor anomalies — sudden wall-adhesion in a school bathroom, involuntary camouflage in a moment of panic, an unintended bioelectric discharge that distresses both subject and Ganke Lee. The presentation is, from a clinical standpoint, indistinguishable from acute panic with conversion features *except that the conversion features are real.* His body is producing them.

The decisive medical-psychological consequence: subject **never seeks evaluation.** Not from his mother (a nurse, who would have caught it instantly), not from a school nurse, not from any physician. Concealment of a medical event from a parent who is herself a healthcare worker becomes the founding template for every subsequent secret. The somatic and the secret are fused at origin.

### 2.3 Post-transformation physiology — the new baseline

A complete chart, were it possible to take one, would show the following stable post-bite phenotype:

- **Musculoskeletal:** strength markedly above human ceiling but sub-Parker in the early years (he is depicted physically over-matched against opponents Parker would handle); by ~age 16–17 (current 616), the gap has narrowed to near-parity. Tendon and bone density implicitly upgraded — he survives falls and impacts (multi-story drops, vehicular collisions) that would fracture an unmodified spine. Joint flexibility above normal range without hypermobility-syndrome pathology (no subluxations, no chronic instability).
- **Integumentary:** palmar and plantar setae-equivalent microstructures providing van-der-Waals adhesion. Subject can voluntarily *release*; the gripping is gated, not constant (he does not stick to bedsheets in his sleep). The adhesion does not appear to wear or callus the skin abnormally.
- **Neurological:** an implied proprioceptive and reflex upgrade ("spider-sense" analog) that is consistently depicted as **less reliable and less acute than Parker's**, requiring him to substitute trained pattern recognition. This is medically interesting: he does *not* trust his own warning system, which converges with his psychological distrust of his own judgment.
- **Bioelectric system:** the most distinct and least understood organ-system change. Subject generates and discharges electrical current through skin contact — the "venom blast." This requires (and implies) an internal generative tissue, plausibly modified muscle or specialized organ, that synthesizes charge. Load and recovery are real: heavy use depletes him (depicted as fatigue, shakiness, depleted strength reserves), suggesting metabolic cost.
- **Chromatophore / electromagnetic-signature suppression:** the "camouflage." Mechanism implied to be both optical (surface pattern matching, like a cephalopod) and partial EM/sensor masking (he has evaded technological detection on multiple occasions). Triggered initially by sympathetic activation; later, with training, voluntary.
- **Healing factor:** present, modest. Closes lacerations in hours rather than days, knits ribs in weeks rather than months, does not regenerate tissue Wolverine-style. Does not appear to confer immune-system upgrades against infectious disease — he gets the flu, on-page, like anyone else.
- **Metabolism:** elevated. Caloric intake repeatedly depicted as adolescent-male-stereotype-high (school cafeteria scenes, late-night refrigerator raids that wake his mother in *USM* and his roommate in college-era stories). This is not vanity; the metabolic cost of his abilities is real, and undereating in the field manifests as performance decline.

The single most diagnostic feature of this new baseline, however, is **autonomic coupling.** His bioelectric and camouflage systems are wired to his sympathetic nervous system. In the first months post-bite, they discharge *involuntarily on fear.* He vanishes when scared. He electrocutes whoever is touching him when startled or angered. **His body broadcasts his anxiety as an environmental hazard.** This is the somatic substrate underwriting every subsequent psychological pattern in the file: the premature emotional discipline, the chronic over-regulation, the abstinence from anything that would loosen inhibition. He cannot afford a panic attack the way a normal adolescent can.

### 2.4 Injury ledger (chronological, partial)

The subject has, by current page-time, accumulated a combat injury history that, in a non-enhanced human, would constitute a small career of orthopedic and neurological insult. The accelerated healing baseline complicates the chart but does not erase it.

- **Year One (*USM* #1–28):** repeated blunt-impact concussions, none documented as causing amnesia or persistent post-concussive syndrome (though there is a plausible argument that the subject's chronic mild irritability and sleep disturbance in this period is post-concussive rather than purely psychological — neither he nor anyone else has ever raised the question). Multiple lacerations from edged weapons and debris. At least one fractured rib in a Prowler-related fight. Burn from his own bioelectric backwash during early uncontrolled discharge. No surgical interventions.
- **Aaron fight, terminal (*USM* #28):** subject sustains contusions, electrical burn from his uncle's malfunctioning gauntlet (the same discharge that killed Aaron), and a soft-tissue injury to the dominant arm. The *signature* injury of this event, however, is not anatomical. He carries a memory of his uncle's grip on his shoulder and his uncle's dying weight — a kinesthetic memory that is rehearsed in subsequent encounters where someone touches the same place. He flinches. This is on-page, repeatedly, for years.
- **Venom / Cataclysm period (*USM* #200, age ~14):** the most severe somatic event of his life that is *not* his own injury. He carries his mother's body. He has her arterial blood on his costume, on his hands, in his hair. He sees her recognition through the mask and her dying instruction. Subsequent appearances depict the classic acute-grief somatic constellation: insomnia (Ganke comments on him being awake at all hours), appetite loss (skipped meals, weight loss implied by costume fit changes), startle response elevated, intrusive flashbacks triggered by the smell of hospital antiseptic and by red-on-blue color combinations (he has been depicted, in quiet panels, unable to look at a particular jacket). **He is never offered, and never seeks, bereavement counseling.** The Morales family grieves privately; the Spider-Man secret precludes integrated grief work.
- **Post-*Secret Wars* period (616 integration):** subject acquires the somatic memory of his mother's death while occupying a reality in which she is alive. This is medically novel and has no clinical analog. He has been depicted, in quiet moments, looking at his living mother with the affect of someone seeing a ghost. He cannot explain it. He has not sought to explain it.
- **Civil War II:** no significant somatic injury, but a prolonged stress state with measurable physiological tells — disrupted sleep, weight loss (Ganke again), gastric symptoms implied (he picks at food, declines meals), and a recurrence of fear-triggered involuntary camouflage during a conversation with Captain Marvel that he is quick to suppress and does not acknowledge.
- **Champions era through present:** standard accumulating combat ledger — broken nose at least once (set without medical attention; his mother notices and he lies about a basketball game), shoulder dislocation reduced in the field, multiple second-degree burns from Roxxon-related conflagrations, chemical exposures of uncertain long-term consequence. None addressed by a physician.
- **Clone arc (Ahmed run):** subject discovers fragments of his own genome / consciousness instantiated in separate bodies. There is no clinical vocabulary for the somatic-identity disturbance this produces. He is depicted touching his own face after meeting Selim; checking his reflection more often; once, in a private panel, pressing a thumb into his own forearm hard enough to leave a mark, as if confirming corporeal singularity. This is the closest the canon comes to depicting dissociation, and it is mild, transient, and self-resolved.

### 2.5 Surgical and procedural history

**None.** This is itself a diagnostic finding. A subject with this combat exposure should have surgical scars. He does not, because (a) his healing factor obviates most surgical indications, and (b) he will not present to a hospital under his real name with an injury inconsistent with his cover story. The one or two occasions on which civilian-grade injury would have warranted ER triage (the broken nose, a deep laceration during the Roxxon arc) were managed at home, by him, with materials from the family medicine cabinet that his nurse mother keeps unusually well-stocked — a fact he relies on without ever discussing.

### 2.6 Substances

The subject is, across the entire canon and into college-age 616 stories, **abstinent** from alcohol, cannabis, nicotine, stimulants, and recreational pharmacology. He has been at parties where substances were available; he has declined. He has been offered a beer by an older hero (off-panel implication, *Champions* era) and refused. He does not drink coffee with any regularity (tea, occasionally; he was raised by a Puerto Rican household where coffee is adult and ceremonial, and he has not crossed that threshold).

This is age-appropriate but, given his stress load and peer environment, **unusually rigid.** The clinical interpretation is direct and convergent with the rest of the file: he cannot disinhibit. His body fires on emotion. A drunk Miles Morales is a public hazard, and he knows it at a level deeper than rule-following. The abstinence is therefore not moral but structural — he is regulating a weapon. Caffeine avoidance fits the same pattern: he will not stack a stimulant on top of an already-hyper-reactive autonomic system.

Prescription medication: none documented. No SSRIs, no anxiolytics, no sleep aids — despite phases where any responsible clinician would have offered all three. He has never been to a psychiatrist. He has never been to a therapist on-page. The closest analog is his conversations with Ganke, with Peter, and with his father after eventual disclosure.

### 2.7 Sleep, nutrition, sexual health

**Sleep** is the most reliably disturbed parameter in his medical picture. Across every era, he is depicted awake at hours that imply chronic partial sleep deprivation — patrols, homework deferred to 2 a.m., insomnia after losses. He functions, but a sleep study would not be flattering. His enhanced physiology likely compensates partially; it does not abolish the deficit.

**Nutrition** is high-calorie, irregular, family-cooked when possible and bodega-acquired when not. No eating disorder pattern. He skips meals under stress (a tell his mother and Ganke both read accurately) and binges to recover. His metabolic load makes both extremes physiologically costly.

**Sexual and reproductive health** is normative for his developmental stage. Relationships (Katie Bishop in the Ultimate continuity, Barbara Sanchez, briefly Kate Bishop, others in 616) are age-appropriate, affectionate, and consistently undermined not by sexual or interpersonal dysfunction but by **the secret.** There is no STI exposure on record, no contraceptive crisis, no pregnancy scare. He is, by adolescent standards, cautious — the same caution that governs his abstinence and his over-regulation. He treats his own body, including its sexuality, as something that must be carefully managed rather than freely inhabited.

### 2.8 The psychological residue of each somatic event — synthesis

Each medical event in this file has left a psychological signature that is, in aggregate, the operational personality:

- **The bite** taught him that his body is not his own and that medical truth must be hidden.
- **The autonomic coupling** taught him that emotional regulation is a public-safety obligation.
- **The Aaron injury** taught him that his uncle's touch — and by extension, his uncle's inheritance — lives in his body.
- **His mother's death-in-his-arms** taught him that proximity to him is dangerous, and that grief must be carried silently because the truth that would let it be shared would also destroy what remains of the family.
- **The 616 restoration** taught him, at a level he cannot articulate, that reality is not stable and that even the living are provisional.
- **The accumulated unrepaired-by-clinicians injury ledger** has taught him that his body heals — which, in the unconscious accounting, also means his body deserves what it takes. The over-functioning hero is also a subject who has never once said to a medical professional: *I am hurt; please help me.*

The medical chart and the psychological chart are, in his case, the same chart. The autonomic coupling between his fear and his powers is not a metaphor for his inner life; it is his inner life, externalized into voltage and invisibility. Everything else — the abstinence, the secret-keeping, the over-regulation, the refusal to seek care — follows from a single fact established at age 13 in his uncle's apartment: **his body became an instrument that fires on his feelings, and he has been compensating for that fact, alone and without medical assistance, ever since.**


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — MORALES, MILES GONZALO

*Subject's body is, more than most, a readable instrument. The bite did not merely augment his musculature; it spliced his autonomic nervous system into a public-facing broadcast channel. What another adolescent would conceal — fear, attraction, embarrassment, rage — Miles emits, sometimes literally, in voltage and photons. The following catalogue reads him as a transmitter as much as a body.*

---

## 1. ANTHROPOMETRY, BASELINE PRESENTATION, AND CARRIAGE

**Build.** Mesomorphic-ectomorph hybrid post-bite; pre-bite he is read as wiry and slight. By age 16 he stands approximately 5'8"–5'9", weight in the 145–155 lb range with body composition disproportionate to silhouette — denser musculature than visible mass implies (he reads in street clothes as a thin teenager and is repeatedly underestimated in physical confrontations, which he exploits). Shoulders narrow relative to lat development; forearm and hand musculature pronounced from adhesion work. Posterior chain — glutes, hamstrings, calves — heavily developed from web-swinging load, but he reads "skinny" because his frame conceals it under hoodies.

**Skin.** Warm medium-brown; readily flushes at the cheekbones, ears, and the bridge of the nose under embarrassment or exertion — a tell he cannot suppress and which his closest observers (Ganke, Rio, Peter) all read fluently. Palms and fingertips exhibit a faint, almost imperceptible texturing under magnification — the setae substrate of his adhesion. Under stress, the palmar surfaces become tacky to objects he is not consciously trying to grip; he has learned to keep his hands open and slightly away from fabric when agitated to avoid pulling sleeves with him.

**Hair.** Tightly coiled, kept short — a low fade or close crop, maintained on a roughly three-week cycle. He runs a barber appointment as a fixed ritual; in periods of acute stress he lets it grow past his standard and Ganke notices before he does. He touches the back of his neck — where the hairline ends — as a self-soothing micro-gesture, particularly mid-sentence when lying or omitting.

**Eyes.** Brown, large, expressive, with a tendency to widen rather than narrow at moments of decision. He does not have a "hard" face; even in combat his default expression reads younger than he is. He has trained, slowly, to keep the eyes neutral during interrogation by adults, but his eyebrows defeat him.

**Resting carriage.** Slight forward head posture from headphone/phone use; shoulders held a touch high and forward in school environments, dropping noticeably when he crosses the threshold of the apartment. Civilian gait is a loose, slightly bouncing step with the weight forward on the balls of the feet — a permanent post-bite recalibration that reads to civilians as adolescent restlessness and to trained observers as a sprinter's set position never quite released. He cannot fully stand still; one foot is always loaded.

---

## 2. GAIT, LOCOMOTION, AND THE ARBOREAL SECOND BODY

**Civilian gait.** Quick cadence, short stride, low vertical oscillation — efficient and quiet. He prefers the inside of sidewalks (building-side, not curb-side), an unconscious carryover from web-swinging logic: walls are friends, traffic is open ground. Crossing streets, he scans up before across — the rooftop check has become reflexive. On stairs he two-steps unconsciously, sometimes three; on descending stairs he overshoots and has to brake, his enhanced reflexes outrunning his calibration.

**Approach to thresholds.** He touches doorframes lightly as he passes through — a kinesthetic check that the adhesion is "off." This is a tic developed after an early embarrassment (pulling a section of drywall away from his own bedroom doorframe). The touch is glancing, often with two knuckles, and reads to others as a casual gesture.

**Costumed locomotion.** Distinct from Parker's. Where Parker swings in long, gravity-loving arcs that telegraph trajectory, Miles swings in shorter, more vertical, more wall-interactive segments — he uses building faces as part of his path, kick-launching and re-attaching, a more parkour-inflected style. His launches initiate from a deeper crouch. He lands in a three-point set roughly 60% of the time and a flat-footed silent landing the other 40%; the three-point is performative (Peter taught it), the silent landing is his native form. He does not stick poses for civilians the way Parker does; he is on and off a roof before he is photographed.

**Wall-perching.** Inverted or sideways postures are *comfortable* to him — he will hold a conversation upside down without registering that this is unusual. In stress, he reflexively gains height: ceiling corner, top of a bookshelf, fire escape rail. This is the camouflage instinct's spatial cousin. When he is upset and indoors, look up.

---

## 3. HANDS

The hands are the most-watched part of him for any trained observer.

**At rest.** Fingers slightly curled, never fully relaxed. He fidgets with small objects — a guitar pick (post a brief musical phase), a webshooter cartridge in his pocket that he turns with the thumb, the drawstring of a hoodie, his phone case. Phone is held two-handed, thumbs working, but during conversation he reverses it screen-down on the table — privacy reflex.

**Writing.** Right-handed for pen work; ambidextrous-tending for combat (Peter noted this; Miles had not). His handwriting is small, careful, slightly back-slanted — controlled to the point of being effortful, which fits the broader pattern of *visible self-regulation*.

**Adhesion management.** Constant micro-attention. He shakes hands deliberately, with a measured pressure, and releases on a count — he over-pressures slightly out of fear of dropping the grip mid-shake, which civilians read as confident. He does not high-five. He bumps fists or claps shoulders. He cannot wear gloves comfortably; the wall-stick interferes and he picks at them. He bites the cuticle of his right thumb when thinking — the only nail-biting tell, isolated to that finger.

**Venom-blast tells.** When his bio-electric charge is building involuntarily, the fine hairs on his forearms lift; there is a faint blue-violet corona visible at the fingertips in low light, sometimes preceded by a static-crawl sensation he describes (to Ganke) as "ants." He clenches his fists to ground the charge, then opens them deliberately when it passes. Under control, he can summon the blast with a snap of the fingers or a palm-strike; under loss of control, it discharges through whatever he is touching, which has included doorknobs, his own phone (three replacements documented in *USM* run), Ganke's arm (once, lightly, apologized profusely), and the kitchen sink faucet (Rio assumed it was wiring).

---

## 4. FACE — MICRO-EXPRESSION ATLAS

**Default.** Open, slightly questioning. Brows held neutral but mobile; mouth in a soft, almost-smile that drops instantly when he registers something serious. He looks younger than he is and is aware of it; among adult heroes he sometimes sets his jaw fractionally to compensate, which is itself a tell.

**The pre-lie tell.** A half-second downward glance, slight tongue-press against the inside of the lower lip, then full eye contact held a beat too long. His father reads this every time and has since Miles was nine. He has not improved at it.

**Embarrassment.** Cheek and ear flush, hand to back of neck, audible swallow, gaze drops to mid-distance. Around romantic interests, add a single nervous laugh — short, breathy, with a head-shake — and a tendency to talk over the moment.

**Concentration.** Brow knits asymmetrically — left brow descends more than right. Lips part slightly. He breathes through the mouth when working on something hard (homework, mid-combat puzzle); through the nose when settled.

**The grief face.** Documented post-Aaron, post-Rio, and post-Peter (the elder). Not crying — the cry comes later, alone, usually in the shower. The grief face is a *vacated* face: eyes lose focus, the small constant motion of his features stops, the mouth goes neutral-soft. He does not blink as often. Observers report a sense that he has gone elsewhere. This is the closest he comes to dissociation.

**Combat face.** Surprisingly mild. He does not snarl, does not glare. The brows go flat, the mouth tightens, and the eyes track. He talks — quips, exhortations, apologies to people he is hitting — in a steady mid-register without breath catches. The mask conceals all of this, which has costs (he cannot signal to civilians that he is friendly) and benefits (he can panic invisibly).

**The smile.** Wide, asymmetric — right corner higher — with a slight nose crinkle. Genuine smiles involve his eyes (crow's foot at the outer corners even at sixteen). Polite smiles do not; the mouth moves, the eyes do not.

---

## 5. VOICE

Mid-tenor, still finishing its settle. Native register sits higher than he prefers; in formal or stressful conversations with adults he drops it a quarter-octave, audibly. Brooklyn cadence — relaxed vowels, dropped consonant endings in casual speech, sharpened to standard register at school and around heroes he respects. Spanish phrases enter under emotion, particularly around his mother (and her memory); the code-switch is involuntary and reliable. He has a slight, occasional adolescent voice crack under sudden exertion or surprise that he winces at audibly.

**Speech tempo.** Fast when nervous, with run-on sentences and self-interrupting clauses ("which, no, that's not — what I meant was —"). Slow when grieving. Measured and almost flat when delivering hard news. Under the mask, the voice quips faster and louder than out of it — performative, Parker-modeled, and a known tell that he is *more* anxious than less when the chatter peaks.

**Vocal tics.** "Look —" as a sentence-opener under pressure. "I'm sorry" used as a transitional phrase rather than an apology. "No no no no" as a four-beat litany when something is going wrong. A sharp exhale through the nose when frustrated (not a sigh; shorter). Audible swallow before disclosing anything true.

---

## 6. CAMOUFLAGE — THE INVOLUNTARY VANISH

**Trigger.** Acute social or physical fear. Onset is fast (sub-second) and total when uncontrolled. Initial canonical presentation: he discovered the power by becoming invisible during a panic episode in a school bathroom.

**Phenomenology.** Visual signature collapses to background match within roughly 200–400 ms; clothing follows (with effort; was inconsistent early). Subject reports a cool, prickling sensation across the skin, peripheral vision dimming, a sense of "becoming a hole." Under voluntary control the effect is partial and tunable; under involuntary trigger it is total and he must consciously *return*, which takes effort proportional to how frightened he was.

**Behavioral signature in social settings.** When overwhelmed at parties, family gatherings, or press events, he will physically move to a wall and *lean* — the lean precedes any actual vanish and is a reliable early indicator. If the vanish initiates, he will sometimes complete it deliberately and slip out rather than fight to remain visible. Multiple documented Champions meetings have ended with Miles "leaving early" via this method, which the team has learned to read as *Miles needs ten minutes alone*.

**Costs.** The camouflage is the somatic externalization of his core defense — *I should not be here* made literal. He has worked, slowly, on staying visible under stress as a discipline; it is one of the few areas where he has explicitly sought to override his physiology rather than train with it.

---

## 7. SLEEP

**Architecture.** Pre-mantle: normative adolescent — late sleep onset, hard to wake, weekend extension. Post-mantle: fragmented. Sleep onset latency has lengthened to 40–60 minutes on a baseline night, longer after patrols. He wakes 2–3 times nightly, with hypervigilant micro-wakes triggered by sirens, his phone, building creak. Sleep is positional — he sleeps on his back, hands at sides or one on his chest, almost never on his stomach (vulnerability to back-attack, an instinct he did not consciously cultivate). He has been observed sleeping on the *ceiling* by Ganke on at least one occasion of extreme exhaustion — adhesion holds through REM. This embarrasses him; he does not do it intentionally.

**Dream content.** Repeating themes: falling without webs, his mother in the kitchen, Aaron's last fight, being unmasked publicly. Post-Rio's death, sleep paralysis episodes documented; he did not name them as such and Ganke had to look up the term.

**Wake pattern.** He wakes early — 6:00–6:30 reliably even on weekends — because the apartment is loudest then (Rio in the kitchen) and the sound functions as a reassurance ritual. On nights he has been out as Spider-Man, he reverses the bed orientation so his head is at the foot, an old anxiety-management technique he learned as a child from a YouTube video and never stopped.

**Naps.** Frequent, short (15–25 min), positional — head down on a desk at school, on the train, on Ganke's beanbag. He can fall asleep instantly when safe and not at all when not. The discriminator is *whether someone he trusts is in the room*.

---

## 8. EATING

**Caloric demand.** Markedly elevated post-bite; his metabolism runs 1.6–2.0x baseline adolescent male. He eats constantly, in small frequent bouts, and has a near-obsessive relationship with snacks (granola bars in every pocket, a stash in his desk, a stash in Ganke's bunk). When food is unavailable he becomes irritable in a way he himself does not recognize as hunger.

**Preferences.** His mother's cooking is a sacrament — *pernil*, *arroz con gandules*, *tostones* — and the kitchen is the room of the apartment where his shoulders fully drop. He eats with his hands when culturally appropriate and with fork-in-right-hand otherwise; he holds the fork in a slight fist-grip rather than a pencil-grip, a thing his mother corrected and which returns under stress. He chews quickly. He drinks water in large gulps, milk with cereal in disproportionate volume, coffee not yet established as a regular habit (a marker of how young he still is).

**Stress eating / under-eating.** Under acute grief he loses appetite (post-Rio, documented). Under chronic stress he overeats junk — convenience-store grazing on patrol breaks, vending-machine intake at school. Ganke has called it out more than once.

**Table manners.** Excellent at the family table; abandoned at the desk. The discriminator is *who is watching*; the discipline is for his mother, not for himself.

---

## 9. GROOMING AND DRESS

**Hygiene.** Compulsively showered — sometimes twice daily — particularly after patrols. The shower is the only reliable room for crying. Showers run long (15–25 min); water bills have prompted Jefferson commentary.

**Dress.** Layered: t-shirt over long-sleeve, hoodie over both, jacket if cold. The layering is partly practical (costume underneath) and partly self-concealment (he does not enjoy being looked at). Color palette: neutrals and dark blues, the occasional red. Shoe rotation tight — one pair of high-tops in heavy circulation, replaced every 3–4 months due to wall-launch wear on the soles. He laces tightly and double-knots.

**Costume management.** Mask in the back left pocket of his jeans, folded twice. Webshooters in the inside hoodie pocket on school days, on the wrists under sleeves on weekends. He checks for all three with a hand-pat sequence (left hip, right wrist, left wrist) before leaving the apartment; he is not aware that he does this.

**Backpack.** Worn on both straps, not one — a Ganke influence and a back-protection instinct. Contents organized; he is the kid who has the charger.

---

## 10. PROXEMICS AND POSTURAL READS

**Personal space.** Larger bubble than his apparent demeanor suggests — he does not initiate touch easily with non-family. With his mother he is a leaner: shoulder, head, hand on her arm. With his father, he keeps a half-step further than the room suggests, a residue of the unresolved disclosure. With Ganke, the bubble collapses entirely — they sit on the same bed, share food, no spatial defensiveness.

**With authority figures.** Stands at a slight remove and slightly off-axis (3/4 facing rather than square), a non-confrontational orientation. Hands clasped or in pockets. Listens with the head fractionally tilted.

**With elder Peter.** Closer than with anyone else outside family. He will stand near Peter, sit near Peter, lean toward Peter. The body confesses the idealization the mouth euphemizes.

**Romantic intimacy.** Initial proxemic awkwardness — he does not lean in cleanly; there is a half-start, a stop, a re-approach. Once contact is established his hands are warm, deliberate, slightly trembling at first contact and then steady. He breaks contact first, almost always, and slightly too soon — a secret-keeper's reflex.

**Threat orientation.** Hands open, weight back-loaded slightly on the rear foot, chin tucked a fraction, breathing deepened through the nose. He talks before he strikes — almost always. The first strike, when it comes, is a non-lethal disabling move: leg sweep, joint lock, venom-blast at minimum amperage. He apologizes mid-fight to opponents whose lives he is sparing.

---

## 11. RITUALS AND ROUTES

**Daily route.** Bedroom → bathroom → kitchen → door, with the doorframe-touch on exit. He greets his mother before his father in the morning. He fist-bumps his father on the way out — invariably, since middle school.

**Patrol routes.** Three preferred Brooklyn loops, varying by night of week, plus a Manhattan extension when he is restless. He has rooftop perches with personal meaning: the building two blocks from his mother's hospital (which he visits to look at, not to enter); the spot where Peter died (visited yearly, on the date, never told to anyone); a corner of the Brooklyn Bridge upper cable he has never told another spider-person about.

**Stim/soothing rituals.** Headphones in. He listens to music in long sittings — predominantly hip-hop, with a sentimental Spanish-language ballad rotation that is his mother's influence. Volume high. He raps along quietly under his breath, lips moving without sound, on the train.

**Phone behavior.** Constantly on. Screen-down on tables. Notifications muted except for parents and Ganke. He checks it in 90-second intervals when anxious — almost compulsive — and not at all during patrol.

---

## 12. SEXUAL / INTIMATE BASELINE

Age-appropriate, normatively developing, conducted with the same secret-keeping pathology that structures every other intimate relationship. He is shy on initiation, sincere on commitment, and physically gentle. Touch is light and inquiring rather than declarative; he reads as someone for whom *consent* is a felt and obvious frame, not a learned protocol. His relationships fail not at the physical interface but at the disclosure one — the body shows up; the truth does not.

Under desire, he flushes (cheeks, ears, sternum), his pulse becomes briefly visible at the throat, and the bio-electric undertone climbs — there have been small, embarrassing static-discharge incidents on initial kisses, treated by partners as charming and by him as alarming. He is more cautious with his hands than his mouth, for adhesion reasons he cannot explain.

---

## 13. STATE TRANSITIONS — A CONDENSED READ

- **Calm.** Shoulders down, hands loose-curled, weight even, easy smile, fast chatter with Ganke, mid-register voice, no flush, no spark.
- **Mild stress.** Hand to back of neck, voice up a quarter-octave, "look —" sentence openers, increased self-deprecation, pacing if standing, foot-bounce if seated.
- **Moderate stress.** Doorframe-checks intensify, phone-check interval shortens, jaw set, eyes more mobile, breathing shallow-and-high, palmar tackiness noticeable, the back-of-neck touch becomes a rub.
- **Acute fear, social.** Move to wall, lean, partial camouflage, voice drops to near-whisper, swallows audibly, leaves room.
- **Acute fear, physical.** Crouch deepens, hands flatten, the corona at the fingertips, hair on forearms rises, voice goes quiet and very young, then *snaps* to combat-flat. First reaction is to *move up* — gain height.
- **Combat.** Mild face under mask, steady mid-register chatter, talks to opponents and to himself, apologizes, finishes fast, leaves faster, does not look back at the body of work.
- **Grief.** Vacated face, slow gait, appetite collapse, sleep fragmentation, long showers, music louder, route includes the perch near the hospital, Spanish under the breath.
- **Intimacy.** Half-step closer than baseline, hands warm and shaky-then-steady, flushes at throat, breaks contact slightly early, smiles asymmetrically with the eyes engaged, does not say the true thing that would let it last.
- **Post-crisis recovery.** *More* regulated than baseline. Quiet, generous, slow. The floor has been tested. He becomes, briefly, the adult he is becoming.

---

*Summary read.* The body of this subject is a *transparent instrument* — secured by attachment, modified by venom, disciplined by necessity, and continuously broadcasting the interior life it was built to conceal. He has trained himself, impressively for his age, to override the broadcast in the directions that matter most (he does not vanish in front of his mother; he does not spark when his father touches his shoulder). The training is real but incomplete, and the surveillance value of his somatic record is therefore high: every important emotional event in his life leaves a physical trace, often a visible one, frequently an electrical one, sometimes a luminous one. He is, in the most literal sense, a body that tells the truth.


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# UATU DOSSIER — SUBJECT: MORALES, MILES GONZALO
## Section 6: Attachment & Relational Patterns

---

### 6.1 Attachment Classification and Its Origins

The subject presents as **securely attached with anxious-protective overlay** — a configuration uncommon in the costumed population and analytically important because it inverts the standard Spider-pathology. Where Parker (616) was orphaned twice before adolescence and Wayne-style figures are built on early catastrophic loss, Morales arrived at the bite with his attachment system already organized around two responsive caregivers and a functional extended kin network. The base is sound. What sits on top of it is the overlay: a learned, post-traumatic, *anticipatory* protectiveness that treats every loved object as already-half-lost. He bonds normally; he then immediately begins grieving the bond in advance.

The origin of the secure baseline is unambiguous in canon. Rio Morales is depicted across *Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man* and the Bendis 616 run as warmly attuned, physically affectionate, verbally articulate about love, and reliably present — she kisses his forehead, asks the second-order question ("you're quiet, what is it"), and is the parent he goes to with the small things. Jefferson Davis is the moral parent: warm but principled, with a stated ethical position (anti-vigilante, pro-rule-of-law) that he expresses *as expectation* rather than as threat. Jefferson does not withhold affection; he withholds *approval of specific behaviors*, which is the developmentally optimal calibration. Subject internalized: love is unconditional, esteem is earned. This is exactly the configuration that produces high-functioning, high-guilt adults.

The origin of the overlay is also unambiguous. Between ages 13 and 14 the subject lost, in order: (1) the predecessor whose mantle he assumed (Parker, *Ultimate Fallout* #4), (2) the uncle who was his first super-confidant and first betrayer (Aaron, *USM* #28), and (3) his mother (Rio, *USM* #200). Three deaths inside roughly eighteen in-story months, each of which his causal model assigns at least partial blame to himself. Attachment systems exposed to that load during late-adolescent identity formation do not become *insecure* if the base was secure — they become *vigilantly secure*, which is the subject's current presentation. He loves the same people the same way, and watches the door.

### 6.2 The Bonding Sequence

Subject's process for forming a new bond is observable across enough relationships (Ganke, Peter, Kamala, Sam Alexander, Barbara Sanchez, Katie Bishop, Starling, the various Champions, and his cousin/clones) to constitute a repeatable template:

1. **Initial wariness with curiosity.** First-contact behavior is polite, slightly self-effacing, with a quick joke deployed to lower the temperature. He reads faces. He does not lead with disclosure.
2. **Provisional trust via shared activity.** He does not bond through self-disclosure first; he bonds through *doing a thing with someone*. Ganke through games and Lego; Peter through patrol; Kamala through team logistics; Barbara through walking-and-talking. Conversation is a byproduct of co-presence, not its purpose.
3. **Asymmetric disclosure.** He reveals little, asks much. Counterparts almost always know more about him externally than he has volunteered. He learns about the other person at a rate considerably higher than they learn about him — a soft form of intelligence-gathering that he would not describe in those terms.
4. **Threshold event.** At some point an event (a fight, a rescue, a small loyalty) flips the relationship into the *kept* category. From this point his loyalty is essentially unconditional. The threshold, once crossed, is not re-evaluated.
5. **Post-threshold structural deference.** He begins arranging his behavior around what the other person needs and minimizing his own asks. The bond becomes asymmetric in his disfavor, by his design.

The asymmetry is the diagnostic point. Subject does not form *peer-symmetrical* bonds easily; he tilts every relationship toward a position of giving more than he receives, which functions simultaneously as (a) genuine generosity, (b) reparation discharge for ambient guilt, and (c) a control mechanism — the over-giver retains the leverage of having less to lose if the relationship ends, because the relationship was never structured around his need in the first place.

### 6.3 The Ganke Template

The relationship with Ganke Lee is the cleanest specimen in his file and functions as the relational *template* against which every other bond can be measured. Ganke is the only person to whom subject discloses identity *voluntarily and early*, without coercion or accident. The pattern that follows is instructive:

- Identity disclosure within days of the bite, while subject is still trying to *refuse* the powers. He does not tell Ganke to recruit help; he tells Ganke because he needs someone to confirm that what is happening to him is real. **Function: reality-testing.**
- Ganke immediately occupies a *managerial* role — researches the bite, builds the costume question, fields the operational logistics. Subject accepts this without resistance. **He is comfortable being managed by a peer who has no agenda.**
- Ganke is allowed to tease, criticize, and override in ways subject permits from no one else. Notable: Ganke is the only character in the canon who routinely tells Miles he is *wrong* about something small and is heard. Peter is too venerated for that role; Rio and Jefferson too parental; Kamala too co-equal-leader. **Ganke is the calibration instrument.**
- Subject's loyalty to Ganke is asymmetric in the standard direction (Miles gives more) but the asymmetry is *smaller* here than in any other relationship. Ganke is the closest thing in his life to a true peer.

Every subsequent friendship is some variation on this template, almost always with one element missing.

### 6.4 The Peter Parker Template (the Inheritance Bond)

Subject's relationship with the 616 Peter Parker is the most psychologically loaded bond in his file and the one least likely to fully resolve. It is structurally a *secure-base relationship with the ghost of the dead one underneath*. Observable features:

- **Permanent permission-seeking.** Across *Spider-Men*, *Spider-Men II*, *Spider-Verse*, and incidental crossovers, subject consistently checks decisions with Peter, defers tactical authority to Peter even when his own read is correct, and accepts Peter's reassurances without internalizing them. Peter has explicitly told him, on at least four documented occasions, that the name is *his* — and the deferential behavior does not change. This is diagnostic. Reassurance does not patch the wound because the wound is structural, not informational.
- **The brother position, not the son position.** Subject does not relate to Peter as a father-figure. Both his parents are alive (in 616), and the slot is occupied. Peter occupies the *older-brother* slot, which carries different obligations — comparison, measurement, the unspoken hope of being thought well of. This is more painful than father-relations because brothers are *comparable* in ways fathers and sons are not.
- **Idealization that survives evidence.** Peter is shown to subject in his ordinary, flawed adult presentation (rent problems, bad relationships, professional setbacks) and subject's idealization is unaffected. He sees the flaws and constructs a frame in which they make Peter *more* admirable, not less. The idealization is need-driven, not perception-driven.
- **The unspoken question.** Subject has never directly asked the question that organizes the relationship: *would the dead Peter have approved of me*. He cannot ask the living Peter because the living Peter is not the relevant authority. The question is unanswerable, which is why it persists.

### 6.5 Family Bonds — The Three Distinct Patterns

Subject's bonds with the three primary kin figures (Rio, Jefferson, Aaron) are structurally different from each other and require separate treatment.

**Rio (mother).** The least conflicted bond in his life. Pre-death: easy affection, casual physical contact, the parent he sought out for ordinary comfort. Speaks to her in code-switched English-Spanish, more so when stressed. Her death is the structuring trauma of his adolescent psychology; her dying instruction ("don't tell your father") was received as a *moral* command and obeyed past the point of utility. Post-restoration (616), the bond appears intact on the surface but carries observable residue: subject is more physically demonstrative with her than he was pre-loss, lingers in goodbyes, checks her location, calls more often than is normatively required. He is loving a person while also remembering having lost her. **This is the only bond in his life where he is the more anxious party in a stable dyad.**

**Jefferson (father).** The bond carrying the highest unresolved load. The pre-disclosure period is marked by *active concealment* — subject not only hides his identity but performs the version of himself his father expects, which requires sustained, exhausting emotional labor. Body language with Jefferson is observably more controlled than with anyone else: shoulders slightly higher, fewer gestures, eye contact more managed. He laughs less around his father. Post-disclosure (varies by continuity) the bond enters a recovery phase that is genuinely improving but not complete; Jefferson's path from *Spider-Man killed my brother* to *my son is Spider-Man* required Jefferson to also revise his self-concept, and the negotiation is ongoing. Subject's deepest unspoken fear regarding his father is not rejection — it is that the eventual full disclosure (Aaron's death) will produce a forgiveness that he, subject, cannot accept as deserved.

**Aaron (uncle).** The original wound, and the relationship that established subject's template for *betrayal*. Aaron was the first adult outside the nuclear family who treated subject as interesting in his own right, who offered access to a wider world, who spoke to him conspiratorially. The grooming pattern is textbook — gifts, special status, secret-keeping framed as bonding. Subject's bond with Aaron pre-discovery was genuine and important to his identity formation, which is what makes the betrayal load-bearing. The discovery sequence (*USM* #22–28) is not a single betrayal but a cascade: Aaron knows, Aaron lies, Aaron threatens, Aaron coerces, Aaron attacks, Aaron dies saying "you're just like me." Each beat is a separate injury. The final injury — the line — is the one that persists because it cannot be rebutted by living counter-evidence; the speaker is dead. Subject has spent the entire canon since *USM* #28 quietly arguing with a dead man.

### 6.6 Distrust — Triggers, Calibration, Recovery

Subject's distrust system is *slow to activate and fast to forgive*, which is the inverse of the operationally optimal setting for a vigilante and a recurring source of tactical risk.

**Activation triggers.** Lying about something material; using him to get at his family; framing him for harm; speaking ill of Peter (the trigger that activates fastest, often before he realizes it). What does *not* activate his distrust readily: violence directed at him personally, ideological disagreement, even prior criminality. He extends rehabilitation credit on the assumption that people can change — an assumption with documented origin in his father's reformed-criminal history.

**Calibration.** Once activated, distrust is *not* total. Subject sorts the offender into a category (compromised, coerced, mistaken, malicious) and titrates response. He is unusually willing to keep relating to people who have hurt him, on revised terms. This is not weakness; it is principled and consistent. The flaw is that it makes him exploitable by repeat offenders who learn the recalibration window.

**Recovery.** Subject seeks repair actively. He will initiate the conversation, name the harm, propose terms, accept a real apology — and then move on with observable speed. He does not nurse grievances. The functional cost is that he often forgives faster than he should and is re-injured by the same actor; the functional benefit is that his stable relationships are deep and resilient because nothing has been allowed to accrete.

### 6.7 Betrayal — Subject's Own Capacity

Subject is structurally incapable of *active* betrayal and routinely engages in *passive* betrayal via secret-keeping. The distinction is critical.

He will not lie *to do harm*. He will lie *to prevent disclosure*. The lie-to-prevent-disclosure pattern is so deeply grooved that it operates below decisional awareness — he produces the cover story before he has considered whether to. Targets: his father (primarily), his romantic partners (consistently), school authorities (constantly), his mother (until her death). The cover stories are competent but not artful; he is a B-grade liar at best, and the people closest to him generally know he is lying and choose, for their own reasons, to let it pass.

The accumulated weight of these small betrayals is the largest unaddressed item in his relational ledger. He does not conceive of them as betrayals; he conceives of them as *protections*. The people he is protecting frequently experience them as betrayals. This gap has cost him every romantic relationship in his file to date.

### 6.8 Repair — His Native Skill

Repair is the relational skill subject is *unusually good at* for his age, almost certainly as a direct consequence of his parents' modeling. Observable repair behaviors:

- **Returns to the scene.** He will physically come back to the person, not wait for them to come to him.
- **Names the harm specifically.** Not "I'm sorry for whatever I did" but "I'm sorry I lied about where I was on Tuesday."
- **Does not over-apologize into manipulation.** He apologizes and stops; he does not pile self-flagellation on top until the other person is forced to comfort him. This is rare and significant.
- **Accepts the other person's pace.** If the counterpart is not ready to repair, he does not push.
- **Updates behavior.** Repair is followed by observable change, not just verbal commitment. The lie about Tuesday is not repeated next Tuesday.

The skill is genuine but bounded by the disclosure problem — he cannot repair fully when the underlying issue (the secret identity) cannot be raised. Romantic partnerships hit this ceiling and break against it.

### 6.9 Intimacy and Dependency Patterns

**Intimacy** in the emotional sense — being known — is the dimension on which subject is most restricted. He is *physically* unembarrassed (warm hugs, comfortable proximity, the easy tactile vocabulary of a kid from a demonstrative family) and *socially* fluent. He is *self-disclosurally* guarded. The number of people who know the contents of his interior life can be counted on one hand and includes: Ganke, his mother (selectively, while alive), Peter (operationally only), and arguably no one else fully. His romantic partners have known him intimately in every register *except* the one that organizes his life.

**Dependency** is the dimension on which subject is most actively *suppressive*. He will not ask for help until the situation is past the point where help is most useful. The pattern is observable across the Aaron arc (does not tell Peter or Jessica Drew until forced), the Rio aftermath (withdraws rather than seeks), the Civil War II vision (goes to Cap alone), the clone arc (tries to handle the clones single-handedly before accepting team support). The cognition driving this is recoverable from his internal monologue in the Ahmed run: *I made this; I clean this up.* Asking for help registers to him as off-loading his guilt onto someone else, which he experiences as an additional moral injury. He would rather carry more than he can hold than ask someone to share it.

The functional consequence is that his support network is *available* but *under-utilized*. The Champions, Peter, his parents, and Ganke are all willing to help; he routinely does not call until he is bleeding.

### 6.10 Romantic Pattern

Subject's romantic relationships across the canon (Katie Bishop, Barbara Sanchez, brief overtures with Kate Bishop, others) form a clear pattern:

1. **Selection bias toward bright, articulate, slightly older-presenting partners** who can hold their own conversationally and do not require him to lead emotionally.
2. **Affection registered cleanly.** He is verbally and physically warm, attentive to small things, comfortable expressing care.
3. **Disclosure failure as structural ceiling.** He cannot tell them what he is, which means he cannot tell them where he goes, why he is late, why he is hurt, why he is afraid. The relationship can grow to the ceiling of what is possible without that information and not past it.
4. **Resentment vector.** Partners generally figure out, accurately, that he is hiding something significant. Their interpretation tends to be relational (cheating, another partner, loss of interest) rather than accurate (he is a vigilante), which compounds his guilt: not only is he lying, the lie is producing *wrong* hypotheses that injure her in additional ways.
5. **Termination via attrition, not rupture.** His relationships do not end in fights; they end in the partner quietly deciding it is not sustainable. He generally does not contest these endings, which itself confirms her hypothesis.
6. **Mourning without resolution.** He grieves them privately, blames himself, and does not seek a debrief.

He has not yet had a romantic relationship in which the disclosure problem was solved on-page in a stable, ongoing way. Until that occurs, the pattern will repeat.

### 6.11 Peer and Team Bonds — Kamala, Sam, the Champions

Within the Champions, subject occupies the *moral-conscience-second-in-command* slot with notable consistency. He defers to Kamala's leadership without challenge, supports Sam's enthusiasms while moderating their excesses, and is the team's go-to mediator for inter-member friction. His bond with Kamala specifically is the closest thing in his file to a true peer-symmetrical alliance with someone who is not Ganke; she is one of the only people whose moral authority he treats as fully equal to his own, and the only one whose leadership he accepts without the deference-with-resentment subtext he brings to elder-hero authority.

His bond with Sam Alexander is the closest thing he has to a *little-brother* relationship — Sam is reckless where Miles is restrained, and Miles plays the steadying role that Peter plays for him, which is one of the few relational positions in his life where he occupies the senior end. Notably, he is *better at being the senior* than he believes he is — and notably, he extends to Sam exactly the patience and credit-of-goodness that he does not extend to himself. This is the cleanest evidence in his file that his self-concept is harsher than his actual character.

### 6.12 The Repeated Template — Synthesis

Across every relationship in the file, with variation in tone and content, the underlying structure is the same:

**He loves easily, gives more than he asks, hides the part of himself that organizes his life, expects loss, forgives quickly, repairs actively, and tracks a private ledger in which he owes more than he is owed.** Counterparts experience him as generous, warm, slightly mysterious, and ultimately unreachable past a certain depth. Counterparts who know the secret experience him as generous, warm, partially reachable, and constitutionally unable to ask for what he needs.

The template is recognizably the *child of a reformed-criminal father and a caregiver mother in a tight observant household*, modified by *serial loss during identity formation*, modified by *a nervous system that broadcasts his anxiety as electricity and invisibility*. The resulting adult-in-formation is one of the most relationally healthy figures in the costumed population on most metrics and one of the most *self-isolating* on the metric that matters most for his own well-being — the willingness to be a recipient rather than a giver of care.

The unresolved relational task of his canon, and the one most likely to organize the next decade of his development, is not the disclosure problem (which is solvable and being solved) but the *receipt* problem: learning to let the people who love him *help* him, on the grounds that he is worth the help. He does not yet believe he is. The people around him uniformly do.


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# UATU DOSSIER — SUBJECT: MORALES, MILES GONZALO
## SECTION 6: DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

---

### 6.0 Orientation

The subject's defensive architecture is, by the standards of costumed operators, **unusually mature and unusually permeable**. He does not present the brittle, archaic defenses (splitting, projective identification, dissociative discontinuity) that dominate the files of trauma-formed vigilantes; nor does he present the rigid character armor (intellectualization weaponized into mania, sublimation industrialized into workaholism) typical of his predecessor.
