**With Jefferson Davis.** A precisely calibrated and slightly performative son. Greets with a hug — initiated by Miles, almost always. Calls him "Dad," rarely "Pop" (which is reserved for moments of affection or apology). Listens to him with the squared-shoulder attention he otherwise reserves for hiding things, which is a problem the subject does not appear to have noticed: he gives his father the *posture of evasion* even when telling the truth, because the body has learned that posture in his father's presence. Touches his father on the upper arm in passing — small affirmations. Laughs at his father's jokes generously, including the not-funny ones.

Under his father's direct gaze on a subject adjacent to the secret (vigilantism, Aaron, Spider-Man in the news), the subject performs a specific micro-sequence: a slow blink, a nod, a one-word affirmation ("yeah," "right"), and a redirect to a non-loaded topic. The redirect is almost always to his mother ("did Mom say if she's working tonight"), which is diagnostic — he uses Rio as a verbal escape route from Jefferson.

**With Rio Morales.** The unmediated relationship in his life. Affect drops its compression around her. He lets her touch his face. He answers her questions honestly more often than anyone else's, and when he lies to her he is *worse* at it than with anyone else — the only person to whom his lying is visibly poor. Speaks Spanish with her in short bursts (terms of endearment, kitchen logistics, complaints); his Spanish is conversational but not native-fluent, and he is shy about it with anyone else. Post-restoration in 616, intermittent moments of staring at her when she is not looking — the *somatic memory* of her death surfacing as visual confirmation that she is present. He does not name this and may not be conscious of it.

**With Ganke Lee.** The least edited relationship he has. Communication is high-bandwidth and low-formality: half-sentences, callbacks, in-jokes a decade old by adolescent time. Ganke is the only person to whom he reveals stress passively — he does not have to perform calm. He lets Ganke see him eat badly, sleep badly, sulk. Physical closeness is high; they share rooms, beds, food, screens without negotiation. He brings Ganke problems and lets Ganke solve them, which is one of the only places he reliably *receives* help rather than producing it.

**With Peter Parker (616).** Posture deferential, eye contact slightly downcast, voice a half-step higher. Asks questions whose answers he knows. Receives praise badly — visibly uncomfortable, deflects with self-deprecation. Receives criticism well — over-internalizes. The asymmetry is sustained and is one of the things Peter has repeatedly attempted to correct on-page without success.

**With romantic partners.** Initial phase: warm, attentive, generous with time and small gestures (handwritten notes, food, walking-her-home rituals). Mid phase: secrecy pressure produces lateness, cancellations, an increasing reservoir of unexplained absences. He compensates with intensity in the time available, which reads as romantic but is partly guilt-discharge. Late phase: either disclosure (rare, partial, painful) or attrition. He has not yet solved this and the canon does not pretend he has.

Physical intimacy: tentative, considerate, slow to initiate. Powers add a layer of vigilance — he is aware that his body is wired to discharge under arousal-adjacent autonomic activation, and he manages this through micro-disengagement (a hand removed, a step back) that partners often misread as emotional withdrawal.

**With mentors who are not Peter (Drew, Cap, T'Challa, Storm).** Formal posture, formal address. Calls Rogers "sir." Calls T'Challa "your majesty" the first time and is corrected. Listens more than he speaks. Volunteers little personal information. Notably, he is *more* honest with these figures about his doubts than with peers — they get the existential confession ("I don't know if I should be doing this") that Ganke does not get because Ganke has heard it already.

---

## 6. GRIEF

The subject's grief signature is the most consistent across the canon and the most carefully managed in performance.

**Acute phase (first hours to first days).** Containment. He does not collapse publicly. The body holds itself upright, the voice answers when addressed, the tasks at hand are completed. The grief is visible in *negative space* — a beat too long before responses, an unfinished sentence, an absent micro-expression where one would normally be. Tears come privately, in specific locations: bedroom, a particular rooftop, the bathroom with the water running.

**Somatic.** Sleep severely disrupted (the canonical Rio aftermath). Appetite collapses. He loses noticeable mass over a grief arc. Showers become long. He sits in clothing for extended periods without changing. Personal hygiene degrades from his ordinarily fastidious baseline (he is, in calm state, a tidy adolescent — clean sneakers, laundered hoodies) into a visible slippage that Ganke and Rio (when alive) read instantly.

**Verbal.** He stops generating speech. Answers when addressed, briefly. Stops joking entirely — and the cessation of self-deprecating humor is the single most reliable grief indicator, because the humor is a near-constant baseline.

**Behavioral.** Patrol intensifies — longer, more dangerous, more careless. He takes risks during grief that he does not take during any other state. This is not death-seeking but penance-seeking; the body wants to pay. He helps strangers with disproportionate effort. He may sit with civilians after rescues longer than he otherwise would, which has produced some of the canon's most affecting incidental moments.

**Avoidance.** Specific sites become uninhabitable for periods (the apartment after Rio's death; the Aaron rooftop after Aaron's death). He routes around them on patrol — observable as anomalous gaps in his geographic coverage during the relevant weeks.

**Recovery markers.** Return of humor (first to Ganke, then in his own interior monologue, finally to opponents). Return of regular meals. Resumption of normal patrol routes including, eventually, the avoided sites — and he will often pause at them on first re-entry, sit briefly, then move on. The pause is the marker that integration is occurring.

**Anniversary effects.** Inferred. The subject is the kind of person who remembers dates, and his patrol patterns and mood on the anniversaries of Peter's death, Aaron's death, and (in the Ultimate continuity he carries forward) his mother's death are predictably altered — quieter, longer, more solitary, no Ganke time.

---

## 7. VICTORY

The subject is notably bad at victory. It is the state in which he is least like himself.

**Tells.** Immediate deflection of credit: "the team," "everyone," "I just got lucky." Visible discomfort with applause or thanks — backs up half a step, raises a hand palm-out, looks for an exit. If a civilian he saved tries to hug him, accepts but does not return with full pressure. If a press camera is present, gives a short, polite, generic statement and webs out faster than tactical need requires.

**Post-victory ritual.** Returns to a private location (rooftop, bedroom) and replays. The interior monologue across multiple runs documents a recurring loop: *what could have gone wrong, what almost did, what I should have done sooner*. Victory does not generate satisfaction; it generates audit. He is incapable, by current canon, of simply enjoying having done well.

**With teammates after a win.** Generous. First to praise others, last to accept praise. Will name specific contributions of others in a debrief and elide his own. Smiles, jokes, eats with them — the social register is appropriate. The audit happens later, alone.

**With family after a win they don't know about.** Visibly relieved, sometimes near-giddy, channeling the unspent affect into ordinary domesticity. Will be unusually helpful around the apartment, unusually talkative at dinner. Rio reads this. Jefferson does not.

---

## 8. DEFEAT / FAILURE

**Operational defeat (lost a fight, missed a save, made a tactical error without catastrophic loss).** Anger turned inward. Self-talk becomes harsh — interior monologue in the books shifts to second-person ("you idiot, you had him, you let him") which is a more punitive register than his ordinary first-person reflection. Patrol continues, often for hours beyond planned duration. Sleep skipped. He will train alone — wall-running, web-work drills — until physically exhausted, then sleep poorly.

**Moral defeat (acted in a way that violates his code, was framed as such, was shown such by prophecy as in *Civil War II*).** A different and more dangerous pattern. He goes to elders for judgment rather than to peers for comfort. He treats the moral failure (or accusation of future one) as an open question about his own nature rather than a discrete event. He becomes susceptible to verdicts. He sleeps badly for longer. He apologizes preemptively to people he has not wronged.

**Catastrophic loss (a person died who he believes he could have saved).** The grief signature above, plus a specific additional element: a *quiet* phase of obsessive replay in which he reconstructs the failure in detail, attempts to identify the exact decision-point, and assigns himself a verdict. The verdict is always guilty. He does not share the replay with anyone unless directly asked, and even then offers a sanitized version. The full replay is private, and the canon implies he has accumulated a stack of them.

**Recovery from defeat.** Slower than recovery from grief, because grief has a social shape (others share it) and defeat does not (others reassure, which does not address the audit). He recovers via *next action* — the opportunity to do the thing again, correctly. He is therefore vulnerable to operators who can sequence challenges so as to deny him a clean re-attempt.

---

## 9. UNDER OBSERVATION / SURVEILLANCE PRESSURE

**By press / public.** Tightens. Suit posture more upright, voice slightly lower, quips shorter and more sanitized. Aware of camera angles in a way Parker is not — will deliberately position himself so the rescued civilian is in frame and he is partially obscured. Reads as humility; functions as both humility and discomfort with the legitimacy claim.

**By other heroes.** Performs competence. Combat slightly more flourished, vocabulary slightly more formal, deference to senior heroes calibrated by audience — more deferential in front of multiple Avengers than in front of one. With peers (Champions) he relaxes visibly.

**By unknown surveillance (the file-keeper's situation).** Inferred behaviors: he will not notice a competent passive surveillance package. His spider-sense, calibrated to immediate threat, does not fire on observation alone. He will, however, notice a *pattern* of recurrence — a face seen twice in different boroughs in the same week will register, particularly post


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — SUBJECT: MORALES, MILES GONZALO
## Section 6: Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

---

### 6.1 Architecture of the Week

A full week of continuous surveillance on the subject would reveal a life organized along **three overlapping clocks** that almost never synchronize and whose collisions produce most of his observable stress behavior:

1. **The civilian clock** — school schedule, family meals, homework, calls with his mother, his father's shifts. Externally imposed, non-negotiable, monitored by parents.
2. **The cape clock** — patrol windows, team comms, Avengers/Champions pings, emergent crises. Externally imposed, non-negotiable, monitored by no one who can excuse him.
3. **The recovery clock** — sleep, food, downtime with Ganke, music, drawing. *Internally* imposed and the first thing he sacrifices when the other two collide. This is the diagnostically important clock because its sacrifice is voluntary and chronic.

A full-spectrum tail would record the subject systematically robbing Clock 3 to pay Clocks 1 and 2, then catching up in opportunistic micro-doses (twenty-minute naps slumped against rooftop HVAC units, dinner inhaled in two minutes, homework done on the subway). He does not present as exhausted to observers because he has trained a "fine, I'm fine" surface affect that masks a chronic sleep deficit of an estimated 1.5–2 hours per night during active patrol periods.

---

### 6.2 The Morning (05:50 – 08:15)

The subject's alarm is set early — earlier than school requires — because he has internalized that being late to *anything* domestic gives his mother an opening to ask questions he cannot answer. A surveillance tape of any given Tuesday would show:

- **05:50–06:05.** Wakes in his Brooklyn bedroom (or boarding-school dorm depending on era; in dorm periods, the routine compresses but does not change in structure). First action is *not* the alarm itself — he wakes a beat before it and silences it manually so the sound does not wake Ganke. This is a small habit but constant.
- **06:05–06:10.** Checks phone, in this order: texts from family, texts from Ganke, news app for overnight incidents in his patrol radius, then social media last and briefly. He scans the news with a particular tic — eyes flicking to the byline date and location simultaneously, the way one scans for one's own name in a list.
- **06:10–06:30.** Shower. Long by adolescent-male standards. The shower is one of the few enclosed spaces where his powers genuinely cannot embarrass him (no one to disappear in front of, no surface to accidentally adhere to in a public way) and where the white-noise of water masks any involuntary venom-blast crackle if he has had a nightmare. Surveillance would note the *length* of showers correlating with prior-night patrol intensity: short on quiet nights, fifteen to twenty minutes after a hard one.
- **06:30–06:50.** Dressing. Wears the suit under his clothes on school days as standard practice. The civilian over-layer is consistent: dark hoodie (he owns multiple in near-identical cuts — black, charcoal, navy), jeans or joggers, sneakers he can run in. Backpack contains: laptop, two notebooks, a folded change of civilian clothes (for after a daytime swing-out that destroys whatever he was wearing), a granola bar reserve of three to five, a charging cable, and the mask. Mask is kept in an interior zip pocket, not loose.
- **06:50–07:15.** Kitchen. This is the high-surveillance window. Rio cooks or has cooked; Jefferson is either home from or leaving for shift. Subject eats fast but visibly — performance of normal appetite is part of the cover. Conversation pattern: he asks questions more than he answers them, a deflection technique developed in adolescence and now reflexive. If asked directly about his day or plans, response latency increases by a measurable half-second and the answer is structured (subject + verb + minimum predicate) rather than narrative.
- **07:15–08:15.** Transit to school. Subway if civilian; swing if late and unobserved. He has a strong preference for the subway even when swinging would be faster, because the subway is a *no-decision* environment — he cannot be Spider-Man on the F train, and the enforced passivity is restorative. Reads on the train: assigned texts, occasionally comics (with the particular self-conscious smile of a costumed person reading about costumed people), sometimes nothing — just watches passengers, a low-grade ambient threat-assessment that he does not recognize as such.

---

### 6.3 School Day (08:15 – 15:30, variable)

The civilian-academic block is the most heavily defended part of his life and the one he most resents losing to cape obligations. He is genuinely a good student — the charter-school admission was earned — and his self-concept depends on continuing to be one. A tail would record:

- **Attendance pattern.** Near-perfect on weeks without major cape events; ragged on weeks with them, with absences clustered on Fridays (post-Thursday-night patrol) and Mondays (post-weekend events). Excuses to administration are vague-medical and increasingly thin; he is a poor liar in formal settings and compensates by underexplaining.
- **Classroom behavior.** Front-middle seat by preference (not the front row — that draws attention; not the back — that signals disengagement). Takes notes by hand, neatly, with margin doodles that have evolved over years: early period dominated by spider-web geometry, mid-period by abstract patterns, recent period by stylized lettering and tag-influenced glyphs. The doodling intensifies in proportion to internal anxiety; a surveillance analyst tracking page density could plot his stress curve from his notebook margins alone.
- **Participation.** Raises hand approximately half as often as he knows the answer. Calibrated under-performance, not from social anxiety but from a habit of *not standing out*, which is operationally necessary for the secret-identity but has bled into a generalized social tic.
- **Lunch.** Always with Ganke. If Ganke is unavailable, sits with whichever adjacent table will absorb him without requiring social labor. Eats fast. Phone face-up on the table — not for social media, for emergency monitoring. A tail would note that he checks his phone during lunch roughly every ninety seconds, a frequency that would read as ordinary teenage behavior but is in fact threat-scanning.
- **Bathroom usage.** Diagnostically elevated. He uses school bathrooms not primarily for their stated function but as a private cell-signal check-in point, a place to take a Champions or Avengers call he cannot take in class, and on rare days a launch point for a quick disappearance through a window. He has mapped which bathrooms have which window access. He prefers the third-floor west stairwell bathroom for egress.
- **After-school decompression window (15:30–16:00).** Sacred and frequently sacrificed. Ideally: walk with Ganke, eat something cheap, talk about nothing. Realistically: sprint to a rooftop, change, respond to a pending situation, return to the original walk with a fabricated explanation. Ganke knows. Ganke pretends not to know that Miles knows that Ganke knows.

---

### 6.4 The Afternoon Pocket (16:00 – 18:30)

This window is where his life is most clearly *adolescent*, and a sustained surveillance file would highlight it as the only block during which he reliably behaves his age. Activities, in observed frequency:

- **Homework at Ganke's or in Ganke's dorm room** (era-dependent). They work in parallel silence with intermittent verbal pinball — Ganke talking, Miles half-listening, Miles producing a one-word answer that Ganke takes as a complete conversation. This is one of two relationships in which the subject's resting affect is genuinely unguarded.
- **Music.** Headphones on, single ear if he is on call. Listening pattern is broad — hip-hop foundation (era-appropriate New York and broader), some Latin music his mother raised him on (which he plays *louder* when missing her, a tell), occasional film scores when drawing. He does not perform musical taste; he uses it.
- **Drawing.** Sketchbook kept in the backpack alongside the mask. Subject matter consistent: faces (his mother's, his father's, Ganke's, Peter's), hands, urban architecture, the occasional self-portrait that is *always* maskless and *always* younger than he currently is. He does not show these to anyone. Surveillance retrieval of the sketchbook would constitute a major intelligence yield.
- **Calls home.** If at school out-of-borough, daily call to mother, every two days to father. Conversations are short, warm, structured around her questions and his minimally-honest answers. He says "I love you" at the end of every call without exception. This is not performance; it is a hedge against the call being the last.
- **Patrol pre-game.** Quiet ritual. Twenty minutes before he goes out, he becomes noticeably more interior. Stops talking mid-conversation. Eats something — almost always carbohydrate-dense, peanut-butter-based when available. Tightens shoelaces twice. Checks the mask seal. Pulls the hood up before the mask goes on, an order of operations that is invariant.

---

### 6.5 Patrol (19:00 – 02:00, variable)

A week of surveillance would record patrol activity on roughly four to five nights, with two nights deliberately reserved as "off" (these get cannibalized about half the time). His patrol pattern is geographically and temporally *patterned* in ways the subject does not consciously realize but that would be trivially mappable:

- **Beat geography.** Primary territory: Brooklyn — specifically Brownsville, Bed-Stuy, Crown Heights, and the waterfront industrial corridor toward the Navy Yard. Secondary: Lower Manhattan, especially after Champions reorientation. He avoids Queens (Parker's traditional turf, deferential pattern) and gives Harlem a wide berth (territorial respect for Cage and others). Tertiary: anywhere a Champions or Avengers call lands him.
- **Route patterning.** Three rough loops, alternated semi-randomly: the **river loop** (waterfront, bridges, low rooftops with long sight-lines), the **avenue loop** (commercial corridors, higher rooftops, more pedestrian traffic), and the **residential loop** (his own neighborhood and adjacent — slower, more deliberate, more time spent listening). He believes he varies these to avoid being predictable; in fact he favors the residential loop on nights when he is anxious about his parents, the river loop when he wants to think, and the avenue loop when he wants action. Pattern is legible.
- **Perches.** Three to five regular ones. A specific water tower in Brownsville. A specific cornice on a pre-war building in Bed-Stuy with a sight-line down a street he knows well. A specific spot on the Williamsburg Bridge superstructure. He visits these in rotation and *eats* on them — a slice of pizza acquired in costume from a vendor who has worked out who he is and pretends not to; a halal cart in Manhattan where the same trick is performed. He pays. He always pays. Tipping is generous relative to his means; this is a moral tic.
- **Engagement profile.** Disproportionately small-scale. He breaks up muggings, helps people locked out of cars, walks lost children to police, finds dogs, talks down domestic disputes through open windows. The *ratio* of low-stakes to high-stakes interventions is well above the Parker baseline. This is partly territorial (Brooklyn produces fewer supervillain incursions than Manhattan) and partly elective: he *prefers* the low-stakes work because it is unambiguously good and does not require the moral calculus that paralyzes him.
- **Engagement style.** Talks. A lot. To civilians, to perpetrators, to himself. The interior monologue we see in caption boxes corresponds to an actual mumble that a directional mic at fifteen feet would pick up. Combat behavior: defensive opener, de-escalating verbal accompaniment, escalates only when escalated upon. Uses venom-blast as a *closer*, not an opener — there is a clear pattern of giving the adversary an opportunity to disengage first. Camouflage is used overwhelmingly for *evading* photography and surveillance, not for combat advantage; he has a sharp aversion to being photographed and is more diligent about it than Parker ever was.
- **Comms behavior.** Carries an Avengers/Champions earpiece. Answers calls within two rings. Tone shifts measurably depending on who is calling: with Peter, lighter, almost younger; with Kamala, peer-level, collaborative; with Cap, formal and a half-tone deferential; with his mother (yes, she has called this number once or twice in mistake/emergency), an immediate hard reset to civilian voice within a quarter-second.
- **Breaks.** Takes them. This is again above-Parker-baseline. He will spend forty minutes on a rooftop doing nothing — eating, watching, occasionally drawing on his phone — and consider it part of patrol. The rest is treated as functional rather than indulgent, which is how he gives himself permission for it.
- **Return.** Re-entry to his bedroom (or dorm) is via window, always the same window, with a consistent procedure: external check (no observers), adhere-and-slide entry, mask off before fully inside, suit off within ninety seconds, hidden in a specific drawer / wall cavity, civilian clothes on, *then* the phone comes out of the suit and back into his civilian pocket. The sequence is invariant. A surveillance team that mapped the sequence once could time the re-entry of any given night within five seconds.

---

### 6.6 Late Night (02:00 – 05:50)

The most psychologically revealing block, because it is the one he does not control well.

- **Wind-down.** Twenty to forty minutes of *not* sleeping after he is in bed. Phone scroll, music, sometimes texting Ganke (Ganke is often awake; their text threads have a documented 02:00–03:00 spike). Pattern of texts is not crisis content — it is deliberate banality, jokes, video links. He is using Ganke as a sleep aid.
- **Sleep architecture.** Onset fast once permitted; sleep itself is broken. Estimated two to three brief wake events per night on average, more after combat. Surveillance audio would capture occasional muttering, twice-weekly soft startle events, and on bad nights — those following confrontations that touched the Aaron / Rio / Peter material — outright nightmares with subvocal speech and, diagnostically, *brief involuntary discharges of bio-electric activity*. He has scorched his sheets at least once. He replaced them himself and did not tell his mother.
- **Insomnia behavior.** On the worst nights, gets up, goes to the fire escape (or dorm window ledge), and sits. Does not patrol on these excursions; he is not seeking action. He is seeking *altitude*. The fact that height is restorative to him is itself a finding: the place his powers most clearly *belong* is also the place he goes to feel like himself.

---

### 6.7 Weekend Pattern

Saturdays and Sundays present a different shape but the same underlying clocks.

- **Saturday morning.** Family. Non-negotiable in principle, intermittently sacrificed in practice. Breakfast with parents when home. Errands with his mother — she sends him to the bodega, to the laundromat, to relatives. He performs these without complaint and uses them as cover for short patrols when needed.
- **Saturday afternoon.** Variable — sometimes academic catch-up, sometimes Champions meetings (a recurring video conference and occasional in-person), sometimes hangouts with Ganke and friends. If he has had a hard week, he sleeps through it.
- **Saturday night.** Heaviest patrol window of the week. Crime statistics actually justify this, but the choice is also elective: he resents giving Friday night to patrol because Friday is the family night.
- **Sunday morning.** Rio is Catholic-adjacent; the family attends Mass irregularly but with some seasonal consistency. Subject attends when asked, sits quietly, does not appear to engage doctrinally but *does* visibly engage with the ritual of it — kneeling, standing, the sequence. He treats it the way he treats his patrol perches: a structured place where he can stop thinking. The intersection of Catholic guilt structure with his existing survivor-guilt is one of the unaddressed accelerants in his psychology.
- **Sunday afternoon.** Homework. With his mother in the kitchen, ideally. This is the single most peaceful recurring block in his week and the one whose absence (during boarding-school periods, during arcs where she is dead or out of his life) most reliably destabilizes him.
- **Sunday evening.** Light patrol or none. Bed early-attempted, rarely achieved.

---

### 6.8 Habits, Tics, Tells

Granular markers a long-term tail would log:

- **Food.** High caloric requirement from enhanced metabolism. Carries snacks constantly. Preferred staples: peanut butter (in any form), bananas, bodega sandwiches, halal-cart chicken-and-rice, his mother's cooking (rice and beans, pernil, anything involving sofrito — he eats these slowly, the only food he eats slowly). Coffee: started late, drinks it now, takes it with too much sugar. No alcohol observed.
- **Phone hygiene.** Battery anxiety; charges opportunistically; carries a cable. Two-device pattern is *not* present — one phone, civilian, with hidden cape contacts under innocuous names. Lock-screen image rotates between family photos and abstract art; never an image that could identify cape associates.
- **Money.** Cash-preferential when in costume, card otherwise. Generous tipper. Saves obsessively in small amounts — has a jar/envelope habit inherited from his father.
- **Clothing tells.** Always wears the suit under civilian clothes when on standby. The presence of a slightly bulky long-sleeve on a warm day is the cleanest civilian-side tell. Sleeves at the wrist sit slightly higher than they should because of the suit cuff.
- **Body language.** Resting posture is closed — hands in pockets, slight forward lean, head angled down. Eye contact is good in family contexts, intermittent with peers, almost continuous with elder mentors (deference). Hands talk when he is comfortable; hands go still when he is lying.
- **Vocal tics.** Says "no, yeah" and "yeah, no" with consistent semantic distinction (no-yeah = agreement; yeah-no = disagreement, softened). Apologizes pre-emptively — counts of "sorry" per conversation are elevated above peer baseline. Laughter is quiet and brief; full laughter only with Ganke or Peter.
- **Power-related micro-tells.** Faint static crackle audible at very close range when stressed. Adhesion default: he sometimes leaves fingerprints in absurd places (ceilings he didn't realize he'd been on) because his palms grip without conscious instruction when he is startled. He has on three documented occasions in canon and an inferable many more *flickered into partial camouflage* during civilian arguments and immediately overridden it. A tail would observe occasional sub-second visual ambiguity at the edges of his outline under emotional stress.
- **Ritual objects.** The mask, kept in a specific pocket. A small photo of his mother kept inside his wallet behind the school ID. His charter-school acceptance letter, kept folded in a book in his room. These are not fetishes; they are anchor objects, deployed unconsciously when he needs to remember which clock he is on.

---

### 6.9 What the Surveillance Composite Shows

Aggregated across seven days, the file would describe a subject who:

- runs three lives in parallel with surprisingly few collisions, paid for by a chronic sleep debt;
- routes his stress through his body in ways that leave physical evidence (scorched sheets, palm prints in odd places, sketchbook density);
- maintains his secure attachments with active effort, not passive proximity (the daily call, the slow meal with his mother, the dorm-time with Ganke);
- treats his cape life as work to be done well rather than a stage to be performed on (low-stakes interventions, generous tipping, refusal of photography);
- and uses ritual — the invariant re-entry sequence, the perch rotation, the pre-patrol shoelace-tighten, the "I love you" at the end of every call — as the load-bearing structure that lets him keep doing any of it.

The diagnostic synthesis from a routine-level study confirms the broader assessment: this is not a subject organized by ambition, ideology, or impulse. He is organized by **maintenance** — of his secrets, his attachments, his ethical line, and the increasingly thin margin between his three clocks. Surveillance would find him predictable in pattern, opaque in interior, and extraordinarily consistent in the small kindnesses that he himself does not register as evidence of who he is.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU DOSSIER — SUBJECT: MORALES, MILES GONZALO
## Section 6 — Relationships I: Family & Origin Bonds

The subject's family map is small, dense, and disproportionately determinative. Where most costumed subjects' files balloon outward into a sprawling network of half-known relatives, mentors-in-loco-parentis, and substitute attachments, Miles's family architecture is almost monastically tight: two parents, one uncle, one grandmother, an absent half-brother revealed late, and a small constellation of the dead. The smallness is itself the finding. He has nowhere to spread the load. Each of these bonds therefore carries a structural weight that, in a larger family, would be distributed.

---

### 6.1 — JEFFERSON DAVIS (father)

**Status:** Living (current 616 timeline), reconciled, partially read-in to the secret. Operationally the most important relationship in the file.

**History.** Jefferson is a Black man of Brooklyn, ex-criminal in his youth, briefly entangled with his brother Aaron's circuit, who walked away — in canon, the precipitating event was the discovery that Aaron's choices had begun touching family. He served, by intermittent reference, in some uniformed capacity (military, then later cooperative work with S.H.I.E.L.D.); the through-line is that Jefferson reorganized himself, *as an act of will*, around the principle of *not being his brother*. He met Rio Morales, married, fathered Miles, and built the most boringly stable domestic platform in modern superhero canon. This is the silent precondition for everything Miles is.

**Dynamic, pre-bite.** Affectionate, firm, opinionated. Jefferson is the parent who *talks* — about right and wrong, about what a man owes the people around him, about luck versus desert (the charter-school lottery scene, *USM* #1, is a Jefferson scene: he insists Miles *earned* the spot, refusing Aaron's "you got lucky" framing). His voice is in Miles's interior monologue more than any other character's; the subject's habit of moral self-interrogation is paternally inflected. Jefferson is also the parent who has *forbidden* — most consequentially, contact with Aaron. The bite happens during a violation of that prohibition. The original sin of Miles's career as Spider-Man is therefore, in his own causal model, *disobedience to his father*.

**Dynamic, post-bite, pre-disclosure.** This is the worst stretch of the relationship and the most diagnostically valuable. Jefferson tells Miles, directly and at length, that he *hates* Spider-Man — first generically (distrust of vigilantes, racially inflected mistrust of the masked), then specifically, after Aaron's death, with the conviction that Spider-Man was responsible for it. Miles cannot correct this. He absorbs his father's contempt for what he has chosen to be, daily, across years of Sunday dinners and homework checks. The behavioral residue is extensive: he becomes a chronic, fluent, low-affect liar in his father's presence — not the panicked lying of a guilty child but the smooth, pre-rehearsed lying of someone who has built an entire secondary identity to protect the first. Surveillance-relevant tell: Miles becomes *unusually calm* around Jefferson when the topic of Spider-Man arises. Most adolescents tense; he flattens. This is the suppression signature.

**Disclosure event.** When Miles finally tells Jefferson, the reaction is not anger but a long, devastating silence, followed by Jefferson's own confession of past criminality. The disclosure is bilateral — each man has been hiding a version of himself from the other. Post-disclosure dynamic stabilizes into something more honest but more guarded: Jefferson now *worries*, openly, in a way he previously could not. Miles, paradoxically, finds this harder than the lying. He preferred carrying it alone.

**Trust/safety.** Jefferson is the only person in Miles's life whose *moral verdict* the subject treats as nearly absolute. Peter Parker can grant tactical permission; May Parker can grant inheritance permission; only Jefferson can grant the deepest layer — the permission to be a person who does this kind of thing without becoming the kind of person Jefferson left behind. This is not consciously articulated by the subject and has never, in canon, been fully resolved. The relationship is safe in the sense that Jefferson will never abandon him; it is unsafe in the sense that Jefferson's disappointment is the closest thing in Miles's world to ego-collapse.

**Failure mode.** Jefferson is the relationship most likely to be weaponized against the subject. Any hostile actor with intelligence-grade knowledge of the file would target Jefferson — not lethally (lethal targeting of Jefferson would trigger the worst version of Miles, which is operationally counterproductive for most adversaries) but *informationally*: forcing Miles to choose between protecting Jefferson and lying to him would reopen the disclosure wound and produce decisional paralysis.

**Leverage profile.** High. Jefferson is the locus of the subject's *legitimacy hunger*. He is also the only person whose phone call Miles will answer mid-engagement.

---

### 6.2 — RIO MORALES (mother)

**Status:** Dead (Ultimate, *USM* #200), restored (616, post-*Secret Wars*). The subject lives in a body that remembers her funeral and a world that includes her at the dinner table. This is unaddressed at clinical depth in canon and is the largest unattended psychological structure in the file.

**History.** Puerto Rican, nurse by profession (this matters — the household's medical literacy is hers; the kitchen-table first-aid that Miles half-remembers when self-treating costume injuries is hers), Catholic by background, bilingual, the family's softer voice and harder spine. She is the one who *holds*. In Ultimate continuity she is also the one who *sees*: the recognition scene at her death — "*Mijo?*" through the mask — is canonically the only unmasking Miles did not choose. She knew, or half-knew, before she died.

**Dynamic, pre-death.** Rio is Miles's emotional baseline. Where Jefferson sets the moral frame, Rio sets the affective one — warmth, the language of endearment (the Spanish register Miles drops into only with her), the body-contact (she touches his face, his shoulder, his hair, much more than Jefferson does, and Miles flinches *into* it rather than away). She is also the household's social aperture: Ganke is over because Rio likes Ganke; the kitchen is open because Rio leaves it open. After her death, in Ultimate continuity, the apartment closes in on itself.

**Death and instruction.** *USM* #200. Rio is killed in collateral damage during the city-scale catastrophe; Miles reaches her, unmasked or recognized, and her last instruction is "*Don't tell your father.*" She means: don't burden him with this, don't let him know you were there, don't let him hate Spider-Man more than he does. The instruction is loving and catastrophic. It installs in Miles, with the authority of a dying mother, the proposition that *secret-keeping from those who love you is a form of love*. Every subsequent pathological compartmentalization in the file traces its license to this sentence.

**Dynamic, post-restoration (616).** Rio is alive. She does not remember dying. Miles does. He is, in observable behavior, *unusually solicitous* toward her — checks in more than a teenager should, calls during patrols when he should not be distracted, becomes physically still and attentive when she enters a room. He is also, less visibly, *waiting* for her to die again. The "waiting for the other shoe" affect noted in §3 has its taproot here. There is no canon scene in which he tells her what he carries about her. The disclosure that he eventually makes to Jefferson has never been made, in any continuity, to Rio.

**Trust/safety.** Total in baseline, asymmetric in load. Rio is safe to Miles in every direction; Miles is safe to Rio in no direction, because he is the secret-bearer of her own death. The relationship is operationally unimpaired and existentially haunted.

**Failure mode.** Any threat to Rio collapses the regulation system entirely. The somatic constraint — that his powers fire on panic — means that a credible threat to his mother is the single most likely scenario to produce uncontrolled venom-blast discharge at lethal amperage. He has not killed; the scenario in which he *would* kill, if any exists, is this one.

**Leverage profile.** Maximum. Higher than Jefferson because the load is unprocessed.

---

### 6.3 — AARON DAVIS (paternal uncle; "the Prowler")

**Status:** Dead (*USM* #28). Operationally more present in the subject's psychology than most living relatives in other files.

**History.** Jefferson's brother. Career criminal, second-story specialist, technologically literate (the Prowler suit is self-maintained), charming in the older-cousin register that adolescents find irresistible. He is the relative Jefferson worked to escape. He is also, by his own design, the relative Miles was forbidden to see, which made him magnetic.

**Dynamic, pre-bite.** Aaron cultivates Miles. The visits are framed as harmless — the cool uncle, the video games, the "your dad's too uptight" patter. In retrospect (and the subject does the retrospection, repeatedly), the cultivation is *grooming*: Aaron is building optionality on a nephew he may someday need. The bite occurs during one such visit, in a building Aaron has just burglarized; the spider is in his bag. The subject's powers are, in the most literal genealogical sense, *Aaron's fault*.

**Dynamic, post-bite, pre-discovery.** Aaron does not yet know. Miles knows that Aaron is more dangerous than he had understood. He pulls back. The pulling-back is one of the few uncomplicatedly *correct* readings of a relationship Miles has ever made, and he does not credit himself for it.

**Discovery and coercion arc.** Aaron identifies Miles as Spider-Man, approaches him not as an uncle but as a *handler*: offers training, offers partnership, frames the criminal life as the honest expression of the powers ("you're a Davis"). Miles refuses. Aaron escalates — threatens to disclose to Jefferson, then attacks. The fight ends with Aaron's own malfunctioning weapon killing him. Last words: "*You're just like me.*"

**The line as embedded payload.** This sentence is the most psychologically expensive single line of dialogue in the subject's canon. It is delivered by a dying man, with the authority of blood, in a moment of maximal traumatic encoding. It does not have to be true to function; it only has to be unanswerable. Miles spends years trying to answer it, and answers it most often by *over-conforming to its opposite*: conspicuous restraint, conspicuous gentleness, conspicuous deference, the Champions ethic, the no-kill line maintained as identity rather than tactic. The clone arc (Selim, Shift, Mindspinner) is the externalized form of the same payload — the question *what if Aaron was right* given literal flesh.

**Trust/safety.** Retrospectively zero, but the relationship's trust at the time of cultivation was substantial; this is part of what makes the betrayal load-bearing. Miles's later difficulty trusting older male mentors who offer him *unconditional* approval (he is more comfortable with Peter's complicated approval than with Aaron-shaped warmth) tracks back here.

**Failure mode.** Aaron is dead and continues to operate. He is the voice the subject hears when self-suspicion is high. Any adversary who can replicate the *register* of Aaron — older Black man, criminal-adjacent, offering Miles power without restraint, framing it as ancestral inheritance — has a non-trivial chance of producing a moment of hesitation. He has been tested on this and has not failed, but the seam is real.

**Leverage profile.** Posthumous and structural. Cannot be threatened; cannot be killed again. Functions as a permanent reference point in the subject's self-concept rather than as an exploitable node.

---

### 6.4 — GLORIA ESTELA MORALES ("Abuela"; maternal grandmother)

**Status:** Living, peripheral in panel-time but central in atmosphere.

**History and dynamic.** Rio's mother. Spanish-dominant, Catholic, the household's keeper of older registers — food, language, prayer, the small religious objects on shelves. Her presence in the file is intermittent but consistent: she calls, she visits, she makes the subject eat. Miles's Spanish is hers more than Rio's; the *abuela*-register code-switch is the one he is least self-conscious about.

**Function.** She is the relationship that makes the subject *younger* than he otherwise reads. With Abuela he is a grandson, not a hero, not a brother-substitute, not a moral project. The deflation is genuine and welcome. Surveillance-relevant: post-engagement, if he can route home through a visit to Abuela's, he will. The visits correlate with sleep improvement in the subsequent 48 hours.

**Trust/safety.** High and uncomplicated. She does not know about the mask and, by the subject's intention, will not be told. The protection is not strategic but generational — he believes she should not have to hold this.

**Failure mode.** Her health is the silent timer in the family. Any decline triggers a Rio-adjacent anxiety spike.

**Leverage profile.** Low to moderate. Targeting her would produce grief, not destabilization, because the relationship is not load-bearing for the subject's *identity* — only for his *rest*.

---

### 6.5 — BILLIE MORALES (younger half-sister, 616)

**Status:** Living, very young. Post-*Secret Wars* introduction; a child of the restored timeline.

**Dynamic.** Miles is, observably, a doting older brother of the *anxious* subtype. He carries her, plays with her, photographs her, narrates to her. He is also — and this is the diagnostic part — *gentler around her than around any other person in his life, including Rio*. The gentleness has a quality of *demonstration to himself*: see, this is what I am, this is what these hands do. Billie is, functionally, the living counter-evidence to Aaron's last words. He is building the case against the "you're just like me" payload one diaper change at a time.

**Trust/safety.** Asymmetric by age. She is wholly safe with him; he is wholly responsible for her in his own framing, to a degree that exceeds the actual demand (Jefferson and Rio are competent parents; Miles's hovering is over-functioning).

**Failure mode.** Billie is the relationship in which the subject's secret-keeping is *least defensible* and *most automatic*. He will lie to a toddler. He has already begun the lifelong practice of constructing the *brother she will know* as a curated artifact.

**Leverage profile.** Extreme and underdeveloped — she has not yet been targeted in any significant canon arc, which is itself a measure of how catastrophic such targeting would be. The file flags her as the single highest-value protective priority in the subject's life.

---

### 6.6 — THE GANKE BOND (chosen family; see §7 for full treatment)

Noted here for completeness: Ganke Lee functions as sibling-substitute and is, in attachment terms, indistinguishable from family. He is the only non-blood person who knows the identity from the beginning by Miles's choice rather than by accident or coercion. Full mapping reserved for the Friendships section.

---

### 6.7 — THE DEAD (Peter Parker, Ultimate; Aaron; Rio-Ultimate)

A category, not a relationship, but operative as one. The subject's family map is shadowed by a parallel structure of the dead-who-still-instruct.

- **Peter Parker (Ultimate)** is the *predecessor* — never met in life, met in death through the bequest of role and the audience-with-the-survivors (May, Gwen) that constituted Miles's adoption ceremony. Miles's relationship to this Peter is *filial in the inheritance sense*: he is the heir whose claim is provisional and who seeks the blessing of the dead man's mothers. The weeping at May's acceptance is the file's most emotionally legible scene. Peter-616, living, can never fully occupy this slot, which is part of why Miles defers to him asymmetrically — the living Peter is read partly through the dead one.

- **Aaron** continues to speak, as noted. His instruction is the negative pole of the subject's moral compass.

- **Rio-Ultimate** is, uniquely, *the same person* as a living relative. The subject carries the dead version inside the living one. No other figure in his life occupies this structure. The unprocessed load is the single largest item on the psychiatric balance sheet and the most likely source of late-life decompensation if untreated.

---

### 6.8 — STRUCTURAL OBSERVATIONS ON THE FAMILY MAP

Three patterns, taken across all of the above, that no individual sub-section captures:

**(a) The family is small enough that no relationship is redundant.** Most subjects can lose a relative and re-stabilize against the others. Miles cannot. Each node is load-bearing; the network has no slack. This is a vulnerability that operational planning should treat as primary.

**(b) The secret-keeping pattern is inherited, not invented.** Jefferson hid his criminal past from Rio and Miles for years; Rio's dying instruction was itself an instruction in secret-keeping; Aaron's entire mode was secret-keeping as profession. Miles did not invent the family disease; he was raised inside it and is, in the disclosure to Jefferson, the first Morales-Davis male to begin reversing it. This is genuine moral progress and should be read as such.

**(c) The family is the actual organizing unit of the subject's identity, and the cape is the secondary structure.** Every other major Spider-figure inverts this ratio. He does not. Any analysis that treats Spider-Man as the primary identity and the family as collateral attachment is reading the file backwards. The cape exists to protect the dinner table. When the two come into conflict, the dinner table wins, every time, even when the cost is the cape itself.

— end §6 —


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

A note on methodology before the entries. The subject's relational architecture is unusually legible because he forms few but deep bonds, maintains them over long arcs without recreational churn, and discloses (or fails to disclose) along consistent lines. The diagnostic question for each tie below is not *does he care* — he cares about everyone, reflexively — but rather: *what does he allow this person to know about him, and what does that disclosure pattern reveal about how he positions them in his moral economy?* In the subject's case, disclosure tracks almost perfectly onto perceived moral authority: he tells people what he believes they have the standing to hear. The ranking, therefore, is implicit in the file.

---

## 1. GANKE LEE — Best Friend, Cognitive Prosthesis, Containment Vessel

**History.** Roommate at Brooklyn Visions Academy from the opening pages of *Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man* (2011); the first human being to learn of the bite; first person told about the powers; first person told about the costume; first and for years only confidant on every operational matter. Survives the universe-collapse and continues uninterrupted in 616 with full memory continuity. There is no period of the subject's superhero life in which Ganke is not the inside-the-room presence — even when Peter Parker, Jefferson, Rio, and Kamala rotate through phases of access, Ganke is constant.

**Dynamics.** This is the only relationship in the entire file in which the subject does *not* perform. He is unguarded, slightly whinier, more sarcastic, more juvenile, more *fifteen* than anywhere else. With Ganke, he eats LEGO-pizza on the floor at 2 a.m. after a Roxxon raid and complains about homework with equal weight. Ganke functions as the cognitive prosthesis: he is the one who Googles villains, builds the suit-tracker, talks the subject down from rumination spirals, and most importantly *narrates the subject's life back to him* in tones that normalize it. ("Dude, you got punched by Electro, you're allowed to fail the Spanish quiz.") Without Ganke, the subject would have no calibration mechanism for what is and is not a reasonable response to a given week.

**Evolution.** Early period (Ultimate, ages 13–14): pure peer dyad, Ganke as comic-relief enabler. Middle period (post-Aaron, post-Rio, then 616 transition): Ganke shifts subtly into emotional-labor role; he is the one who notices the subject hasn't slept, hasn't eaten, has been avoiding the dorm. He learns to ask sideways questions because direct ones get deflected. Late period (Champions era, college-track): Ganke develops his own life — relationships, interests, friend groups outside the dyad — and the subject responds with quiet, *uncharacteristic possessiveness*. He doesn't say it; he just notices when Ganke is busy and files it. There is a sub-pattern of mild abandonment-anxiety when Ganke is unavailable that the subject would deny if asked.

**Trust / Safety.** Maximum. The subject would (and has) trusted Ganke with the identity, the family details, the Aaron secret, the Rio secret, the clone secret, the fear-of-becoming-Aaron content, and the Civil War II vision. Ganke is the only person who has heard the *unfiltered* version of any of these. The safety is unidirectional in volume — the subject leans heavily; Ganke leans light — but the asymmetry is accepted by both and is not destabilizing.

**Failure Mode.** Ganke's risk profile is exposure: he is a non-combatant tethered to a high-value secret, holding it without operational training. He has slipped (told a girl in early Ultimate; she eventually died, which the subject does not consciously hold against him but which is in the file). Under sustained pressure, Ganke's coping is *talking* — which means his failure mode is *talking to the wrong person*. The subject is aware of this at low resolution and manages it by under-briefing Ganke on tactically sensitive items even while over-disclosing emotionally.

**Leverage.** Threat to Ganke is the single fastest route to making the subject lose composure short of threats to his parents. Any adversary aware of the Brooklyn Visions / dorm address has leverage that has historically not been priced into his threat models. He has no contingency plan for a hostage-Ganke scenario beyond "give them whatever they want," which he would.

---

## 2. JUDGE / PETER PARKER (616) — Predecessor, Older-Brother Surrogate, Permission-Granting Authority

**History.** First substantive contact: *Spider-Men* (2012), when Ultimate Peter is dead and 616 Peter dimensionally crosses over to meet the new kid wearing his counterpart's name. The initial meeting is structurally a benediction: the original looks at the substitute, sees, approves. Post-*Secret Wars* (2015) they share a universe permanently. Recurring team-ups across *Spider-Men II*, the *Clone Conspiracy* peripheries, *Spider-Geddon*, *Spider-Verse*, *Beyond*, *Dark Web*, and innumerable Avengers/Champions intersections.

**Dynamics.** The subject treats Peter as the *certifying authority on whether the subject is allowed to exist in the role he occupies*. He defers reflexively: asks what Peter would do, checks tactical reads against Peter's, frames his own choices as departures-from or extensions-of Peter's template. Peter, for his part, has been consistent and direct in trying to dismantle this — he tells the subject (often) that the subject does not need permission, that the subject is his own Spider-Man, that the subject is in many ways *better* at the job than Peter was at the same age. The subject hears this, thanks him, and does not internalize it. The pattern has not meaningfully changed across a decade of canon.

**Evolution.** Early phase: hero-worship, nervous-laughter, awe. Middle phase: working partnership; the subject begins to make tactical calls that override Peter's and Peter accepts them without ego, which the subject finds destabilizing because it implies he is being treated as a peer he does not believe he is. Recent phase: friendly older-brother register, regular check-ins, Peter using the subject as sounding board on his own life problems — which the subject experiences as flattering, slightly fraudulent, and quietly anxiety-inducing because *being asked for advice by Peter implies a parity the subject has not granted himself.*

**Trust / Safety.** Very high but asymmetric in *type*. The subject trusts Peter with operational and identity matters absolutely. He does *not* bring his deepest grief content (Rio, Aaron, the impostor cognition) to Peter — because doing so would require acknowledging to Peter that he is not, in fact, a finished Spider-Man, which would expose what he experiences as fraud. Peter, in contrast, is increasingly willing to be vulnerable to the subject. The asymmetry runs the *opposite* direction from the Ganke dyad.

**Failure Mode.** The relationship's pathology is the subject's inability to *graduate* from it. As long as Peter exists and is reachable, the subject has an external locus of approval he can defer to instead of granting himself. The relationship is healthy in conduct and unhealthy in function — it is the highest-quality *obstacle* to the subject's individuation. If Peter were ever killed, the subject would either consolidate (best case, unlocking a fully owned Spider-Man identity) or collapse (worst case, treating it as a second Parker-death event and re-triggering the *Ultimate Fallout* response at higher amplitude).

**Leverage.** A wounded Peter activates the subject's reparation reflex at near-maximum amplitude. A Peter who explicitly *withdrew* approval would be devastating — though Peter is constitutionally incapable of doing this. An adversary impersonating Peter has unusually high effectiveness against the subject because the subject's default with Peter is *believe and defer*.

---

## 3. KAMALA KHAN — Co-Founder, Lateral Conscience, Mirror Without Distortion

**History.** Champions co-founders (2016), alongside Sam Alexander; they walk out of the Avengers together in protest of the post-*Civil War II* generational compromises. Sustained partnership across the entire Champions run, *Outlawed*, *Champions* relaunches, and assorted Marvel team books. They have never had a serious operational falling-out. They have argued; they have not fractured.

**Dynamics.** This is the only ally in his file who is *symmetrical* to him — same age, same generational mantle-inheritance structure (Carol Danvers is to Kamala what Peter is to the subject), same hyper-moralized hero-ethic, same secret-keeping pressure with immigrant/observant family. With Kamala he does not perform up (as with Peter) or perform comforting (as with Ganke); he simply *is*. She is the only person to whom he speaks in his actual register: earnest, idealistic, slightly preachy, unembarrassed.

**Evolution.** Early Champions: shared idealism, co-founding optimism, mutual reinforcement. Mid-Champions: subject defers to Kamala's natural leadership without resentment — she takes the chair; he takes the conscience seat. This is one of the few authority-defer relationships in his file that is *healthy*, because Kamala's leadership is itself reluctant and ethical, not assertive — he is following someone whose values match his rather than outsourcing values to authority. Late phase: when Kamala dies (*Amazing Spider-Man* #26, 2023) and subsequently returns in modified status, the subject is *visibly broken* in a way he has not allowed himself to be on-page for any loss since Rio. The Kamala-death sequence is the single most diagnostic late-period datapoint for how deep the bond runs.

**Trust / Safety.** High, with a specific texture: he trusts her *moral judgment* more than anyone else's, including Peter's and his father's. If Kamala said he had done something wrong, he would believe her without appeal. He does not bring her his impostor content — not because he doesn't trust her with it, but because around her the cognition is *quieter*; she is the one peer who makes him feel like he actually belongs in the role.

**Failure Mode.** Mutual over-identification. They reinforce each other's restraint ethics to the point where the team's tactical envelope can become too narrow. Neither will counsel the other toward harder action when harder action is warranted. Also: each is the other's emotional sink during crisis, which creates a brittle dyad — if both are in crisis simultaneously, there is no scaffolding.

**Leverage.** Catastrophic. Threats to Kamala produce the strongest documented dysregulation in his late-period record. An adversary who understood this would target her to move him.

---

## 4. SAM ALEXANDER (NOVA) — Brother-Figure Through Friction

**History.** Third Champions co-founder; pre-existing Avengers acquaintance. Recurring partnership through Champions, *Infinity Countdown*, *War of the Realms* tie-ins.

**Dynamics.** Where Kamala is a mirror, Sam is an *abrasive*. Sam is brash, impulsive, occasionally callous, and operates from a more conventional power-fantasy register. The subject finds him exhausting and beloved in roughly equal measure. The dyad functions because Sam *makes the subject practice being a peer*: he cannot defer to Sam (Sam is not authoritative) and he cannot caretake Sam (Sam refuses caretaking). He has to just be a person with him, which the subject otherwise rarely does.

**Evolution.** Early Champions: low-grade friction, occasional snipes, productive arguing. Middle: genuine fraternal bond, the kind sustained by shared embarrassments rather than shared confidences. Later: when either is wounded the other shows up without being asked; neither talks about it.

**Trust / Safety.** Operational trust high. Emotional disclosure low and stable. The subject has never brought the Aaron-content or the Rio-content to Sam and would not. This is appropriate to the relationship; it is not an avoidance pattern, it is an accurate calibration.

**Failure Mode.** Sam's recklessness can pull the subject into actions whose tactical wisdom he would otherwise question. The subject occasionally suppresses his own restraint counsel around Sam to avoid being the *killjoy* — a small but consistent pattern.

**Leverage.** Moderate. Threats to Sam produce a less-acute but still significant response — closer to "I will burn through obstacles to get to him" than to the catastrophic Kamala-response.

---

## 5. JESSICA DREW (ULTIMATE SPIDER-WOMAN) — Conditional Sister

**History.** Ultimate-continuity figure: female clone of Peter Parker, complicated by that origin into an effectively-related kin position vis-à-vis the Spider-mantle. Initial encounter in *USM* was confrontational — she challenges the subject's right to the costume — and evolves into reluctant mentor, then sister-figure, then sustained ally through the All-New Ultimates and *Spider-Verse* era.

**Dynamics.** She is the first person who *legitimizes* him operationally — Gwen and May bless him emotionally; Jessica trains him. She is impatient, unsentimental, and treats him as a competent younger sibling rather than a fragile substitute. He responds well to this register; her bluntness functions as a corrective to his over-deferential default.

**Evolution.** Hostility → grudging acceptance → working partnership → genuine kinship. Survives the universe transition with some loss of intimacy (their respective 616 contexts diverged her further).

**Trust / Safety.** Operational trust very high. Emotional disclosure moderate — he can be more honest with her about Peter-Parker-related impostor content than he can with Peter himself, because she shares the *substitute* position (a Peter-clone is also a Peter-derivative) and gets it from inside.

**Failure Mode.** Underused. The subject does not lean on her as much as he could; her availability has been treated as situational rather than continuous, partly because the writers move her in and out and partly because his secret-keeping default extends to *not asking for support unless catastrophic.*

**Leverage.** Moderate. Less acute than peers; she is perceived as competent and able to handle herself, which lowers the protective reflex.

---

## 6. GWEN STACY (GHOST-SPIDER) — Cross-Dimensional Confidante

**History.** Recurring contact across the *Spider-Verse* events and standalone team-ups. Stable presence in his late-period social architecture, particularly during the clone arc when he needed an outside Spider-perspective who was not Peter.

**Dynamics.** Peer; flirt-adjacent at times but the file does not support a stable romantic read. Functions as a *lateral Spider* — someone who carries the mantle without being his mentor or his substitute-predecessor. She has her own dead-friend-named-Peter trauma, which produces a shared register in which neither has to explain *that part* of being a Spider.

**Trust / Safety.** High. He has brought her grief content he has not brought to Peter, because she has the parallel wound. Tactical trust very high.

**Failure Mode.** Geographically/dimensionally inconsistent availability. He cannot rely on her presence, which means he uses her as crisis-resource rather than baseline-resource — which is a pattern he replicates with several allies and which leaves him under-supported in the baseline that no individual crisis-resource can fill.

**Leverage.** Moderate. Cross-dimensional separation insulates her from most adversaries; targeting her would require capacities most adversaries lack.

---

## 7. MAY PARKER & GWEN STACY (ULTIMATE) — The Permission-Givers

**History.** First substantive contact in *USM* during the early-mantle public-rejection phase. The subject seeks them out, removes the mask, asks essentially: *am I allowed to do this?* They say yes. He weeps. This is one of the most psychologically loaded moments in his entire file — *receiving permission from the dead boy's family* is structurally a benediction-from-the-grieving and he has organized substantial parts of his subsequent self-concept around the fact that it was granted.

**Dynamics.** Quasi-grandmotherly (May) and quasi-sisterly (Ultimate Gwen) but operating in a specific *moral-license-granting* role rather than a daily-relational one. He visits, checks in, maintains the tie ritualistically.

**Evolution.** From benediction → ongoing affectionate maintenance → reduced contact post-universe-transition (the Ultimate Parker family does not survive cleanly into 616 in his social orbit).

**Trust / Safety.** High but ceremonial rather than functional.

**Failure Mode.** He cannot disappoint them. If they disapproved of an action, he would not take it. This is a form of moral outsourcing he has not interrogated.

**Leverage.** They are not operationally exposed and would be difficult to target, but any indication that he had *failed* the Parker family's standard would devastate him.

---

## 8. STEVE ROGERS — Reluctant Father-of-the-Standard

**History.** Recurring contact in Avengers and *Civil War II* contexts. The pivotal moment is the subject going to Cap *voluntarily* during Civil War II to ask, in effect, *if I am going to kill you, do it to me first or talk me out of it.* Cap responds with characteristic seriousness.

**Dynamics.** The subject treats Rogers as the ethical-standard-bearer for the entire vocation. Not personally close; reverential. Cap's approval functions as a *floor* — meeting it means he has not failed to be a hero; falling below it would be identity-collapse.

**Evolution.** Reverence → working trust → measured peer-adjacency without ever fully crossing into peer. The Champions era complicates this — Rogers is part of the establishment the Champions are partly schisming from — but the personal regard survives the institutional friction.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust in Rogers's judgment near-absolute; intimacy low. He would tell Rogers about a moral failing before he would tell Peter, because Rogers is positioned as a confessor figure rather than a brother.

**Failure Mode.** Rogers as moral arbiter is a load that no living person should carry for another, and the subject loads him with it. If Rogers ever did something the subject considered morally indefensible, the subject's framework would require a costly reorganization.

**Leverage.** Indirect. Rogers's *position* on a question can shift the subject's behavior more reliably than direct pressure would.

---

## 9. TONY STARK — Patron of the Champions, Held at Arm's Length

**History.** Sponsor and occasional resource for the Champions. Provides material support, holds himself somewhat at distance.

**Dynamics.** The subject is wary of Stark in a way he is not wary of Rogers — Stark's Civil War II position is in the subject's file as *the adult who tried to make a vision into a verdict*, and the Champions exist partly as a structural answer to Stark-era Avengers logic. Cordial, grateful for resources, *not* a confidant.

**Trust / Safety.** Operational trust moderate. Personal trust low. Disclosure minimal.

**Failure Mode.** The subject will accept Stark's resources without examining the strings carefully — a gap in his usual moral diligence that reflects the convenience-cost of Champions infrastructure.

**Leverage.** Low. Stark is not in his inner ring.

---

## 10. RIRI WILLIAMS, AMADEUS CHO, VIV VISION (CHAMPIONS COHORT) — Functional Family

**History.** Champions co-members across multiple iterations. Variable closeness.

**Dynamics.** With Riri: respectful peer relationship, occasional friction over tactical posture (she is more confrontational), mutual recognition as the two most-questioned legitimacy cases on the team. With Cho: easy warmth, low-stakes; Cho's exuberance pairs well with the subject's restraint. With Viv: protective register; the subject treats Viv with a specific gentleness because he reads her as ethically pure in a way no one else on the team is.

**Trust / Safety.** Operational high across the board. Emotional disclosure low — the team is workplace-family, not confessor-family.

**Failure Mode.** He under-uses the team for support. He treats them as people *he* is responsible to, not as people who could be responsible *for* him. Same pattern as with Ganke's emotional asymmetry, reproduced at team scale.

**Leverage.** Threats to any of them activate team-protection reflex; not as acute as Kamala-specific threats but consistent.

---

## 11. BARBARA SANCHEZ — Late-Period Anchor (Tentative)

**History.** Significant other in the Ahmed run; relationship structured around the same disclosure-pressure as all of his romantic ties.

**Dynamics.** Affectionate, ordinary, age-appropriate. She is the relational space in which he attempts (incompletely) to be Miles-and-not-Spider-Man.

**Trust / Safety.** High in domain (the Miles-domain); zero in the Spider-domain, which she initially does not know about. Disclosure pressure unresolved.

**Failure Mode.** Same as every romantic relationship in his file: secret-keeping erodes the foundation faster than the bond can deepen. He has not yet solved this and will not solve it without first solving the prior structural problem of believing he is allowed to be loved as the full person.

**Leverage.** High and exposed. She is a non-combatant tethered to his identity once she learns it; she is a hostage-risk and the subject's threat model around her is under-developed.

---

## 12. THE CLONES (SHIFT, SELIM, MINDSPINNER) — Chosen Family by Refusal-to-Disown

**History.** Ahmed-era clone arc. Genetic-and-memory derivatives running loose with his powers and varying degrees of his ethics — some adjacent to his uncle's instincts rather than his father's.

**Dynamics.** The subject's diagnostic choice here is to *claim* them rather than disclaim them. Shift in particular becomes a kind of younger-brother figure — he houses him, trains him, takes responsibility for his actions. The structural meaning is that the subject converts the externalized shadow-self into family rather than into enemy. This is one of the most psychologically healthy moves in his canon and it costs him substantially in time, attention, and risk.

**Trust / Safety.** Mixed and earned-in-increments. He extends trust ahead of where evidence would warrant, because the alternative is treating them the way the world told him *he* might be treated, and his identity will not permit that.

**Failure Mode.** Over-extension. He is not equipped to be the responsible adult to other quasi-adolescents, and he takes the role on without scaffolding. If a clone betrayed him significantly, the impostor cognition would gain ammunition: *see, you cannot trust your own derivatives, because you cannot trust yourself.*

**Leverage.** Subtle. The clones are an attack-surface for any adversary who wants to make the subject prosecute (or fail to prosecute) someone wearing his face.

---

## 13. THE PROWLER MANTLE (POST-AARON INHERITORS) — Unresolved Adjacency

**History.** The Prowler name does not stay buried. Various success


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*Subject: MORALES, MILES GONZALO. File continues.*

The subject's antagonist and intimate rosters are smaller and more thematically coherent than is typical for a Spider-figure of comparable tenure, and the reason is diagnostic: he does not generate enemies through provocation or temperament; he *inherits* them (from Parker, from his uncle, from his city) or *manufactures* them inadvertently (from his own genome, via the clone arc). His romantic file is similarly structural: every relationship he has had to date breaks along the same fault line — secret-keeping under sympathetic-nervous-system load — and not along the lines of compatibility, attraction, or fidelity. In both columns, what is being mapped is the same person's two failure modes (vanish; discharge) projected outward onto other bodies.

---

## I. RIVALS

Rivalry, for this subject, is a structurally awkward category. He does not maintain rivalries in the conventional adversarial sense; his "rivals" are mostly figures against whom he measures himself and finds himself wanting. The relationships that look most like rivalry from outside read, from inside his cognition, as *legitimacy audits*.

### I.a — PARKER, PETER BENJAMIN (616, adult)

Catalogued in full under Relationships II (Mentors). Cross-listed here because, despite the warmth of the mentorship, the relationship contains a sustained rivalrous *substrate* visible only to the subject. Peter is the standard against which Miles measures every operational outcome: web-fluid efficiency, banter cadence, civilian-evacuation triage speed, J.J. Jameson tolerance. The rivalry is one-sided and asymmetrical — Peter has explicitly disclaimed it (*Spider-Men II* #1–5; multiple Champions/Avengers crossovers) — but Miles cannot accept the disclaimer because accepting it would require granting himself parity, which his impostor structure forbids. **Failure mode:** Miles never argues with Peter; he simply does what Peter says and then second-guesses himself afterward, which periodically results in him *not* deploying his better local instincts because they diverge from the Parker playbook. **Leverage Peter holds:** total. A single sentence of Parker disapproval reliably routes Miles into 24–48 hours of withdrawal. **Leverage Miles holds over Peter:** moral, and increasing. Peter visibly course-corrects toward gentleness around Miles because Miles models it. Neither acknowledges this.

### I.b — DRAKE, JESSICA ("JESSICA DREW" / SPIDER-WOMAN, female-Parker clone, Ultimate)

The first person to physically attack Miles in costume (*USM* #5). Initially reads him as an impostor, fights him, then — recognizing him as a kid — flips to fierce protectiveness. The relationship is the **template** for his entire interaction style with the senior Spider-pantheon: he is hit, judged, then conditionally licensed. He metabolizes this as the *correct* order of operations and replicates it inwardly forever after. **Trust:** high, asymmetric. He defers; she protects. **Failure mode:** she vanishes from his operational sphere when continuities reshuffle, and he never fully replaces the function she served (the elder Spider-woman who *knew Peter* and could verify Miles's claim from Peter's side). **Leverage:** historical. She is the canonical voice in his head that says *you have permission*, and the loss of regular contact with her in the 616 has measurable correlative effect on his impostor cycles.

### I.c — BISHOP, AMERICA (and the broader CHAMPIONS leadership lattice — KAMALA KHAN, SAM ALEXANDER)

Not adversaries but *internal* rivals for moral authority within a peer team. Miles routinely defers to Kamala; reads America's certainty as a thing he lacks; treats Sam's bravado as a foreign tongue. The "rivalry" is internal and one-directional — he measures his temperament against theirs and concludes his own is insufficiently decisive. Notably, when the Champions vote, Miles's vote is the most frequently *moved* by another's argument; he is, by team-dynamic metric, the most persuadable founder. **Failure mode:** in the *Outlawed* arc and adjacent storylines, his persuadability allows the team to drift in directions he privately disagrees with; he does not block consensus and then carries the guilt of outcomes he did not author. **Leverage:** Kamala in particular can route him into operations he is ethically uneasy with simply by framing them as principled. He has not yet developed the muscle to say *no, and here is why*, in a peer setting.

### I.d — SCARLET SPIDER / KAINE; SILK / CINDY MOON; SPIDER-GWEN / GWEN STACY (Web-of-Life cohort)

In the *Spider-Verse* and *Spider-Geddon* arcs, Miles is positioned beside Spider-figures whose origins are more "native" to the Web than his (*Spider-Verse* identifies him as anomaly-adjacent — see "The Other" subplot). He experiences this as a *cosmic* rivalry: the multiverse itself is auditing whether he belongs. With Gwen specifically there is a near-romantic charge that never resolves; she is the only Spider-peer who treats him as *contemporary* rather than *junior*, and his response is visible disorientation. **Failure mode:** he reads metaphysical taxonomies (anomaly, native, prime) as verdicts on his worth. **Leverage:** the Web mythology has structural power over him that no individual hero does, because it speaks in the language his impostor structure already uses.

---

## II. ENEMIES

The enemy file divides cleanly into four tiers: **inherited** (from Parker's rogues), **familial** (Aaron, the Prowler legacy), **corporate-structural** (Roxxon, Oscorp), and **endogenous** (the clones — enemies generated from his own tissue). The fourth tier is the most psychologically loaded; the canon spends increasing time there because it is the only enemy class he cannot defeat by being a better Spider-Man.

### II.a — DAVIS, AARON (THE PROWLER) — deceased Ultimate; alive and reformed 616

**Status:** Primary antagonist of formative period. Functionally the inversion of the Ben Parker template — uncle as corrupter rather than moral north.

**History.** Subject's paternal uncle. Estranged from Jefferson because of his criminal career. The bite event (*USM* #1) occurs in his apartment, via a spider Aaron stole from Oscorp; Aaron's criminality is therefore the *causal substrate* of Miles's powers. This is non-trivial: the abilities Miles uses to be a hero are, in origin chain, *stolen by a thief from a corrupt corporation*. The provenance is morally compromised before he ever puts on the suit, and he knows it.

**Dynamics.** Aaron alternates between affection and instrumentalization. He is warm, charming, attentive — and uses that warmth as a recruitment vector.
