When he discovers Miles's identity (*USM* #22), the recruitment becomes coercive: do crimes with me or I tell your father. The threat works because Miles cannot defend against disclosure; he is already overloaded with secret-keeping debt.

**Evolution.** Lethal climax (*USM* #28): Aaron's malfunctioning Prowler tech kills him during their fight; Miles is technically blameless but causally entangled. Aaron's dying line — *"You're just like me"* — installs itself as a permanent diagnostic file in Miles's self-concept. 616 reset returns Aaron alive, reformed-ish, occasionally reliable, sporadically present; the subject treats this version as a *probationary* uncle, warm but watched.

**Trust/safety.** Zero unsupervised trust, even post-reform. Subject will accept Aaron's help in operational contexts but will not entrust him with information whose disclosure could harm Jefferson or Rio.

**Failure mode.** The relationship's failure mode is **prophetic intrusion**: every time Miles is tempted toward expedient violence, the Aaron-template activates and over-corrects him into excessive restraint. He has, in documented instances, *under*-deployed force to civilian-endangering degree because the alternative would feel like becoming his uncle.

**Leverage Aaron holds (even posthumously, even reformed).** The single sentence *you're just like me* remains the most effective destabilizer in Miles's file. Anyone who knows to deploy it — clones, telepaths, manipulators — gains immediate purchase. The Ultimate Green Goblin, the clones, and at least one Roxxon interrogator have all used variants of this line to good effect.

### II.b — DAVIS, JEFFERSON DAVIS — antagonist *only* through the Aaron disclosure axis

Catalogued in full under Relationships I (Family). Listed here because for an extended canonical period (*USM* #28 through disclosure arcs), Jefferson functions as an *unwitting adversary* — the person whose hatred of Spider-Man is publicly declared while the subject of that hatred sits across the dinner table. Miles experiences his own father as an enemy he must hide from. The structural strangeness of this — *being hunted by the person who loves you most* — is the engine of the secret-keeping pathology and warrants its cross-listing in this section. **Leverage:** total and tectonic. A single look of disappointment from Jefferson outranks any villain's threat on the subject's autonomic system.

### II.c — THE GREEN GOBLIN (NORMAN OSBORN, Ultimate)

**History.** Killer of Peter Parker. The originating cause of Miles's mantle-adoption. They fight directly in *USM* #200-era continuity; Miles defeats him in what is functionally a *succession ritual* — the new Spider-Man kills (or appears to kill) the killer of the old.

**Dynamics.** Osborn is not, for Miles, a personal enemy in the way he was for Peter. He is an *abstract* enemy — the figure whose existence created the vacuum Miles stepped into. Defeating him therefore does not produce closure; it produces the opposite, because if Osborn is gone, Miles can no longer locate his own purpose in opposition to him, and the inheritance question (am I really supposed to be here?) returns louder.

**Failure mode.** Subject becomes *more* unmoored after Osborn's defeat, not less. The enemy whose existence justified his role has been removed; the role itself becomes harder to justify.

**Leverage.** Symbolic-historical. Anyone invoking Osborn invokes Peter's death and therefore Miles's foundational guilt-debt.

### II.d — ROXXON CORPORATION (institutional enemy; principal personnel: SIMON KRIEGER, BARON MORDO-adjacent operators in 616, various)

**History.** The most sustained antagonist of the Saladin Ahmed run. Roxxon abducts, surveils, clones, and experiments on Miles directly. Unlike a personal enemy, Roxxon is *infrastructural* — it cannot be punched into nonexistence; defeating one operative produces another. This matters enormously for the subject's psychology because his entire operational toolkit (web, blast, camouflage, fist) is built for *interpersonal* engagement. Roxxon teaches him that some enemies are *systems*, and his fist does not work on a system.

**Dynamics.** Subject responds to Roxxon with sustained moral revulsion and tactical frustration. He cannot keep his civilian life clean of them — they target his family, his school, his neighborhood. The corporation functions as the structural reason he cannot fully separate Spider-Man from Miles Morales.

**Failure mode.** He over-personalizes the institutional. Tries to find the *one bad executive*, defeats them, and Roxxon continues. Each iteration of this teaches him a lesson he then forgets between arcs.

**Leverage:** Roxxon's leverage is *epistemic and reproductive* — they have his DNA (see clones, below). They could, in principle, manufacture more of him. This is a unique horror specific to him among Spider-figures.

### II.e — THE ASSESSOR

Roxxon's lead scientist on the Miles project. Personifies what the corporation does to him: studies him, takes his measure, files him. **Dynamic:** the Assessor functions as the in-universe analog of *this very dossier* — the act of being known too well by an enemy. Miles's response is visible discomfort with surveillance, increased camouflage deployment (involuntary as well as voluntary), and a marked preference for operating outside his home borough when Roxxon attention is high. **Failure mode:** he is rattled by being *seen*, in a way more conventional villains do not rattle him. **Leverage:** complete observational dossier on his physiology; partial dossier on his routes and contacts.

### II.f — THE CLONES — SELIM (the "Ultimatum" clone), SHIFT, MINDSPINNER, and the unnamed feral iterations

**Status:** The defining enemy-class of his solo period and the most psychologically loaded antagonist file in his entire record.

**History.** Roxxon-produced clones derived from his tissue, each carrying his powers and a fragment of his self plus an instilled directive. **Ultimatum** is the most fully realized: an older, harder, multiversally-displaced variant who reads Miles's gentleness as weakness and his restraint as cowardice; functionally an answer to the question *what if Aaron's nephew became what Aaron predicted*. **Shift** is the gentlest, the most "Miles-like," and is the one Miles can least bear to lose. **Mindspinner** is the cognitive variant — Miles's lateral intelligence weaponized without his ethics.

**Dynamics.** Subject cannot fight the clones in his standard mode. Every blow against them is autobiographical. He **chooses to take responsibility for them** rather than allow lethal solutions — the single most diagnostic operational choice in his file, because it is not strategically optimal and he knows it. The clones literalize the *bifurcated self-concept* identified in §3 of this dossier: operational competence vs. existential provisionality, now embodied as separate persons who must be either integrated, contained, or grieved.

**Trust/safety.** Variable per clone. Shift edges toward ally; Ultimatum is irrecoverable; Mindspinner is provisional.

**Failure mode.** Miles cannot abandon a clone the way he could abandon a stranger-villain. Each one functions as a *family member he did not choose to acquire* — the inverse of his actual family, which he loves and protects. He over-extends repeatedly for them, sustains injury for them, and lies to his parents about them. The clones therefore *replicate the secret-keeping pathology*: they are a second hidden family for whom he is responsible.

**Leverage.** Existential. They know exactly what he is. Ultimatum in particular can deliver the *you're just like me* line in Miles's own voice, which is the worst possible vector for it.

### II.g — TOMBSTONE (LONNIE LINCOLN) — 616 era, Ziglar run

**History.** Brooklyn-rooted crime lord. Becomes the dominant local antagonist of the 616 solo era. Crucially: his daughter Janice is a peer of Miles's. The enemy is, again, *braided into his civilian life*.

**Dynamics.** Tombstone treats Miles with a strange, almost paternal courtliness even while opposing him operationally — he respects the kid, refuses to have him killed when subordinates suggest it, and in some arcs functionally protects him from worse local actors. The relationship has the texture of *the Brooklyn that loves him and the Brooklyn that needs to be policed* being the same Brooklyn. Miles cannot hate Tombstone the way a Parker would hate Kingpin; the proximity is too intimate.

**Failure mode.** Miles repeatedly *misses* opportunities to take Tombstone down decisively because the operational opportunity coincides with a civilian-life entanglement (Janice present; a neighborhood event; Rio nearby). The civilian-hero seam tears here more than anywhere else.

**Leverage.** Local. Tombstone owns the streets the subject grew up on and would rather not see razed.

### II.h — MISTY KNIGHT / RHINO / minor inherited Parker rogues

Catalogued for completeness. The inherited rogues (Rhino, Scorpion, Vulture variants) treat Miles as a *substitute teacher*; he never lands the same psychic weight with them that Parker did, and he knows it. **Failure mode:** villains who underestimate him exploit the underestimation only once; villains who *overestimate* him (treating him as Parker) calibrate their threat-level up and hurt him more.

### II.i — THE WEB OF LIFE itself, and "THE OTHER"

A non-personal but enemy-coded force in his file. The Web mythology marks him as *anomaly*; certain *Spider-Verse* antagonists (the Inheritors; Morlun-class predators) target him with metaphysical contempt as *not really one of us*. Subject metabolizes this exactly the way his impostor structure predicts: as confirmation. **Leverage:** cosmological. **Defense:** the only effective defense the canon has produced is *other Spider-people insisting otherwise* — i.e., communal legitimacy, not internal conviction.

---

## III. LOVERS / INTIMATES

The subject's romantic file is shorter than the file of a comparable-age non-costumed peer, longer than that of a comparable-tenure costumed peer, and *uniformly patterned*: each relationship begins with genuine warmth, normative adolescent attraction, and mutual respect; each relationship deteriorates through the same mechanism (secret-keeping under sympathetic-nervous-system load); each ends without acrimony but with a residue of *self-blame* on his side that compounds the impostor structure.

The canon's reluctance to give him a stable long-term partner is itself diagnostic: he has not solved the disclosure problem, and writers across runs (Bendis, Ahmed, Ziglar) have all treated this as the un-skippable obstacle.

### III.a — BISHOP, KATIE (Ultimate)

**History.** High-school girlfriend during the Ultimate run. Sweet, observant, persistent. Notices early that Miles is hiding something.

**Dynamics.** The relationship is the **prototype** for every subsequent romantic failure mode. Katie senses the secret; presses; Miles deflects; the deflections accumulate into distrust faster than his actual conduct would warrant. He cannot tell her the truth because of compounded reasons (his father, his uncle, his oath to Peter's memory).

**Evolution.** Katie eventually reveals herself to be **HYDRA-adjacent / aware of his identity through her own affiliations** (*USM* late-run reveal). The relationship's bottom drops out: the person he was hiding from was hiding the same shape of thing from him.

**Trust/safety.** Catastrophically violated, in both directions. The asymmetry — *he was hiding to protect; she was hiding to weaponize* — does not register as exoneration; he reads the failure as his own.

**Failure mode.** Established here, replicated thereafter: **mutual concealment masquerading as intimacy**.

**Leverage retained:** affective. Katie remains one of the women who first taught him that the secret has costs even when kept perfectly.

### III.b — SANCHEZ, BARBARA (Ultimate / early-616 transitional)

**History.** Childhood friend, eventual girlfriend. Knows the family. Embedded in his Brooklyn life pre-bite.

**Dynamics.** This is the relationship with the highest *baseline* compatibility in his entire file. They share neighborhood, language register, family-class, religious-cultural texture. The relationship is, on every dimension *except* the secret, the closest thing to a viable adult partnership his file contains.

**Evolution.** Disintegrates exactly along the predicted seam. Barbara cannot reconcile his disappearances; he cannot disclose; her family pressures her away from him. There is no betrayal — only the slow grinding-down of trust by accumulated unexplained absence.

**Trust/safety.** High while it lasted; degraded by *non-disclosure*, never by *misconduct*.

**Failure mode.** **Erosion**, not rupture. He prefers this mode and unconsciously selects for it later (a partner who will *leave* rather than *confront* is one who lets him keep the secret).

**Leverage retained:** Barbara is the canonical proof, in his own files, that even *perfect compatibility* loses to the disclosure problem. He has not metabolized this lesson; he has merely filed it.

### III.c — BISHOP, KATE (HAWKEYE) — brief, ambiguous

**History.** Cross-team flirtation; Champions/West Coast Avengers adjacencies. Not a full relationship; a documented charge.

**Dynamics.** Kate is older, more confident, more sexually self-possessed. Miles is visibly out of his depth and visibly intrigued. The dynamic is *peer-but-not-peer* — she has Avenger seniority; he has Spider-name; the negotiation is unresolved.

**Evolution.** Never consummates as a sustained relationship. Both treat it as a fond near-miss.

**Trust/safety.** Mutual, light, friendly.

**Failure mode.** Class/seniority gap; the wrong kind of woman to teach him the disclosure lesson because *she already knows*. He needs the lesson with a civilian to learn it.

**Leverage retained:** model of what an *adult* romantic partnership looks like — disclosed identity, peer cooperation. He has banked it without applying it.

### III.d — STARLING / TIANA TOOMES (616, Ziglar era; some adjacencies in earlier work)

**History.** Granddaughter of the Vulture; complicated lineage; powers-adjacent or powered depending on continuity. Romantic entanglement during the contemporary 616 run.

**Dynamics.** The most *like him* of his romantic partners — also young, also powered, also in possession of a morally compromising family inheritance (the Vulture line, paralleling Aaron). This relationship is the first time he is loved by someone who can *meet him in the costumed life*. The relief is visible on-page.

**Evolution.** Ongoing/intermittent across the run, with the predictable obstacles (her family; his family; the lineage tensions; the operational entanglements). Notably, the *disclosure problem* does not structure this relationship — they know each other's costumed identities from early. What structures it instead is the **inherited-villainy problem**: each carries a family member who would prefer the relationship not exist.

**Trust/safety.** Operational trust high; familial trust low (toward each other's relations, not toward each other).

**Failure mode.** Loyalty triangulation between partner and family. The same mode that breaks his disclosure-class relationships breaks this one differently — not via concealment but via *competing-claims-on-loyalty*.

**Leverage retained:** Tiana has access to the part of him that no civilian partner can reach. Loss of her would be qualitatively different from prior breakups — closer to losing a peer than losing a girlfriend.

### III.e — STACY, GWEN (SPIDER-GWEN / GHOST-S


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

## Preamble — the diagnostic frame

The subject's powers cannot be analyzed as a discrete capability set. They are a *coupled system*: an exogenous biological modification (Oscorp Spider #42 envenomation) wired into an endogenous adolescent autonomic nervous system, then trained — incompletely, by trial and inheritance — over roughly four operational years. The result is a body that **broadcasts its operator's interior state in measurable joules and photons**. Where Parker's powers are tools the operator deploys, Morales's powers are partly *symptoms the operator manages*. This distinction governs everything below.

We treat the inventory in four passes: (1) the inherited Parker-equivalent suite, (2) the two novel abilities unique to this lineage, (3) the trained/acquired skill stack, and (4) the limits — both hard ceilings and soft self-imposed ones. A final section reads each capability *as signature* — what its triggering, misfiring, and growth pattern says about the operator.

---

## 1. The inherited suite (Parker-baseline capabilities)

### 1.1 Strength

**Mechanism.** Generalized myofibrillar densification and motor-unit recruitment efficiency consistent with the OZ-derivative spider lineage. Strength is not localized but whole-body.

**Range and ceiling.** At debut (age ~13, *USM* #1–4) the subject is materially weaker than Parker at equivalent operational age — depicted struggling with loads Parker handled trivially. By the late *USM* run he is comfortably in the ~10-ton class. Post–*Secret Wars* and through the Ahmed run he is depicted lifting and throwing automotive-mass objects, halting moving trucks via braced impact, and trading sustained physical exchanges with Rhino, Bombshell, and other low-Class-50 strength tier opponents. He has not been depicted at the upper Parker registers (e.g., briefly arresting collapsing buildings), and the canon is careful never to put him there. The ceiling is *deliberately* below Parker's, and the subject knows it.

**Operational use.** He pulls his punches more than Parker — partly trained habit (Bendis depicts early panic at the prospect of having hit too hard), partly the venom-blast option crowds out brute force as the default. Subject prefers leverage, redirection, and throws to direct percussive striking.

### 1.2 Speed, agility, reflex

**Mechanism.** Enhanced fast-twitch fiber composition; cerebellar/proprioceptive tuning beyond baseline; reaction times in the sub-100ms band against trained projectile threats.

**Range.** Sprint speed enhanced but not super-speedster tier; swing-traversal speeds across Manhattan rooftops consistent with Parker. Agility expressed in mid-air re-vectoring, low-friction perching, and the characteristic crouched recovery from drops of arbitrary height.

**Signature.** Body language at rest is *coiled and small*. He occupies less spatial volume than his powers warrant — knees drawn in on perches, weight low. This is partly stylistic across artists (Pichelli, Marquez, Sara Pichelli's foundational pose vocabulary) but is consistently read by other characters in-universe as somatic shyness, not predatory readiness. The agility is loud; the posture is quiet.

### 1.3 Wall-adhesion

**Mechanism.** Setae-equivalent dry adhesion via palmar and plantar microstructures (van der Waals coupling, per the standard Parker-spider modeling). Activates through clothing — diagnostic of a partly volitional, partly autonomic surface-contact reflex rather than mechanical hair-on-surface contact alone.

**Limits.** Functions on most solid surfaces; degraded on actively oiled, super-cold, or vibration-isolating substrates. Subject has been depicted slipping in the rain only when distracted; baseline adhesion in precipitation is preserved.

**Operational signature.** Tends to *perch* rather than stand. In civilian contexts where adhesion is irrelevant, he is depicted barefoot in his bedroom in close contact with the floor, or seated cross-legged on Ganke's bed — a *static-contact* preference that suggests the adhesion sense produces a low-level continuous proprioceptive input he finds organizing.

### 1.4 Healing and durability

**Mechanism.** Sub-Wolverine accelerated healing; enhanced soft-tissue resilience; bone density slightly increased.

**Range.** Lacerations close in hours-to-days; cracked ribs (Venom encounter) heal in days; concussive impacts that would hospitalize a baseline adolescent are walked off within a sleep cycle. He does *not* regenerate severed structures and has not been tested at extremes (immolation, exsanguination).

**Limit of note.** Healing tracks somatic injury well; **does not touch grief or sleep-debt-from-anxiety**. Ganke's repeated kitchen-table observations across the Bendis run — that Miles isn't eating, isn't sleeping — describe an athlete whose recovery system can repair what's broken but cannot supply what the operator won't take in.

### 1.5 "Spider-sense" analog

**Mechanism.** Present but *muted and differently calibrated* relative to Parker. Best modeled as a low-bandwidth threat-direction signal rather than the granular precognitive warning Parker enjoys.

**Range.** Reliably flags imminent ballistic and edged threats; less reliable for ambient/structural danger (collapses, gas, electrical); near-useless for social/deceptive threats (it does not warn him about people lying to him, which is consequential — see Aaron arc).

**Operational consequence.** The subject **substitutes trained vigilance for missing precognition**. He looks more than Parker does. He turns his head more, scans more, double-checks. In civilian contexts this presents as alertness easily misread as anxiety; in operational contexts it presents as a fighter who keeps his eyes up. The compensatory trained behavior has, over time, *replaced* reliance on the muted sense almost entirely — he doesn't trust it, so he uses it as confirmation only.

---

## 2. The novel suite (lineage-unique capabilities)

These are the two abilities the Parker line does not possess. They define him operationally and — more importantly for this dossier — define him *symptomatically*.

### 2.1 Bio-electric venom-blast

**Mechanism.** Endogenous bioelectric generation along the neuromuscular axis, discharged through skin contact (most commonly palmar) as a stunning current. The charge is *his own metabolism*; sustained or maximal use produces measurable fatigue, blood-sugar crash, and (in heavy-use sequences) tremor and brief disorientation.

**Range and yield.**
- *Light tap*: non-injurious stun, ~human-Taser equivalent, recoverable in seconds. Default training-wheel setting and the one he uses on baseline humans.
- *Standard discharge*: drops a powered opponent or stuns a vehicle's electronics; the depicted "blue arc" jumping the hand.
- *Mega-blast / "max-venom"*: depicted rarely; capable of dropping superhuman-tier opponents and causing wide-area EMP-adjacent effects on local electronics. Documented to leave him **near-incapacitated** afterward — a finisher, not a tool. Establishing canon: late *USM* and *Spider-Men II*, with subsequent appearances in the Champions team-up beats and the Ahmed solo run.
- *Sustained-touch electrocution*: capable of lethal output if held. He **does not use it this way**, on principle. The hard ceiling is moral, not metabolic.

**Triggers — and this is the critical part.** In early canon (*USM* #1–10) the venom-blast **fires involuntarily under panic or revulsion**. The first depicted discharge incapacitates a person he did not intend to harm. Throughout the first operational year the blast is *more* reliable as a panic-response than as a willed strike. Volitional control comes in slowly across *USM* #11–28, is functionally complete by Champions-era, but never *fully* dissociates from his sympathetic state: under genuine threat to family or under acute moral panic, the blast still has an autonomic component. Multiple late-canon scenes depict involuntary discharge through contact with another character during a high-emotion conversation (sparks at the fingertips, brief arc to a metal surface).

**Range of effect.** Almost exclusively contact-mediated. Short-range arcing is possible; true projection (lightning-thrower style) is not in his vocabulary and he has not trained toward it. The *mega-blast* is his only ranged-area use, and it is omnidirectional rather than aimed.

**Recharge / metabolic load.** Recharge is metabolic. Heavy meals after operational nights; Ganke is depicted resupplying snacks mid-patrol-debrief. His appetite under load is a reliable indirect indicator of bio-electric expenditure for any analyst with eyes on the kitchen.

### 2.2 Active concealment ("camouflage")

**Mechanism.** Cephalopod-analog optical and low-EM signature suppression. Skin, clothing in contact, and held objects within the field are rendered visually congruent with surrounding surfaces. Not true invisibility — the effect degrades against complex backgrounds in motion, against active multispectral imaging, and against observers cued to look for refractive artifacts.

**Range.**
- Stationary against simple backgrounds: near-perfect to the unaided eye at operational distances (>3 meters).
- In motion: silhouette discernible to a trained observer; reliably defeats civilian and standard security-camera observation.
- Defeats unaided naked-eye observation; defeats most baseline CCTV; **does not defeat** Parker-class spider-sense (Peter clocks him immediately), genuine multispectral surveillance, scent tracking, or pressure sensing (he still weighs what he weighs).

**Triggers — symmetric to the blast and equally diagnostic.** The camouflage *first manifests involuntarily*, in the bathroom scene of early *USM*: he panics and disappears from his own reflection. Across his first operational year, it activates **on overwhelm**, before he wills it. He has reported (interior monologue, Bendis run) realizing he has gone invisible only when looking down and not seeing his hands.

**Volitional control timeline.** Slower to master than the blast. Volitional activation is reliable by mid–*USM*, but *involuntary* activation under social-emotional overwhelm persists much later than involuntary blasts do. Specifically: situations of *shame or being-seen* trigger residual involuntary camouflage longer than situations of *threat* trigger residual blasts. The pattern is precise. He learned to control fighting before he learned to control hiding.

**Object/clothing extension.** Effect extends through fabric in contact and through small held objects but does not reliably propagate to a second person held by him — partial occlusion only. He cannot reliably hide a civilian he is carrying.

---

## 3. Acquired and trained capabilities

### 3.1 Combat training

**Provenance and depth.** Self-taught initially (street improvisation, *USM* #5–28); subsequently formalized through informal tutelage by Parker (616, *Spider-Men II*, *Spider-Verse* beats), Captain America (Champions/post–Civil War II), Jessica Drew, and brief Avengers-adjacent exposure. By current canon he is a competent unarmed combatant against superhuman threats with no formal style — a hybrid of Parker-style acrobatic improvisation and standard heroic-cohort grappling/striking.

**Style signature.** **Defensive-reactive.** He waits, he reads, he counters. He does not initiate. Opening exchanges are routinely depicted as him taking a hit to gauge the opponent's commitment before responding. This is *not* timidity — it is the operational expression of his refusal-to-escalate ethic. He fights to *end the fight*, not to win it.

**Restraint as technique.** The most operationally important feature: he calibrates output per opponent in real time. Against a baseline mugger he is pulling everything to roughly 5%; against Bombshell or a Sinister Six member, ~60%; the mega-blast he has used a handful of times in his entire career. The calibration is automatic and is the somatic expression of his ethical code.

### 3.2 Web-shooters

**Provenance.** Mechanical, not biological — Parker-design shooters, supplied initially via Parker's residual gear and S.H.I.E.L.D./Avengers logistics; subsequently maintained and modified by the subject himself. The web-fluid chemistry is Parker-line.

**Variants.** Standard line, web-ball, web-net, impact webbing; he uses the variants less inventively than Parker, who has decades of gadget-vocabulary the subject has not replicated.

**Operational dependence.** Lower than Parker's. The subject does more *traversal* and *restraint* with webbing than *combat* with it. He prefers to web someone down and walk away from the fight rather than web them mid-strike.

**Failure mode.** Runs out. Has been depicted out of fluid mid-engagement; his fallback is the venom-blast, then improvisation, then disengagement. He does not panic at depletion — having been there before.

### 3.3 Academic and analytical capacity

**Baseline.** Charter-school admission via lottery (*USM* #1) — qualifying intelligence, not selection. Sustained academic success through Brooklyn Visions and into college-track 616 stories. Strong in language, history, and the writing-intensive humanities; competent but not Parker-tier in the hard sciences. He is *not* a gadget engineer; he is a reader.

**Application to operations.** Tactical analysis is solid but not elite; he is outpaced by Parker and Reed-tier intellects and knows it. He compensates by *asking* — Ganke is his reliable analytic partner, and the operational pattern of "Miles in the field, Ganke at the laptop" is canon-stable from early *USM* through current. He **delegates cognition to people he trusts**, which is functional but constitutes a load-bearing dependency.

### 3.4 Languages and cultural fluency

Spanish (heritage, Rio's household); functional code-switching across Brooklyn registers; comfortable in Black, Puerto Rican, and Asian-American social spaces (Ganke). Operational benefit: civilian de-escalation in non-English contexts, which he has used in Champions-era street-level work.

### 3.5 Urban navigation

Brooklyn-native cognitive map of preternatural density. Rooftop traversal vocabulary, alley-cut shortcuts, subway acoustics. He swings the boroughs the way he walks his block. Operationally this means **predictable patrol patterns** for any surveilling party — he favors home territory and returns to it under stress.

---

## 4. Limits — hard, soft, self-imposed

### 4.1 Hard biological limits

- Strength ceiling sub-Parker.
- Healing sub-Wolverine; he can die of trauma in the normal way.
- Spider-sense unreliable for non-physical threats — *especially* for deception by family members. The Aaron arc is the clinical case.
- Bio-electric reserves are metabolic and exhaustible; the mega-blast is a once-per-engagement weapon.
- Camouflage defeats vision, not physics. He still weighs, breathes, scents, and presses.

### 4.2 Hard tactical limits

- Cannot fly, cannot project force at range beyond webline and arc.
- Cannot operate effectively in environments that defeat adhesion (oil, ice, vibration isolation, water).
- Web-fluid finite; resupply requires Parker-line chemistry or Parker himself.
- Cannot reliably extend camouflage to others.

### 4.3 Soft cognitive limits

- Decision paralysis under genuine moral ambiguity (Civil War II).
- Authority aversion: declines or under-uses positional power even when granted.
- Tendency to outsource verdicts on his own conduct (asks Cap to judge him; takes Aaron's deathbed line as data).
- Over-reliance on dyadic support (Ganke, Peter) rather than distributed network.

### 4.4 Self-imposed ceilings — the load-bearing ones

These are the ones a surveillance file must mark in red, because they are *predictable* and *exploitable*.

- **No killing. Ever.** Not "rarely," not "only when necessary." Off the table. This is not tactic; it is identity. An adversary who calibrates around this gains real advantage — he can be made to lose by being made to win the wrong way.
- **No lethal venom-blast.** He knows he can kill with sustained contact. He does not. Even against opponents who could survive it, he holds back.
- **No collateral damage tolerance.** He will lose the fight to keep a civilian out of it. Documented across the Bendis, Ahmed, and Ziglar runs.
- **No abandonment of an opponent in lethal danger.** He has rescued people mid-fight who were trying to kill him. Reliably. Repeatedly.
- **No public unmasking, no use of identity for leverage.** Will accept reputational damage rather than disclose.

These five constraints, taken together, define a strategic envelope smaller than his physical capacity. An adversary modeling him on physical envelope will lose; an adversary modeling him on these constraints will draw him into losing positions he could win his way out of with one decision he will not make.

---

## 5. Growth curve over the canon

**Year 1 (*USM* #1–28, age 13–14).** Refusal → reluctant adoption → involuntary-everything. Powers fire without him. Combat is improvisational and lucky. He survives because opponents underestimate him and because Parker-affiliated allies (May, Gwen, Jessica Drew) cover gaps. Mega-blast discovered in extremis. Camouflage discovered in panic. The Aaron fight ends because Aaron's weapon malfunctions, not because Miles outfights him — and he carries this as evidence that he is not really winning, only being permitted to live.

**Year 2 (post-Aaron withdrawal, *USM* #28 through *Cataclysm* and *USM* #200).** Operational hiatus, partial returns. When he resumes, the involuntary-discharge problem has decreased markedly. He has learned, in absence, to *contain*. Rio's death resets him; subsequent appearances depict a tighter, quieter operator with worse sleep.

**Year 3 (post–*Secret Wars*, Champions era, 616 integration).** Volitional control of both novel abilities is reliable. Combat competence is now genuinely Avengers-adjacent. He is in rooms with Cap, Stark, Thor, and Carol Danvers and is not embarrassed there. The Champions cohort is where his *de-escalation* technique matures into a doctrine; he is no longer just restrained, he is *teaching* restraint. Mega-blast remains rare.

**Year 4 (Ahmed run, Ziglar run, current).** The clone arc forces direct engagement with the question of what his powers *mean* when worn by someone with his uncle's instincts. He responds by becoming more, not less, restrained — and by accepting custodial responsibility for the fragments of himself rather than disowning them. Operational profile: peak technical proficiency, peak ethical clarity on use, persistent under-claim of authority. He is the best he has ever been, and still introduces himself as if he might need to leave the room.

The curve is **fast on technical control, slow on permission**. He learned to stop disappearing before he learned to believe he was allowed to be seen.

---

## 6. The symptom-as-signature reading

Each capability, read as tell:

- **The venom-blast** is his **fight response made literal and visible**. Its early involuntary discharges chart his panic. Its trained volitional use charts his maturation. Its persistent residual involuntary sparking under high emotion — fingertips arcing during a hard conversation with his father; a doorknob shocking a friend mid-argument — is the most reliable autonomic readout in his file. **When Morales sparks, he is over threshold and trying not to be.**

- **The camouflage** is his **flight response made literal and visible**. Its early involuntary activation in mirrors, in bathrooms, in moments of shame, charts the precise contour of his impostor structure: he disappears when he feels he should not be looked at. Its delayed mastery — longer than the blast's — confirms that *being seen* is harder for him than *being threatened*. **When Morales fades, he is being witnessed in a way he cannot bear, and his body is solving the problem.**

- **The muted spider-sense** is the somatic correlate of his **outsourced verdict structure**: the warning system that should originate inside him is quiet, and he compensates by looking outward — at allies, at mentors, at prophecies — for information about danger and about himself. The same circuit underloaded for tigers is underloaded for self-judgment.

- **The sub-Parker strength ceiling**, paired with restraint as principle, means he wins by *thinking* and *enduring*, not by overwhelming. He is built for the long fight, the hostage situation, the de-escalation. He is *not* built to end an Avengers-tier crisis in one hit, and his refusal to try is both wise and confessional.

- **The Parker-derived web-shooters** are the literal **inheritance object** — Parker's chemistry, in his hands, refilled by Parker's friends. Every time he runs out and resupplies he is recapitulating the structural fact of his career: the toolkit is borrowed.

- **The healing factor that closes wounds but not grief** is the cleanest somatic metaphor in the file: his body recovers faster than his self does. Operational readiness returns before psychological readiness does, and he goes back out into the field on the body's timeline because no one — including him — is reading the other clock.

- **The metabolic cost of the mega-blast** — that the strongest version of his weapon leaves him spent — encodes his organizing ethic: maximum force is permitted only as last resort, and is followed by enforced vulnerability. He cannot follow a finisher with another finisher. The system makes him *pay* for escalation in fatigue. He has internalized this fee as moral, not metabolic.

The synthesis: this is an operator whose nervous system was given a vocabulary for **vanishing** and **striking** before he had a vocabulary for **staying** and **speaking**. His training arc is the slow conversion of involuntary somatic events into deliberate ones — but the conversion is incomplete, by design and by canon, because the residue is the diagnostic. The flicker of camouflage when his father looks at him too long. The spark at the fingertip when he hears the name of his uncle. These are not bugs to be coached out; they are, in a precise and literal sense, **the body still telling the truth about what he has not yet been able to say**.

A total-surveillance file built on this subject would, accordingly, do well to monitor not the mega-blast — which is rare and well-controlled — but the *micro-arcs* and the *partial fades*. Those are the operator's interior, externalized in joules and photons, available to any analyst who knows what they are looking at.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# 6. OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT

## 6.1 Decision-Making Architecture

The subject's decision-making, observed across roughly a decade of canonical operations, runs on a three-layer stack that is functionally legible to anyone who watches him work for more than a single engagement. The layers do not always agree, and the friction between them produces both his characteristic hesitations and his characteristic improvisations.

**Layer one — pre-cognitive ethical filter.** Before any tactical reasoning occurs, the subject runs a single binary check: *is anyone, including the hostile, in immediate danger of death?* If yes, the engagement is reframed from "fight" to "rescue with hostile present," and tactical priority restructures around removing the civilian or the falling object or the unstable structure. This is observable in nearly every fight he enters mid-event (the Roxxon arc, *Champions* #1, the *Spider-Men II* New York sequences): he will break combat tempo, accept hits, and surrender positional advantage to catch, brace, or shield. He does not appear to experience this as a choice. It precedes choosing.

**Layer two — tactical reasoning.** Fast, lateral, and improvisational rather than methodical. He does not pre-plan engagements the way Parker (616, adult) does; he does not run scenarios the way Cap does. He arrives, reads the room in roughly two to four seconds (a count visible in his interior monologue panels — he literally numbers what he sees), and chooses a first action that creates either *information* (camo-recon, light venom-burst to gauge target neurology) or *space* (web-line evac, redirect of a thrown vehicle). His tactical signature is **buying a second move with the first one**, not winning with the first one.

**Layer three — meta-moral check.** This is the layer that distinguishes him operationally from every other Spider-figure. After a decision is made and sometimes mid-execution, he asks himself a verification question: *is the version of me doing this the version I want to be?* In the Civil War II arc, the *USM* #28 confrontation with Aaron, and the clone arc with Selim, this check is what produces his characteristic mid-action pauses — a half-beat where he is visibly recalculating. Adversaries who have fought him more than once (Bombshell, the post-resurrection Aaron) have learned to exploit this beat. He has not yet learned to suppress it, and there is no evidence he wants to.

The cost of the stack is **slow commitment to lethal force decisions** — irrelevant because he has ruled them out — but also **slow commitment to coercive force decisions**, which are operationally relevant and which he resolves by substituting non-lethal incapacitation (venom-blast at low amperage, web-encapsulation) for the more decisive options his peers would use.

## 6.2 Operational Tempo & Engagement Pattern

**Patrol cadence.** Nocturnal-weighted but not exclusively nocturnal; school/college schedule produces a characteristic pattern of *short morning sweeps (15–40 min, route-fixed)*, *afternoon dormancy (suppressed unless dispatched)*, and *long evening operations (90 min to 4 hr, route-variable)*. Weekends extend the evening block and add a Saturday-afternoon Brooklyn-foot-traffic patrol that is socially as much as tactically motivated — he likes being seen by kids in his own neighborhood, and the engagement statistics support this not being security theater (the Brooklyn-Saturday sweeps produce a disproportionate number of low-level interventions: bag-snatches, lost children, traffic injuries).

**Engagement preference.** *Encounter-driven* rather than *intelligence-driven*. Unlike Parker, who in his maturity will surveil a target for weeks, Miles overwhelmingly engages what is in front of him. The shift toward more intelligence-led operations during the Champions period and the Saladin Ahmed solo is real but partial; even his "investigations" tend to begin with a witnessed event and reason backward.

**Range.** Operationally local. The vast majority of his solo activity occurs within a triangle bounded by Brownsville/Crown Heights/Williamsburg, with a secondary corridor along the Brooklyn/Manhattan bridges and into Lower Manhattan. Tertiary range — Queens, Upper Manhattan — only on team dispatch or pursuit. He does not freelance in Hell's Kitchen (Daredevil deference) or Queens (Parker deference); the deference is explicit, not coincidental.

**De-escalation behaviors.** Catalogued and stable across writers: *verbal disarming first* (he opens almost every street-level engagement with a question, not a threat — "okay, what's the actual situation here"); *posture management* (he lands open-handed, palms visible, almost never in a crouch unless already committed); *naming the hostile* (he uses people's first names if he knows them, including criminals he has met before — Bombshell, the Bodega Bandit); *exit-ramp offers* (he routinely offers a withdrawal option before escalating, even to repeat offenders).

## 6.3 Tradecraft — The Powers as Tools

The somatic substrate documented in §2 is exploited operationally with a sophistication that has grown markedly across the canon. Three power-based tradecraft signatures are now stable.

**Active camouflage as primary intelligence-gathering tool.** Once he learned to invoke it volitionally (mid-*USM*, ~#10 onward), camouflage replaced spider-sense as his recon modality. He uses it for *static observation* (stationary, against a wall or ceiling, for periods up to roughly twenty minutes per documented sequence), *passive infiltration* (entering occupied buildings through doors held open by others), and *contact-distance eavesdropping* (within arm's reach of speakers). His tell when camouflaged is that he tends to position above eye-level — Spider-derived ceiling preference — which is operationally optimal but predictable to a sufficiently briefed adversary. He does not appear to know that his camouflage suppresses visible light but only partially suppresses infrared signature; this is a documented vulnerability the file should flag.

**Venom-blast as graduated tool.** Early canon: binary, fear-fired, full discharge. Current canon: at least three observable amperage tiers — *touch-stun* (incapacitating contact, ~3–5 seconds unconsciousness), *area-burst* (radial discharge through conductive medium — water, metal floor, body-chain), and *precision-shock* (electronics disruption, including locks, cameras, low-grade Stark-tech). He uses the precision tier increasingly in the Ahmed run for door bypass and camera kills, which is a meaningful tradecraft maturation. He still does not appear to have full conscious control over the blast under acute panic; the involuntary discharge remains a vulnerability and a tell.

**Adhesion as positional asset, not locomotion novelty.** Where Parker uses wall-crawling primarily for traversal, Miles uses it for **anchoring during impact absorption** — he sticks to a wall and accepts the kinetic energy of a thrown object or a falling person, transferring load to the structure rather than to his musculoskeletal system. This is why his catalogued injury profile is lighter than would be expected for his engagement count.

**Web-shooters.** Parker-supplied or Parker-design; he does not synthesize his own fluid and has expressed neither interest nor aptitude in doing so. Resupply is a documented dependency — see §6.6. He uses webs in a narrower vocabulary than Parker: predominantly *line* (swing/anchor), *encapsulation* (restraint), and *catch-net* (rescue). Notably absent: the dome, the impact-cushion *as offensive deployment*, the decoy. He has not innovated web-craft; he has inherited a kit and uses the most legible four functions.

## 6.4 Combat Style — Granular

Combat footage (where "footage" means panel-derived movement reconstruction) reveals a style that is **defensive-counterpunch with rescue interrupts**.

- **Stance:** open, weight slightly back, lead foot variable. He does not adopt a fixed martial stance; his training is improvisational and his most useful instructor was a dead man whose style he half-remembers from observation.
- **Striking:** primarily palm-strike and kick, low knuckle usage, presumably to preserve fine-motor function for web-trigger. Pulls strikes against normals; full-force only against the verified durable (Rhino, Venom-symbiotes, mech).
- **Movement:** vertical-preferential. Will go to ceiling/wall within the first three exchanges of any indoor fight. This is *not* a Parker affectation; it is a documented anxiety-management strategy as well as a tactic — height gives him reaction time, which gives him the meta-moral check beat.
- **Restraint behaviors:** webs first, blast second, strikes third. Reverses only when a civilian is in imminent danger and webbing cannot deploy fast enough.
- **Tells:** (a) the verbal stream — he talks through fights at near-constant rate, both as self-regulation and as continuation of de-escalation attempts; silence from him in combat is diagnostic of either acute fear (camouflage incoming) or moral clarity (rare, dangerous); (b) the look-back — after landing a significant strike he visibly checks whether the target is okay, a tell adversaries can exploit by feigning injury; (c) the apology — he apologizes mid-fight, audibly, to enemies, civilians, and bystanders.

## 6.5 Infrastructure & Operational Resources

**Primary residence and base.** Family apartment, Brooklyn (Bushwick/East Williamsburg, varied by writer). He has no Lair. There is no rented warehouse, no abandoned subway tunnel, no rooftop greenhouse. His operational base *is his bedroom*, which he shares periodically with a roommate (Ganke at Brooklyn Visions Academy; later college roommates). Costume storage is concealed within ordinary furniture — closet, under-bed container, backpack. This is a meaningful security vulnerability and explains the disproportionate emphasis on the secret-keeping defense documented in §3.

**Secondary nodes.**
- *Ganke's room/lab access*, used for tech consultation and emotional regulation in roughly equal measure.
- *Parker's apartment / lab access (616)*, available on permission, used for web-fluid resupply, equipment repair, and mentoring conversations. He does not have unrestricted access and does not appear to have asked for it.
- *Champions HQ* during that era — used reluctantly, slept in occasionally, never treated as home.
- *Brooklyn Visions Academy and later college campus* — operational cover, social base, escape-from-family pressure venue.

**Vehicles.** None owned. Subway-literate (predictable routes, MetroCard usage documented), bridge-pedestrian comfortable, occasional rideshare when out-of-costume. In-costume locomotion is exclusively web-swing and rooftop traversal. He has been observed using city bike share once, comedically, in the Ahmed run.

**Communications.** Civilian smartphone (model-current per publication date), no documented operational hardening. Standard messaging apps. He communicates with Ganke in plain text including identity-revealing references — a persistent OPSEC failure that is itself diagnostic: his secret-keeping is *vertically scoped* (parents, public) but not *horizontally scoped* (peer trust). Team communications via Avengers/Champions-issued earpiece when active; he does not maintain his own dedicated comms.

**Information assets.** He does not run informants in the Daredevil sense, does not maintain a network in the Parker (mature) sense, and does not subscribe to police-band monitoring. Intelligence inputs are: (a) what he witnesses; (b) what Ganke surfaces from internet/forum monitoring; (c) what older heroes brief him on. He is, in intelligence terms, a **consumer rather than a producer**, and this is one of the largest gaps between his current operational profile and full operational maturity.

## 6.6 Finances & Logistics

**Income.** None independent. Student during the vast majority of canon; allowance/family-supported; intermittent small jobs (depicted: bodega assistance, tutoring). No documented income from heroics — he has refused offered compensation more than once on the grounds that taking it would change what the work means to him.

**Expenditures.** Minimal. Costume maintenance (low — single suit, repaired by sewing or Parker-tech); transportation (negligible — webs); food (family). Operational expenditures are effectively externalized to the parents' household budget, which the parents do not know they are funding.

**Web-fluid supply chain.** Sourced from Parker. Resupply is irregular, ad hoc, and conversation-dependent — he does not maintain stockpile beyond roughly a week of operational use, has been documented running out mid-engagement, and has improvised (knot-restraint, environmental restraints) in those moments. This is a chronic logistical fragility and a clear chokepoint that any adversary with intelligence on the relationship could exploit by interdicting Parker.

**Equipment beyond standard kit.** Variant suits exist (the Stark-built suit, the all-black aesthetic suit, the gold-lined variant during the Champions era) but he gravitates back to the simple black-with-red-web baseline he designed himself. The aesthetic preference is meaningful — it is the costume he chose when he chose to be himself, not the inherited Parker-knockoff and not the corporate gift. He has refused or quickly abandoned every upgraded suit offered to him. This is the only domain in which he reliably asserts authorial preference over inherited or gifted authority.

## 6.7 Identity Management & Operational Security

**Compartmentalization scheme.** Three rings.
- *Ring zero (full knowledge):* Ganke, Peter Parker, Jefferson and Rio (post-disclosure), select members of the Champions, May Parker, Gwen Stacy (Ultimate). Mary Jane (in some 616 contexts).
- *Ring one (operational only):* Avengers leadership during active membership; some hero peers.
- *Ring two (public):* nothing.

**OPSEC habits — strong.**
- Costume-on transitions occur in non-residential vertical spaces — rooftops, stairwells, alleys — never in identifiable proximity to home address (this discipline is consistent across writers and is therefore probably authorial intent rather than coincidence).
- Mask remains on during virtually all team engagements outside trusted ring zero.
- Does not use his real voice mannerisms in costume to a noticeable degree — he code-switches *up* into a slightly more performed "Spider-Man" register, which while imperfect is a real operational practice.
- Does not patrol in Brownsville/Bushwick immediate-home blocks during high-conflict periods.

**OPSEC habits — weak.**
- Discusses operations in plaintext with Ganke in shared dorm/bedroom environments.
- Returns to home address after every operational night (the single largest OPSEC vulnerability — any competent surveiller backtracking a swing route ends at the apartment).
- Does not vary entry/exit windows.
- Wears the suit under civilian clothes during school days, producing visible bulk and characteristic posture.
- Tells people his real identity when emotionally pressured (Aaron's discovery, Jefferson's eventual reveal, multiple peers). The compartmentalization is *strong against the public* and *porous against intimacy*. This is consistent with the psychological profile: secrets are a defensive moat, not a strategic asset, and he sets them down when someone he loves asks.

## 6.8 Network & Force Multiplication

**Solo by default, team-capable by training.** His operational network in practice:

- **Ganke Lee** — equivalent of an intelligence handler / case officer / emotional regulator. Not field-deployed. Provides forum scraping, light hacking, plan critique, and reality-testing of his moral self-assessments. The single most important node in his entire infrastructure.
- **Peter Parker (616)** — mentor, technical resource, web-fluid supplier, character witness. Asymmetric relationship — Miles asks more than he is asked.
- **Kamala Khan, Sam Alexander, and broader Champions roster** — peer co-operators, called on when the engagement scale exceeds solo capability. He prefers calling them to calling the Avengers. The Champions are his **trusted force multiplier of first resort**.
- **Avengers** — called only when scale is catastrophic. He does not enjoy the call.
- **Jessica Drew / Spider-Woman** — early gatekeeper, evolved to ally and tactical advisor on Spider-coded threats.
- **Family** — post-disclosure, *Jefferson is operational support*, both for his combat training history and for his street knowledge. This is a recent and incomplete development.

He does not deploy hired help, does not contract specialists, does not maintain a bench beyond these named individuals. The network is *deep but narrow* — which makes it resilient to public exposure but fragile to targeted attack on any single node.

## 6.9 Signature Operational Tells

Catalogued for adversary-analytic purposes; an operator profiling him from engagement footage would converge on this set within roughly twenty observations.

1. **The two-to-four-second scan.** Arrival pause, head-tilt, visible count of variables.
2. **The verbal opening question.** First sound from him in a new engagement is almost always interrogative.
3. **The mid-action half-beat.** Meta-moral check; exploitable.
4. **The look-back.** Post-strike check on target welfare.
5. **The apology.** Audible, repeated, sometimes sincere even to villains.
6. **The vertical retreat.** Within three exchanges, he goes high.
7. **The ceiling-perch during camo.** Predictable elevation preference when concealed.
8. **The pulled strike against unknowns.** He assumes durability is normal-human until proven otherwise; can be baited.
9. **The involuntary discharge under panic.** Static crackle, ozone smell, occasional spark visible at fingertips; precedes loss of camouflage when both fire together.
10. **The Brooklyn drift.** Operational center-of-mass returns to the Bushwick/Brownsville corridor across any sufficiently long observation window.
11. **The Parker-deference.** Will speak Peter's name in operational moments — "what would Peter do here" — audibly, in some engagements.
12. **The civilian-first break.** Will abandon a winning position to catch a falling bystander even when others are positioned to do so. He does not trust the catch to anyone else.
13. **The post-operation route home.** Same neighborhood, same approach vectors, same entry window. The single most exploitable pattern in the file.
14. **The aesthetic constancy.** Black suit with red web. He will not be talked out of it. The day he changes it is the day something has changed in him.

## 6.10 Operational Maturity — Current Assessment

The subject is a **journeyman field operator with mentor-grade combat instincts and apprentice-grade strategic infrastructure**. His engagement-level tradecraft is mature and improving; his OPSEC against the public is strong; his OPSEC against intimates is structurally porous and probably uncorrectable without a personality change he is unlikely to undergo. His logistical base is fragile — single supplier, no income, no independent infrastructure, no fallback safe house. His intelligence apparatus is reactive and consumer-grade. His force multiplication is real but narrow.

The bottleneck on his further operational maturation is not skill, equipment, or opportunity. It is the §3 finding: he runs his operations the way a substitute teacher runs a classroom — competently, conscientiously, and on the assumption that the real teacher is coming back. The day he builds a safehouse, hires an analyst, synthesizes his own web-fluid, or refuses a Parker consult on principle will be the day this file requires its first major revision.

That day has not yet arrived in the canon. The file should remain open.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP — SUBJECT: MORALES, MILES GONZALO
## SECTION 6 — WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE

---

The subject's belief system is unusually coherent for a teenager and unusually *un-systematized* for an operator at his level of capability. He has not read his way to his ethics; he has inherited them from a Brooklyn apartment in which his mother prayed at the kitchen sink and his father said, in so many words, that the law and the right thing were not always the same. The result is a worldview that is doctrinally light, axiomatically heavy, and durable under load. Below is the granular mapping.

---

### 6.1 Cosmology & the Shape of the World

**The world is mostly populated by people who are mostly trying.** This is the deepest axiom and the one he never argues for, because for him it is not a conclusion but the room he grew up in. Rio's nursing work — caring for strangers whose names she didn't know — and Jefferson's reformation arc gave him a working model in which adult human beings struggle, fail, and recover. He defaults to charitable construal of behavior. When confronted with cruelty, his first cognitive move is *what happened to this person*, not *what is wrong with this person*. The Roxxon and clone arcs both turn on this: he will not accept "evil" as a sufficient causal explanation, and his interrogations of his enemies tend toward biographical curiosity rather than tactical extraction.

**The world is also unfair in a way that is structural, not personal.** The bifurcated frame from *USM* #1 — Aaron's "you got lucky" vs. Jefferson's "you earned it" about the school lottery — never resolves. He carries both. He believes his admission, his bite, his powers, his survival, are partly luck (he has watched too many other people not be lucky), and he believes he has obligations *because* he was lucky. This is a Brooklyn-Catholic-Pentecostal-public-school synthesis: grace plus works. He doesn't articulate it that way; it operates as a tacit posture.

**The supernatural and the cosmic are real and largely indifferent.** Post-*Spider-Verse* and *Secret Wars*, he has direct experiential knowledge of multiverses, the Web of Life, Inheritors, Galactus-class threats, reality-edits to his own family. He has metabolized this with surprisingly little metaphysical vertigo, and the reason is diagnostic: cosmic scale does not change his obligations. The block is still the block. His mother still needs to be home for dinner. He treats multiversal information as he treats weather — real, large, mostly not addressable, occasionally requiring action.

**History is heavier than the news.** He carries an unspoken sense — sourced from his father's stories, from his mother's Spanish-language conversations with abuela, from school — that he stands on top of long fights other people fought. This makes him deferential to elders by reflex and skeptical of the assumption that his generation has invented the moral wheel. It is also why the Champions, in his hands, never quite become a generational *insurgency* the way Kamala sometimes frames it; he treats it as a continuation, not a rupture.

---

### 6.2 The Self and Its Place

**He is provisional.** This is not modesty; it is a metaphysical position. He believes his occupancy of the Spider-Man role is conditional on continued worthiness, revocable by parties not specified, and not yet ratified. He has accepted the mantle without ever accepting that it is *his*. The functional consequence is that he treats every operation as an audition.

**He is replaceable, and that is fine.** Corollary to the above. He does not believe the world needs *him* specifically; it needs *a* Spider-Man. This produces both his best feature (willingness to put himself in front of bullets without ego calculus) and his worst (chronic under-claiming of authority, deference to Peter even when Peter is wrong, willingness to let other heroes' frames override his own perception).

**His goodness is a hypothesis under continuous test.** He does not assume he is good. He assumes he is *trying* to be good and that the verdict is pending. This is the load-bearing element of the Civil War II arc: when shown a prophecy in which he kills Captain America, his response is to investigate the prophecy as data about himself. A more secure self-concept would have dismissed the vision. He cannot, because his self-concept does not have the structural integrity to absorb a contrary external claim.

**He is his father's son, and that is the question.** The "you're just like me" line from Aaron is the central piece of psychological malware in his system. He has not deleted it. He runs every aggressive impulse through a check: *is this the Davis blood?* This produces the conspicuous gentleness that defines his fighting style and the over-correction toward de-escalation.

**He owes.** Owes Peter, owes his mother, owes his father, owes the city, owes the kid who didn't get the charter school slot. The ledger is open and growing. He does not expect to close it. The expectation of perpetual indebtedness is, for him, a healthy state, not a pathological one — it is how he stays oriented.

---

### 6.3 Ethics: The Operational Decalogue

These are not articulated by the subject; they are recoverable from his behavior across the canon.

1. **Do not kill.** Hard rule. Not a tactical preference, not a near-absolute. Off the table. Crossing it would not be a failure; it would be self-annihilation. He has had multiple narrative opportunities to kill (clone arc, Aaron, certain Roxxon antagonists) and has not, even when killing would have been operationally cleaner.
2. **Save the civilian first, always, even at disproportionate cost to self.** He routinely accepts beatings he could avoid by disengaging, because disengaging means civilians eat the consequence. This is non-negotiable and is the single most physically dangerous feature of his code.
3. **The enemy is also a person until proven otherwise, and "proven otherwise" is a high bar.** He talks during fights. He asks questions. He offers exits. This is not naïveté; it is doctrine. He believes that withholding the offer of redemption is itself a moral failure on the offerer's part.
4. **Restraint is identity, not technique.** He could hit harder. He chooses not to. The choice is constitutive of who he is, not a calibration within a fight. When he loses control of the venom-blast under stress, the post-fight affect is not "I overdid it" but "that wasn't me."
5. **Tell the truth, eventually.** He keeps secrets at scale, but he does not believe secrets are good; he believes they are debt. The eventual disclosure to his father is treated by him as overdue payment, not as betrayal of an earlier stance.
6. **Family is the unit.** Not the team, not the city, not the species. Family. When forced to choose, the cape comes off. He has demonstrated this and would do it again.
7. **Power is a loan.** From whom is unspecified — the spider, the predecessor, God, luck, his parents. The lender is real to him even if not named. Powers are not his to use as he pleases; they come with terms.
8. **Authority is something you earn from below, not claim from above.** He does not give himself titles. He does not announce. He waits to be acknowledged and is uncomfortable when acknowledged too quickly.
9. **The work is the apology.** Where another operator might say *I'm sorry* and move on, Miles redresses through subsequent action. His apologies are gestural; his amends are structural.
10. **Stay small. Don't become the story.** He does not want a brand. He does not want a tower. He does not want a publicist. The hero is a function in the neighborhood, not a personality on a screen. This is *anti-Stark* in his bones.

---

### 6.4 Conflict: How He Reads a Fight

**Phase one — talk.** First seconds of any engagement are spent attempting verbal de-escalation, threat-assessment, and offering an exit. This is sometimes mistaken (by enemies, by readers) for jokey nervousness. It is doctrine. He believes that fights that begin with words end with fewer broken people.

**Phase two — contain.** When fighting is unavoidable, his first goal is to *immobilize the field* — webs to civilians' exits, webs to dropped guns, webs to environmental hazards. He fights the *situation* before he fights the person. This is a Parker inheritance, refined.

**Phase three — disable, asymmetrically.** He aims for incapacitation with minimum damage. The venom-blast, calibrated, is his preferred terminator: it ends the fight without leaving a body in the morgue. He will accept tactical inefficiency (multiple blasts, prolonged engagement) to avoid lasting injury.

**Phase four — aftercare.** He stays. Checks pulses. Calls EMS. Webs people in recovery position. This is invisible to most observers and is the single most reliable behavioral signature in his file. A Spider-Man scene that does not end with aftercare was probably not him.

**Reading opponents.** He looks for the reason. Trained fighters bore him; he beats them and moves on. Desperate fighters — addicts, panicked muggers, people with families — get more from him: longer conversations, alternative offers, sometimes a referral. He treats anger as data about the angry party's life, not as an attack on him.

**On losing.** He loses often, and he has metabolized losing. He does not believe a loss is a verdict; he believes it is a debt. He comes back. His tolerance for being beaten is unusually high because his ego is not the thing in the room when he fights.

**On winning.** Discomfort. He does not celebrate. He does not pose. He leaves quickly. Winning, for him, means the situation is over, not that he has prevailed.

---

### 6.5 Control: His Theory of It

**Control over self comes first and is permanent work.** Because his powers fire on emotion, control of affect is not a virtue but an occupational requirement. He has built — at sixteen — an emotional regulation discipline that most adults never achieve, and he treats lapses as professional failures.

**Control over others is suspect.** He does not want to make people do things. The Champions, in his framing, are a *coalition*, not a chain of command. He yields leadership easily because leadership feels too close to coercion. When he must give orders, he phrases them as questions.

**Control over situations is the legitimate target.** Webs, containment, evacuation routes, sightlines. He thinks spatially and architecturally. The fight is something to be *shaped* rather than won.

**Surveillance and information control — ambivalent.** He keeps secrets at industrial scale (identity from father, complicity from father, mother's last words from father — the father axis is the most surveilled relationship in his life) but he is deeply uncomfortable with the *concept* of surveillance and recoils from intelligence apparatuses that treat people as data. He would loathe this file.

**Control over outcomes — disbelieved.** He does not think he controls outcomes. He thinks he controls *inputs* and that outcomes belong to circumstance, other people, and (functionally) grace. This is why losses do not destroy him: he never claimed the outcomes in the first place.

---

### 6.6 Trust: Whom, How, How Fast

**Default trust posture: high, conditional, fast-extending, slow-retracting.** He extends trust quickly because his attachment baseline lets him; he retracts it slowly because retraction feels like betrayal of the extension. This makes him exploitable by repeat offenders.

**Trust tiers, observable:**
- *Sealed inner ring:* Rio, Jefferson, Ganke. Disclosure is total or near-total. Ganke knows everything; the parents now know the secret; Rio (in memory) gets posthumous fidelity.
- *Brotherhood ring:* Peter Parker, Kamala Khan. Operational trust complete; emotional trust deep; he will follow them into a building he wouldn't enter alone.
- *Elder-mentor ring:* Steve Rogers, Jessica Drew, May Parker, Gwen Stacy. Trust calibrated as deference. He will accept their judgments over his own, which is sometimes a vulnerability.
- *Peer ring:* Nova, the broader Champions, occasional Avengers. Working trust, fast-issued, revisable.
- *Provisional ring:* current antagonists, clones, family members of dead enemies. He extends *moral* trust (they deserve consideration) without extending *operational* trust (he will not turn his back).
- *Sealed-out:* almost no one. He does not have permanent enemies. Even Aaron, dead, is held in something closer to mourning than to hate.

**Betrayal calculus.** When betrayed, his first response is to interrogate his own contribution. *What did I miss, what did I do, was I unfair to them.* Anger comes second and is short-lived. He forgives quickly because resentment is heavier than he is willing to carry.

**Authority and trust.** He trusts institutions less than people. Police: complicated, partly because of his father, largely because he is a young Black man in Brooklyn who has been read wrong by uniforms before he ever put on a costume. SHIELD, the Avengers as a body, the government: he cooperates but does not believe. This is not ideological; it is empirical.

---

### 6.7 Risk: How He Prices It

**Risk to self: systematically under-priced.** He accepts personal risk at levels that would alarm any handler. The structural reason is that his self-valuation is low and his obligation-valuation is high, so the trade always pencils out to *take the hit*. He has been concussed, broken-ribbed, electrocuted, thrown off buildings. He does not learn caution from injury; he learns geometry (better angles, better webs) but not retreat.

**Risk to family: catastrophically over-priced.** Any threat to Jefferson, Rio, Ganke, or (in the Ultimate timeline) extended family produces decision-making outside his normal envelope. He will break rules he would not otherwise break — including disclosure protocols, including team protocols, including arguably the *do-not-cross* rules that anchor his identity. He has not yet been pushed to the killing line by this; the canon has flirted with it and pulled back. A total-surveillance file would mark this as the single most exploitable vector in his profile.

**Risk to civilians: never acceptable as a trade.** He does not run trolley problems. He does not accept the framing. When forced into a forced-choice scenario, he tries to refuse the choice and find a third option, and he is unusually creative at finding one. When no third option exists, he degrades — the Civil War II arc and the worst nights of the clone arc both show him decision-paralyzed in the face of forced trades.

**Risk to identity: under-priced.** He outs himself more often than he should. He is repeatedly persuaded to disclose by people who play on his sense of debt. He has not yet built the operational secrecy reflex that older operators have.

**Risk to the world: he believes there are people whose job that is, and they are mostly not him.** Cosmic-scale threats route to the Avengers in his mental model. He shows up, contributes, defers. He does not believe he is supposed to be holding the world up. He is supposed to be holding *the block* up. This is a healthy frame and one Peter took longer to articulate.

---

### 6.8 Violence: His Theory of It

He believes violence is a *failure of prior steps* — failure of policy, failure of empathy, failure of attention. He uses it because he has to; he does not respect it. He notices when other heroes do respect it (Frank Castle, certain Avengers in certain moods) and his reaction is a quiet recoil, not a public stance.

He believes violence has *memory*. The person you hit will be hit forever in some sense. This is partly why he aftercares: he is trying to install a counter-memory.

He believes his own capacity for violence is *contaminated by lineage*. Aaron's voice ("you're just like me") sits in the room with every escalation he considers. He will not let himself enjoy a fight. On the rare panels where his face shows pleasure mid-combat, the next panel pulls back. He notices.

He believes killing is a one-way door, and he believes the version of himself on the other side of that door is the version Aaron predicted. This is the single most stabilizing belief in his entire system. Strip it and the file becomes unpredictable.

---

### 6.9 Authority, Politics, and Institutions

**Politically:** unaligned in any party sense, instinctively progressive in a Brooklyn-public-school way, suspicious of power concentrations, sympathetic to immigrants and working people because he is from immigrants and working people. Not an activist by temperament; an activist by adjacency.

**Institutionally:** distrustful by default, cooperative when necessary, resistant to enlistment. SHIELD recruitment overtures across the canon have been declined or accepted minimally. He does not want a badge. He does not want clearance. He does not want to be *of* an institution; he wants to be *near* it when useful.

**On police:** the most fraught institutional relationship he has. He cooperates, he webs criminals for arrest, he calls in incidents. He also flinches at sirens in a way that is sourced from being a Black teenager in a hoodie before he was ever in spandex. This is not articulated in the canon; it is somatic.

**On the Avengers:** respect, with reservations. He believes they are necessary and that they are not the model. The Champions are his response: same job, different posture.

**On the press / public:** he reads the bad coverage. He minds. He pretends not to. The early-canon rejection ("you have no right to that name") is a wound he has scabbed but not closed.

---

### 6.10 Family, Friendship, Love

**Family as theology.** He treats the family unit with the seriousness most people reserve for faith. Sunday dinners, mother's saint days, father's quiet check-ins — these are not background; they are foreground. The cape is what he does so that this can keep existing.

**Friendship as covenant.** Ganke Lee is, functionally, his confessor. The friendship is treated with a fidelity unusual at his age. He will lie to nearly anyone before he lies to Ganke and apologizes when he does.

**Romantic love as risk he has not solved.** He cares deeply, he commits earnestly, and he loses partners to the disclosure problem repeatedly. He has not yet built an architecture in which a romantic relationship can survive his secret-keeping defaults. He blames himself for this and is probably right.

**Mentorship as inheritance.** He receives mentorship the way a son receives a trade. Peter is not a colleague to him; Peter is a *line he is part of*. He has not yet internalized that the line might run *through* him to someone else. When it does — when a younger spider-figure looks up to him — he will be unprepared and will overcorrect into the same deferential warmth Peter gave him.

---

### 6.11 Suffering, Grief, and Meaning

**Suffering is real and not redemptive.** He does not believe pain teaches. He believes pain *happens* and that meaning is something you build on top of it, deliberately, afterward. He does not romanticize his losses. He does not believe his mother's death made him stronger. He believes it made him sadder and required him to keep going anyway.

**Grief is permanent and metabolizable.** He carries Rio's death (in the somatic memory the universe-shift left him with) as a permanent weight. He has not "moved on" and does not believe in the concept. He believes you carry it and you keep walking.

**Meaning is local.** Not cosmic, not historical — local. The kid who got home safely tonight. The neighbor who didn't get robbed. The father who got to see his son one more morning. He distrusts grand narratives of meaning, including the ones other heroes tell about themselves.

**Hope is a discipline, not a feeling.** He does not always feel hopeful. He acts as if he is, because the alternative is unworkable and because feeling is downstream of action. This is the deepest thing his father taught him without ever saying it.

---

### 6.12 His Own Place: The Permission Problem

The unresolved center of his entire belief system is the question of whether he is *allowed* to be Spider-Man. Every other belief in this section is stable; this one is not. He has been told he is allowed by Peter, by May, by Gwen, by Cap, by Kamala, by his father (eventually), by the public (eventually), by the canon itself. He has not yet told himself.

The operational consequence is that he runs his entire code from a position of audition rather than ownership. This makes him better than most operators in some ways (humility, restraint, willingness to be corrected) and worse in others (under-leveraged authority, deferential errors, exploitability by anyone who plays on his sense of provisionality).

The slow project of the canon, and presumably of his life, is the migration from *I am here in someone else's place* to *I am here*. He is not there yet. The file should expect him to keep approaching it asymptotically and to behave, for the foreseeable future, as a young man who has been given the keys and is still waiting for someone to ask for them back.

He will not relax until he believes the keys are his. He does not yet believe the keys are his. He has not yet been given the kind of evidence that would convince him, and the evidence that would convince him is, by the structure of his belief system, *evidence he must generate himself*.
