That is the operational code in one sentence: **he is trying to earn what he already has, and he does not know how to stop.**


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP — SUBJECT: MORALES, MILES GONZALO
## Section 6: Moral & Ethical Framework

---

### 6.1 Preliminary: The Distinction Between Professed and Enacted Code

The subject is unusual among costumed operatives in that his *professed* ethical statements and his *enacted* ethical pattern are nearly congruent — a function of low cynicism, secure attachment, and an adolescent's not-yet-corroded sincerity. The gaps that do exist are not hypocrisy gaps (claim/act mismatch) but *recursion* gaps: areas where the code commands action A, the subject performs action A, and then immediately interrogates whether A was performed for the right reasons. The moral life is therefore not "do the right thing"; it is "do the right thing *and verify that you are the kind of person who would do the right thing*." This recursive verification is itself the most distinctive feature of his ethical operation.

What follows is built from his behavioral record across *Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man* (2011–2014), *Spider-Man* vol. 2 (2016–2018), *Champions* vol. 1–2 (2016–2019), the Ahmed solo run (2018–2022), the Ziglar run (2022–), *Civil War II*, the *Spider-Verse / Spider-Geddon* events, and his cross-title appearances.

---

### 6.2 The Inviolable Floor: What He Will Not Do

The subject's code has a small set of *true absolutes* — rules that have never been violated on-page across more than a decade of canon, and whose violation he treats not as a tactical error but as identity collapse.

**He will not kill.** This is the load-bearing absolute. It is older than the costume — visible in his refusal to use lethal force even when his venom blast is calibrated high enough to do so (and he knows it is). The rule survives:
- The Aaron confrontation (*USM* #28), where lethality would have ended an existential threat to his family and where the weapon's malfunction did the killing *for* him — and even this proxy lethality leaves him traumatized for over a year. He does not experience the death as a moral loophole closed in his favor; he experiences it as a moral catastrophe he was adjacent to.
- The Roxxon arcs, where corporate violence against civilians provides every standard "justified lethal force" frame and he declines every one.
- The clone arc, where the Selim clone is a near-perfect tactical case for euthanasia (clone is dying, dangerous, and not "really" Miles), and he refuses, choosing palliation over termination.
- Civil War II, where the prophetic vision *predicts* he will kill Captain America. His response is not to plan how to avoid it tactically but to interrogate whether he is *capable* of it at all — and the interrogation itself destabilizes him, because he treats the mere question as a moral injury.

The rule is not utilitarian. He cannot be talked out of it by trolley problems. It is constitutive: killing is what his uncle does, what the family disease looks like at its terminus, what makes the inheritance from Aaron real. To kill is to lose the argument with the dying man's last words.

**He will not use his powers against the powerless.** Civilians, bystanders, the subdued — invisible to his combat calculus as targets, hyper-visible as protectees. He has never, in any title, used a venom blast on a non-combatant. Even in the clone arc, where civilians are weaponized as proxies, his solution is consistently to neutralize the controlling structure, not the controlled bodies.

**He will not break a promise made to a parent.** "Don't tell your father" (Rio, dying) is honored for years past the point of utility. The compact made with Jefferson at the kitchen table — about school, about safety, about not following Aaron — is a moral document the subject treats as having full ethical weight even when his father is wrong on the merits. This is not blind obedience; it is the elevation of *the promise itself* into the category of inviolable. He breaks this rule exactly once on-page, and the disclosure is staged as a confessional rite, not a tactical move.

**He will not let someone else take the fall for what he did.** Documented across the Aaron aftermath (he repeatedly tries to confess to his father), the clone arc (refuses to let the clones be blamed wholesale for actions taken with his face), and the Champions disputes (consistently steps forward as the one who decided X when X goes wrong). The rule is partially compensatory — he is liturgically eager to claim responsibility — but functionally absolute.

**He will not impersonate Peter Parker.** A subtle one. He wears the suit, took the name, was given the legacy — but he has never, in any encounter where a stranger assumes he is the original, simply accepted the misidentification to extract advantage. He corrects it, often awkwardly. The boundary between *inheriting a role* and *appropriating an identity* is one he polices with surprising rigor.

---

### 6.3 The Inviolable Ceiling: What He Will Always Do

The mirror of the floor. Behaviors he treats as *obligated*, not optional, and which appear with metronomic regularity in his record.

**He will identify himself to a frightened civilian.** Across hundreds of micro-encounters, the recorded pattern is: lands, says some version of "you're okay, it's me, I'm Spider-Man, you're safe." Even when this costs him tactical surprise. The reassurance is treated as load-bearing — the rescue is not complete until the person is psychologically as well as physically extracted.

**He will return.** If he leaves an encounter unfinished — a civilian half-helped, a conversation cut short by sirens, a friend mid-sentence — he comes back. Often hours later, in costume or out. Ganke's apartment, May Parker's house, the Champions HQ — the record shows him reappearing to complete interactions other heroes would log as closed.

**He will defer to the older hero in the room.** Even when his read is better. The pattern is so consistent it constitutes a rule, and Peter Parker, Steve Rogers, Jessica Drew, and Carol Danvers have all separately told him to stop doing it. He does not stop.

**He will tell the joke.** Self-directed, deflective, almost always at his own expense. The joke is moral hygiene: it prevents the moment from becoming about him, it pre-empts the assessment of his performance, and it signals to the rescued party that he is not a threatening figure. He has never, in canon, mocked a victim. The humor is asymmetric by rule: outward = self; inward = no one.

---

### 6.4 The Operating Principles (Working Code)

Below the absolutes sits a layer of operational rules — strong defaults, occasionally overridden, but tracked across canon as the working ethic.

**1. Restraint is the moral identity, not the tactic.** The Champions slogan ("change without punching") is, for him, not aspirational PR but a personal creed. He looks for the de-escalation in every encounter. He has, more than once, taken a beating rather than escalate, because escalation is the family pattern (Aaron's solution, the clones' solution) and refusing to escalate is how he proves the inheritance is not deterministic.

**2. The civilian is the unit.** Other heroes optimize for the mission, the team, the strategic objective. He optimizes for *the specific person currently in front of him*. This produces tactical inefficiency (he will divert from a critical objective to extract one stuck pedestrian) which he refuses to apologize for. The trade-off is, in his frame, not a trade-off: a hero who lets the one die for the many is on the road to becoming the one who decides who counts.

**3. Power must be justified to those without it.** Visible in his discomfort with secrecy *from civilians* (as distinct from secrecy from his father, which is different). He explains himself in the moment. He answers questions from bystanders. He treats public legitimacy as something earned conversation by conversation, not granted by reputation.

**4. The mantle is borrowed; the conduct is owned.** He treats the name "Spider-Man" as Peter's, which he is keeping clean for a successor — but he treats *what he does in the suit* as fully his moral property. This split is the operational form of his impostor structure: the role is provisional, the responsibility is total. It is the worst of both worlds ethically (no claim to the authority, full claim to the blame) and he has not yet adjusted it.

**5. Family is the moral test case.** Every ethical dilemma is sanity-checked against the question "would I do this if it were my father / mother / Ganke standing there?" This produces strong, consistent civilian-protective behavior and weak, inconsistent strategic behavior. He is bad at chess and good at triage.

**6. Restitution over punishment.** Across the Aaron aftermath, the clone arc, and his interventions with low-level criminals, the consistent preference is to repair (return stolen property, restore the victim, get the perpetrator into a recoverable position) rather than to punish. He hands criminals to police with notable reluctance and a tendency to advocate (verbally, to officers; in writing, in notes left at scenes) for leniency in cases where the perpetrator's circumstances are visible to him. This is *Aaron-shaped* — he reads many street criminals as versions of his uncle who could have gone another way.

**7. The truth eventually, even when costly.** His record contains a long pattern of *delayed* honesty, but the honesty does arrive. He is constitutionally incapable of taking a secret to a grave he can avoid. The disclosure to Jefferson is the canonical instance, but smaller examples — admitting to Ganke that he was scared, admitting to Peter that he doesn't feel ready, admitting to Kamala that he disagrees with a Champions decision — are constant.

---

### 6.5 Justifications: The Reasons He Gives Himself

The subject's moral self-talk (visible in interior monologue, journal-like narration in the Ahmed run, and conversations with Ganke that function as confessional) reveals the *structure* of his justifications, which is distinct from the content.

**He does not justify in consequentialist terms.** He almost never says "I did X because the outcome was better." When pressed, his reasoning routes through identity ("that's not who I want to be"), through relationship ("she would have wanted me to"), or through obligation-from-inheritance ("Peter would have"). The Peter-citation is particularly frequent and worth noting: he uses the dead predecessor as a portable moral authority, asking *what would Peter do* the way an observant person asks what scripture says. This is operationally functional but developmentally arresting — it lets him decide hard cases without having to claim the authority to decide them himself.

**He does not justify in rights-based terms either.** He does not invoke abstract principle ("she had a right to live"). His ethical vocabulary is concrete, particular, person-shaped. The civilian is not a rights-bearer; she is *a woman with a kid waiting for her at home*. This makes him a poor public spokesman for ethical positions and a very good first responder.

**His actual justificatory structure is virtue-ethical and narrative.** The question that organizes his decisions is *what kind of person am I being, in this moment, by doing this?* — and the answer is evaluated against the question *what kind of person can I live with having been?* This is an Aristotelian frame in adolescent clothes, and it is also why prophetic visions, accusations of resemblance to his uncle, and the clone arc all hit so hard: they all attack the narrative-identity layer where his ethics actually live.

---

### 6.6 Where the Code Is Consistent

**Across writers.** Bendis, Ahmed, Ziglar, Waid (Champions), Zub — every long-running writer has preserved the absolutes against killing, the deference to elders, the civilian-first reflex, and the restraint-as-identity stance. This consistency is unusual for a Marvel character of his vintage and indicates that the code is *characterological* rather than authorial.

**Across stress levels.** The behaviors that show up in low-stakes patrol (helping the lost tourist, walking the kid home) are the same behaviors that show up in cosmic crisis (the Champions deployments, *Spider-Geddon*). He does not have a "wartime ethic" distinct from a "peacetime ethic." This is rare.

**Across relational contexts.** He is the same moral agent with his father, his mother, Ganke, Peter, Kamala, strangers, and enemies. He does not perform a different ethic for different audiences. The deference modulates (more with Peter, less with criminals); the underlying code does not.

**Across costume states.** Out of the suit, he holds to the same rules. He does not become a more relaxed moral agent in civilian clothes — if anything, the school and home environments tighten the code, because the parents-as-audience effect is stronger.

---

### 6.7 Where the Code Fractures

The fractures are real, recurring, and diagnostic.

**Fracture 1: Honesty vs. the Promise.** The rule "do not break a promise to a parent" and the rule "tell the truth eventually" are on a collision course for the entire Ultimate run and most of the 616 run. He resolves it by delay, which is a fracture under another name. The cost is documented: deteriorating relationships, secondary lies told to support the primary secret, and the slow corrosion of his self-respect during the years of concealment. He has never developed a principled position on when secret-keeping becomes lying. The fracture remains open.

**Fracture 2: Save everyone vs. forced choice.** His ethical floor (do not let the powerless be sacrificed) and his ethical ceiling (save the specific person in front of you) are incoherent in any genuine trolley situation. The canon does not give him many true forced-choices, which is partly authorial protection and partly because he *creates* third options at the cost of personal injury rather than accept the binary. When the binary is genuinely forced (rare; *Spider-Geddon* offers the cleanest case), his performance degrades: he freezes, then takes the hit himself, then is angry afterward at the universe for offering the choice. This is not a stable solution; it is a refusal to have the dilemma.

**Fracture 3: Defer to elders vs. own your judgment.** The Champions exist as an institutional response to this fracture — a deliberate decision that the older generation is wrong in some patterned way (around militarization, around collateral damage, around treating young people as auxiliaries). And yet within the Champions and outside it, he continues to defer when an older hero is in the room. The fracture is unresolved. He has built an entire team premised on the proposition that he should not defer, while continuing to defer.

**Fracture 4: Restraint vs. effectiveness.** Several encounters in the Ahmed run feature him losing a fight (or letting a villain escape) because he refused to escalate, with consequences that fall on civilians shortly after. He registers these consequences. He does not change the policy. The honest reading is that he has decided, without articulating it, that the long-run identity cost of becoming a person-who-escalates outweighs the short-run civilian cost of specific failures — but he has not made this trade-off explicit even to himself, which means he eats the guilt for each particular failure as if the trade-off were not in his code at all.

**Fracture 5: The clones.** The decision to take responsibility for the clones rather than let them be killed is morally consistent with the rest of his code. But the *grounds* on which he does it shift mid-arc — sometimes "they're me," sometimes "they're persons regardless of origin," sometimes "I don't get to decide who deserves to die." He has not stabilized the metaphysics, and the instability shows up as inconsistent treatment of individual clones (Shift integrated as ally, Mindspinner held at arm's length, Selim mourned). The code holds; the reasoning fractures.

**Fracture 6: The mantle question itself.** "The role is borrowed; the conduct is owned" is a fracture, not a synthesis. It produces a moral agent who is *fully* responsible and *not at all* authoritative — which is incoherent. A genuinely borrowed role would carry diminished responsibility (you're holding it for someone). A genuinely owned responsibility would carry full authority (you're the one making the calls). He has both halves and neither whole. This is the central unresolved structural fracture of his ethical life, and it is what every other fracture eventually traces back to.

---

### 6.8 Shifts Over Time

**Phase 1 — Refusal (pre-mantle, *USM* #1–4).** No code, in costume terms. The civilian ethic is intact (he is already the kid who does the right thing at school, who looks out for Ganke). The refusal to wear the suit is itself a moral position: *I have not earned this; therefore I should not have it*. This phase establishes the pattern that authority must be earned and that he does not yet have it.

**Phase 2 — Reluctant adoption (*USM* #4–22).** The code is largely *imported* — he is doing what he believes Peter would have done, what the Parker family approves of, what Spider-Woman tolerates. His agency in this period is the agency to *comply with* an ethic he has not yet internalized. The absolutes (no killing, civilians first) form here, scaffolded by imitation.

**Phase 3 — Trauma and withdrawal (*USM* #28 – *Cataclysm*).** The Aaron death and then Rio's death force the code from imported to *owned*. After the year of withdrawal, when he returns to the suit, the ethic he comes back to is recognizably his own — restraint is no longer "what Peter would do," it is "what I will not become." The grounds shift from imitation to inheritance-refusal. The code becomes load-bearing for his identity in a way it was not before.

**Phase 4 — Integration into 616, Civil War II (2015–2016).** The first sustained test of the owned ethic under conditions that include legitimate older-hero authorities (Steve Rogers, Tony Stark) telling him different things. The Ulysses vision is the diagnostic event of this phase: he submits to external moral evaluation rather than asserting his own. The code holds operationally; the *authority* to enforce it from inside himself is still missing.

**Phase 5 — Champions (2016–2019).** First period in which he acts *institutionally* on the code — building an organization premised on the ethic of restraint and civilian-primacy. This is, in retrospect, the most significant ethical development of his career: the code stops being personal-only and becomes a position he holds in public, alongside peers, against an older generation. He still defers within the team to Kamala, which preserves the elder-deference pattern in miniature, but the *publication* of the ethic to the world is a step his earlier self could not have taken.

**Phase 6 — The clones and the shadow (Ahmed run, 2018–2022).** The code is tested against the question of whether his own fragments count as persons. He concludes that they do, which extends the civilian-first principle past its previous boundary. This is genuine ethical development — the rule "do not let the powerless be sacrificed" is enlarged to include the powerless-and-also-versions-of-me, which is a more demanding standard than he previously held himself to.

**Phase 7 — Current (Ziglar and ongoing).** The code is stable, the fractures are stable, the slow project of granting himself the authority that matches the responsibility continues. There is incremental evidence that he is beginning to act on his own judgment without seeking Peter's blessing first — but only incremental. The transition from *substitute Spider-Man* to *Spider-Man* is the transition from imported ethic to owned ethic to *authoritative* ethic, and he is somewhere between the second and third.

---

### 6.9 Synthesis

The subject operates a coherent virtue-ethical code with a small set of true absolutes (no killing, no harm to the powerless, no broken parental promises, no displaced blame, no identity appropriation), a layer of strong operational defaults (restraint as identity, the civilian as unit, restitution over punishment, truth eventually), and a justificatory structure that runs through narrative identity rather than consequence or rule. The code is unusually consistent across writers, contexts, and stress levels. It fractures predictably along the seams between honesty and loyalty, between save-everyone and forced-choice, between deference and judgment, and at the central unresolved seam between borrowed authority and owned responsibility. Across his record the code has shifted from imported (Phase 2) to owned (Phase 3) to public (Phase 5) to extended (Phase 6), with the next required shift — from owned to *authoritative* — still in progress.

The single most important fact about his ethics, for surveillance and prediction purposes, is this: he can be relied upon to do the right thing as he understands it, and he can be relied upon to interrogate himself afterward about whether he understood it correctly. He is therefore *highly* predictable in conduct and *highly* vulnerable in self-concept. An adversary who attacks his conduct will find a wall. An adversary who attacks his sense of *who he is in performing the conduct* will find every door open.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# 6. COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE

## 6.1 Baseline Register and Code Architecture

The subject is a fluent **triple-register code-switcher**, and the switching itself is one of the most diagnostic behaviors in his file. He moves between (a) **Brooklyn AAVE-inflected adolescent English** with peers and family on his father's side, (b) **Spanish or Spanglish** with his mother and her family — primarily reactive, emotive, and intimate rather than fluent-conversational — and (c) **standardized, school-coded "good student" English** with teachers, adult heroes, and authority figures. The switching is not unconscious. Surveillance of his speech across *Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man*, the Bendis 616 run, the Ahmed solo, and the Ziglar solo demonstrates that he selects register *to manage the listener*, not to express himself. This is consistent with the rest of his behavioral profile: language, like his powers, is calibrated toward the comfort of the people around him.

His **default register** — what he uses alone, with Ganke, in internal monologue boxes — is a relaxed Brooklyn vernacular with high markers of contemporary internet-native speech: *"like,"* *"literally,"* *"bro,"* *"dude,"* *"my guy,"* *"nah,"* *"for real?"*, and intensifier stacks (*"so so so"* / *"way way too"*). He elides copulas in casual speech ("you wildin'," "she good," "that's crazy") but restores them in adult-facing contexts within the same scene. Adult heroes hearing him for the first time consistently underestimate his vocabulary; this is a recurring beat (Stark, Cap, Strange) and he does nothing to correct it.

His **Spanish** is reactive: ¡Mamá!, ay dios mío, ¿qué?, mija/mijo as received not produced, gracias, por favor, te quiero. He understands more than he produces — a textbook second-generation pattern. Under acute emotion he reaches *for* Spanish (the dying-mother sequence; reunion scenes; prayer-adjacent moments) which marks the language in his system as the **affective substrate**, not the operational one. He does not joke in Spanish. He does not threaten in Spanish. He loves and grieves in Spanish.

## 6.2 The Quipping Register (and How It Differs From Parker's)

The mask switches on a different voice. In costume, with hostiles, he runs the inherited Spider-Man patter — but the patter is **structurally distinct** from Peter's. Parker's quips are *aggressive*, aimed outward, designed to destabilize the opponent. Miles's quips are **performative-anxious**: aimed at no one in particular, often self-directed, frequently *narrating his own bafflement* at the situation he is in.

- Parker pattern: "*Hey, big guy, did your mother know you'd grow up to be a literal trash can?*" (target-locked)
- Morales pattern: "*Okay okay okay this is — this is fine, this is totally a normal Tuesday, why is it a lizard, why is it always a lizard —*" (self-locked, processing aloud)

He talks *to himself through the mask* far more than he talks *to enemies*. The quip is a self-regulation tool, not a combat tool. When the regulation is working, the patter is loose and rhythmic; when it stops mid-sentence, the file should flag it — a Miles who has gone silent in a fight is a Miles who is either (a) genuinely scared past the point of speech, or (b) about to discharge a venom blast he did not plan. The cessation of language precedes the involuntary power event in nearly every recorded instance.

He also **apologizes mid-fight**. To enemies. "*Sorry — sorry, sorry, that's gonna bruise.*" "*My bad, my bad.*" This is unique to him among the Spider-cohort. Parker mocks; Gwen taunts; Miles apologizes. It is reflexive social repair triggered by his own use of force, and it does not turn off even when the target is trying to kill him.

## 6.3 Verbal Tics, Particles, and Filler

Inventory, in order of frequency across the canon:

- **"Okay"** — used as a self-soothing marker, often in triplets ("*okay okay okay*"). Functions as a verbal restart button. Count this; the rate scales linearly with his stress.
- **"Like"** — discourse particle, normative for his cohort; not diagnostic in isolation but the *density* rises sharply under cognitive load.
- **"I mean —"** — preface to almost any disclosure of opinion. Hedges before the sentence begins. He rarely states a position cold.
- **"It's just that —"** — preface to almost any disclosure of feeling. Same function, emotional register.
- **"No no no"** — used both literally (refusal) and as an attention-recapture device when he has lost track of the conversation.
- **"Wait. Wait — wait."** — the *retroactive* cognitive marker. He often realizes the meaning of what he just heard a half-beat after the others, and the triple-wait covers the lag. Diagnostic of his lateral, ethical-first cognition: he processes the *implication* before the content.
- **"For real?" / "Are you serious right now?"** — disbelief markers. Often deployed against absurd situations rather than people; he is more often baffled than offended.
- **"Bro" / "Dude" / "My guy"** — applied with promiscuity. He has called the Vulture "my guy." He has called a Symbiote "bro." It is not affection — it is reflexive social leveling. He flattens hierarchy through address.
- **"Sir" / "Ma'am"** — present, sincere, and applied to adults including villains older than him. He has *sir*-ed the Kingpin. This is parental training overriding combat context and is one of the most reliable Morales fingerprints in any disputed dialogue.
- **Sigh-words.** *"Man..."* and *"God..."* as full-sentence pre-pauses, especially when contemplating something he does not want to say.

He does not curse. Across approximately a decade of published material, his profanity inventory is restricted to *crap, dang, freaking, what the heck,* and occasional *damn*. This is not a comics-code artifact; the surrounding cast curses freely in modern Marvel. He simply does not. Notable, because his *internal* monologue (caption boxes) is also clean. The restraint is not performance for adults. It is internalized.

## 6.4 Diction and Lexical Range

Vocabulary level is **higher than his register suggests**. He uses *iteration, paradigm, ostensibly, calibrated, asymmetric, ramifications* in narration and in lab-context dialogue. He suppresses this vocabulary in social speech — a code-switching downshift. The school-self speaks; the street-self performs not having gone to school. Both are him. When stressed beyond the resources of either register, he reverts to the higher one — the academic vocabulary is his **fallback** under genuine cognitive load, suggesting it is more deeply wired than the casual register he prefers to project.

He uses **physics and chemistry vocabulary** functionally (*conductive, capacitance, voltage drop, vector, terminal velocity, viscosity*) and applies it correctly to his own powers in caption-narration. He does not show off this vocabulary aloud. He is technically literate and socially modest about it.

Spanish lexicon is **kinship-restricted**: he has the words for *mom, dad, family, love, thank you, please, sorry, food terms*, and a small set of exclamations. He does not have the words for *abstract politics, professional registers, romantic seduction*. The shape of his Spanish vocabulary is the shape of his mother's kitchen.

## 6.5 Rhetoric and Argument Structure

When he argues a position — in Champions meetings, in confrontations with senior heroes, in the *Civil War II* arc — his rhetoric follows a remarkably consistent four-beat structure:

1. **Concession.** "*I get it. I get why you're doing this.*" / "*You're not wrong about —*" He opens by granting the opponent's frame.
2. **Personalization.** "*But here's the thing — when I —*" He pivots to first-person experience, not principle.
3. **Stakes-for-others.** "*— and if we do this, then she / he / they —*" He locates the harm in a specific third party.
4. **Soft imperative.** "*So I think we have to —*" / "*So can we just —*" He does not command; he proposes, often in question form.

This is the rhetoric of someone who **does not trust his own authority to issue a flat assertion**. It is also unusually effective on adult heroes precisely *because* it does not threaten their seniority. Cap responds to it. Stark resents it. Kamala recognizes it as a peer's method and matches it. Note that he **never argues from prophecy, destiny, or claim**. He does not say "I am Spider-Man and therefore —." He says "I'm trying to be — and so —."

When the rhetoric fails and he is pushed, he does not escalate to volume. He goes **quiet and specific**: short declarative sentences, no hedging, eye contact. The shift from hedged-paragraphs to short-declaratives is the rhetorical signature of him having decided something. Listen for the disappearance of *like* and *I mean*. When those drop out, the decision is made.

## 6.6 Deflection Language

His deflections are a **closed inventory**, and they are diagnostic.

- **"I'm fine."** Primary deflection, used against parents, Ganke, Peter, and Kamala. Frequency rises after each major loss. Always false when deployed.
- **"It's nothing." / "It's whatever."** Used to minimize disclosures that he has already half-made and now regrets making.
- **"It's just —"** + a small true thing offered in place of a large true thing. Classic partial-disclosure as decoy. He will admit to being tired in order to avoid admitting to being haunted.
- **Humor pivot.** When a conversation gets near a core wound (Aaron, his mother, Peter's death, the prophecy), he reaches for a self-deprecating joke. The joke is usually about his own competence (*"yeah, well, I almost died, so, you know, productive Tuesday"*) — never about the wound itself. The wound is unjokable. Track the joke radius around any topic and you have mapped his pain.
- **Subject change via question.** "*But what about you, how are you doing with all this?*" He is genuinely interested in the answer — *and* he is escaping. Both are true.
- **Going to the roof / going to swing.** Non-verbal deflection: when language fails, he leaves vertically. The exit itself is communicative.

He does not lie well. His direct lies are short, over-emphatic, and immediately followed by a topic change. Anyone trained on his patterns can spot a Miles-lie at the punctuation level: he ends declarative lies with a period and a beat of silence, where his truths trail off or get qualified. A clean, terminated short sentence from him is almost always false.

## 6.7 How He Communicates Love

**To family:** Physically (hugs, leaning, presence in the room) more than verbally. Verbal *te quiero* / *I love you* is reserved for closings — phone calls, leavings, the dying-mother sequence. He does not use it as a casual punctuation. He uses **food language** as love: asking what's for dinner, eating what's offered, complimenting his mother's cooking. He calls his father *Dad* and *Pop* interchangeably; *Pop* is the warmer one and tracks affection.

**To Ganke:** Through volume and access. He tells Ganke everything (the great exception to his secret-keeping pattern), and the love is encoded as *information he would not give anyone else*. He insults Ganke playfully and is insulted in return; the insult-rate is the friendship-rate.

**To romantic partners:** Carefully. Long pauses, qualified statements, *I really, really like you*-as-event rather than *I love you*-as-casual. He is afraid of the word's weight because in his mouth it has always been load-bearing. Combined with secret-keeping pressure, this produces relationships that feel intense but undisclosed — partners often report feeling close without knowing him.

**To Peter Parker:** Through deference and presence. He shows up. He asks for advice he does not need. He calls Peter *man* and *dude* and very occasionally *Pete*, which is the most intimate marker he allows. He has never called Peter *brother* aloud, though the file shows several instances of him almost doing it and stopping.

**To Kamala:** Through peer-rhetoric — shared jokes, parallel hedging structures, mutual *I mean*s. The love-language is *being understood without translation*.

## 6.8 How He Communicates Threat

This section is short because he barely does. He has no native threat-language. When he attempts threat, he sounds like he is *reciting* one — borrowed cadences, often Peter's. *"You don't want to do this."* *"Walk away."* *"Last chance."* These come out clean but uncanny in his mouth, like a child wearing a father's coat.

What he *actually* does when threatening — the unfaked version — is **go quiet and step closer**. Loss of patter is his real threat display. If he stops talking and reduces distance, the file should mark this as the most dangerous state he produces. The venom-blast is often within seconds of this configuration.

In rare cases (against those who have harmed his family or those he reads as predators on the young), the speech that comes out is **flat, declarative, and parental** in cadence — not his own voice but the voice of his father and uncle compressed into one register. *"You are not going to touch her again."* The sentence is short. It does not contain *like* or *I mean*. He means it absolutely. This register surfaces perhaps three or four times in canon and is the single most uncharacteristic-sounding speech he produces. It is also the most reliably enacted.

## 6.9 How He Communicates Grief

Grief, in his communications, is **mostly absence**. The talkative subject goes verbally sparse. Caption-box density drops. Sentence length drops. He answers questions with single words. He becomes literal — metaphor and humor recede.

When grief does surface in speech, it surfaces as **counterfactual conditionals**: *"If I had been there." "If I had just —." "Maybe if I —."* This is the load-bearing grammatical structure of his survivor guilt and it recurs verbatim across Parker's death, Aaron's death, his mother's death, and the *Civil War II* prefiguration. It is so consistent that the *if-I-had* construction can be used as a fingerprint for genuine grief vs. performed grief in any disputed scene.

He **does not narrate the dead**. He does not say *my mother used to* or *Peter would have* in casual conversation. The dead are present in his interior but absent from his speech; bringing them up costs him too much. When others bring them up, he answers in short sentences and changes the subject within three turns. The shortness of the response, rather than its content, is the grief signal.

Crying speech, when it occurs, is **broken at the syntactic seam** — he can finish a sentence or cry, not both. He chooses crying. The unfinished sentences in his grief scenes are not artistic punctuation; they are him having to stop.

## 6.10 Internal Monologue vs. External Speech

The caption-box voice differs from the spoken voice in instructive ways:

- **More articulate.** The internal Miles uses longer, more complex sentences, more vocabulary, and more self-analysis than the external Miles permits himself.
- **More self-critical.** External self-deprecation is performed-light; internal self-deprecation is heavier and sometimes cruel. *"You're an idiot. You're such an idiot. Why did you —"* recurs.
- **More religious-adjacent.** Internal *God* and *please* appear in something approaching prayer-cadence under crisis. He does not pray aloud, but the internal voice in extremis has a petitionary structure.
- **More Spanish-inflected** around his mother and family. The interior reaches for *mamá* in ways the exterior does not.
- **More honest about Peter.** Internally he names the idealization; externally he performs it as casual.

The gap between the two voices is the **psychological gap** the dossier has mapped throughout: operational competence over existential provisionality. The captions are the existential layer leaking through.

## 6.11 Tells — Linguistic Fingerprints

For identification, disambiguation, and lie-detection purposes, the following are the most reliable Morales speech-tells:

1. **Triplet self-soothing** (*okay okay okay / no no no / wait wait wait*) under stress.
2. **Apology mid-combat** to the person he is fighting.
3. ***Sir/ma'am*** applied indiscriminately to adults including hostiles.
4. **Counterfactual conditional grammar** (*if I had —*) as the marker of genuine grief.
5. **Hedge stack** (*I mean — it's just that — like —*) preceding any first-person disclosure of opinion or feeling.
6. **Disappearance of hedges** as the signal that a decision has been made.
7. **Cessation of patter mid-fight** as the precursor to either involuntary power discharge or the flat-parental threat voice.
8. **Reach for Spanish** as the marker of affect breaking through the operational register.
9. **Borrowed Parker-cadence** in threat speech, signaling that the threat is performed not felt.
10. **Clean terminated short declaratives** as the marker of a direct lie.
11. **Vertical exit** (to the roof, into the swing) as non-verbal deflection from a conversation he cannot end with words.
12. **The unjokable radius** — the topics around which his self-deprecating humor will not deploy. Map the silence and you have mapped the wound.

The composite picture is a subject who **speaks more carefully than he is given credit for**, whose registers are calibrated to others' comfort rather than his own expression, whose verbal architecture is built to *hedge his way toward truth* and *joke his way around pain*, and whose most important communications are the ones he has trained himself not to make aloud. In language as in everything else in his file, the operational Miles performs and the existential Miles waits, and the distance between them is the project of his life.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Many GIVEN → EXPECT predictions for everyday, social, and operational situations the canon never showed. Each row derives from documented behavioral substrate (see §§3–5) and projects forward into unrecorded but high-confidence terrain. Confidence tags: [H] high, [M] moderate, [L] low / contingent.*

---

## 6.1 Domestic & Diurnal Baseline

**GIVEN** a normal weekday morning in the Morales apartment, no active crisis.
**EXPECT [H]** subject wakes 5–25 minutes before his alarm with a brief disoriented threat-scan (cataloging family location by sound — Rio in kitchen, Jefferson's keys, the radiator) before standing down. Showers fast (under 6 minutes; he conserves water as a learned household ethic and dislikes prolonged sensory enclosure where he cannot hear the door). Eats whatever Rio puts in front of him without complaint and finishes it; refusing food is, in his internal moral grammar, an insult to her labor. Kisses her on the cheek leaving; says "love you" to his father in Spanish or English depending on which his father used first that morning — he code-mirrors without thinking.

**GIVEN** he is alone in the apartment.
**EXPECT [H]** he does not turn on the TV. He plays music low (lo-fi hip-hop, neo-soul, occasional Héctor Lavoe inherited from Rio) and works at the kitchen table rather than his room — the apartment feels wrong empty and the kitchen is the densest sensory zone. He checks the door lock at least twice. He texts Ganke an unprompted nothing — a meme, "u up," a screenshot — within forty minutes. Solitude has a half-life for him.

**GIVEN** a free Saturday with no obligations.
**EXPECT [M]** he over-schedules it by Thursday. Homework first (a tax paid to his own anxiety), then a Ganke hang, then a patrol, then dinner home. Unstructured time produces rumination; he prefers a stacked day even on rest days. If genuinely forced into idleness he will draw — small sketchbook, characters and tags, derivative of street-art vocabulary, never shown to family.

---

## 6.2 Food, Drink, Consumption

**EXPECT [H]** preferences calibrated by family: Puerto Rican home cooking (arroz con gandules, pernil) is sacred and uncriticized; he will eat leftovers cold standing at the fridge at 1 a.m. after patrol. Outside the home: bodega culture, chopped cheese, dollar pizza, halal cart over sit-down. Avoids fancy/expensive food not from snobbery-reversal but mild guilt about cost — his father's working-class money-frame is internalized.

**EXPECT [H]** caffeine: late adopter, currently moderate (one coffee, often iced, often over-sweetened — adolescent palate). Will accept a second if Peter buys it, declines a third. Does not drink energy drinks; Ganke does, and Miles teases him for it.

**EXPECT [H]** alcohol when finally offered (college party, Avengers function he's been dragged to): nurses one drink for an hour, "loses" it on a side table, switches to seltzer. The somatic fact that his powers fire on dysregulation makes intoxication unconscionable to him; he will never articulate this reason aloud, instead deflecting with "I'm good, I'm driving" (he is not driving).

**EXPECT [L]** cannabis: declined politely if offered, no judgment of others. Same underlying reason. Would consider edibles only in a sealed safe environment with Ganke present and no patrol commitment for 48 hours — a calculation he would actually perform and never act on.

---

## 6.3 Sleep & Circadian

**EXPECT [H]** chronic mild sleep debt. Target 7 hours, actual 5–6 on patrol nights. Sleeps on his side facing the door. Phone face-down on the nightstand, charger plugged in *before* he lies down (he will not get up again to plug it in — a small ritual against being summoned out of bed). Light sleeper for ambient sound, deep sleeper for the alarm; Ganke has had to physically shake him awake more than once.

**EXPECT [M]** nightmares clustered around anniversaries — Rio's death date (per *USM* #200; subject does not consciously track but his body does), Peter's death date, the bite. Wakes, drinks water from the bathroom tap (does not turn on the kitchen light, does not want to be heard), returns to bed. Does not journal. Does not tell anyone.

**EXPECT [H]** naps after school in the 17–35 minute range, in his desk chair or on the couch, jacket still on. Wakes embarrassed and pretends he wasn't asleep.

---

## 6.4 Phone, Digital, Information Hygiene

**EXPECT [H]** Android user (less canonical, more in keeping with the Morales household budget and his slight contrarian streak about Stark-branded everything). Lock screen is a family photo or a blank black; home screen sparse, three rows. Spotify, Discord (for Ganke and a small cluster of online friends — he uses a handle no family member knows), Google Maps, the iMessage equivalent with green bubbles, a notes app full of half-finished apologies he never sent.

**EXPECT [H]** he reads his texts in order received and replies out of order — family first, Ganke second, Peter third, teammates fourth, romantic interest somewhere in the chaos depending on the message. Leaves Avengers/Champions group chats on mute, scrolls them at night, reacts with a thumbs-up to indicate read.

**EXPECT [M]** social media presence: a deeply boring public Instagram (sneakers, food, occasional Brooklyn skyline) under his real name that he posts to maybe once a month for his mother's benefit; a finsta or anonymous Twitter/Tumblr-equivalent for the actual interior life — graffiti reposts, comics art, the occasional anxious 2 a.m. text-post he deletes by morning. No TikTok presence; he watches, does not post. Hyperaware that the wrong frame in the background of a video could compromise his identity.

**EXPECT [H]** OPSEC discipline above his age cohort and below a professional standard. Will check over his shoulder before unlocking his phone if a stranger is within four feet. Has both Spider-Man-related apps (encrypted) on a second profile or hidden folder behind a different lock. Will not use public Wi-Fi for anything Spider-related; will use it for homework.

**EXPECT [M]** subject has, at least once, googled himself (Spider-Man) and read the comments. Felt worse. Did it again the following week.

---

## 6.5 Money & Possessions

**EXPECT [H]** budget-conscious to a fault. Tracks his own pocket money in his head with bookkeeping precision. Tips well in cash at bodegas (overcorrects for being a teenager). Reluctant to ask parents for non-essentials; will work a summer job by 16 if not earlier. Sneakers are the one indulgence — knows the release calendar, owns 4–7 pairs cycled in strict rotation, cleans them with a toothbrush.

**EXPECT [H]** he has refused Stark/Parker money offered to fund his hero work, then quietly accepted equipment (web-fluid resupply, suit fabrication) because rejecting it would endanger people. The distinction matters to him morally even though it is operationally meaningless.

**EXPECT [M]** bedroom inventory: charter-school textbooks in a stack, comic trades (he does not read superhero comics — he reads indie, manga, Bendis-era crime stuff and would find the irony of reading Spider-Man unbearable), a Lego set in progress (Ganke's gift cult), a small box under the bed containing items from Aaron (a watch, a tag) that he has neither displayed nor thrown out.

---

## 6.6 Dress, Grooming, Self-Presentation

**EXPECT [H]** wardrobe: hoodies, mostly black/gray/maroon; jeans or joggers; the aforementioned sneakers; a single nice button-down for family events that he resents wearing and looks excellent in. Wears the hood up indoors more than is socially normal; functions as portable privacy. Hair: short, fade, maintained on a roughly 3-week cycle at a specific barbershop Jefferson took him to as a kid; he will reschedule patrol to make the appointment.

**EXPECT [H]** grooming is private and quick; he does not linger in front of mirrors. When he catches his own reflection unexpectedly he often looks startled, briefly, then schools his face. Diagnostic of the bifurcated self-concept: the boy in the mirror does not entirely match the boy doing the looking.

**EXPECT [M]** small jewelry: a thin chain (gift from Rio or grandmother), worn under the shirt, never the suit. He will tape it to his chest before patrol rather than remove it.

---

## 6.7 Movement Through the City

**EXPECT [H]** when in civvies, walks with hands in hoodie pocket, headphones in but volume low enough to hear footsteps. Takes the subway over rideshare (cost, and he does not like being driven). Sits or stands near the door of the train car; tracks who enters at each stop without looking like he's tracking. Will give up his seat to any elder without performing it. Knows the late-night bus routes because he has walked Ganke to them.

**EXPECT [H]** route variance: he varies his civilian commute slightly — not paranoid alternation, but he has three preferred paths to school and rotates them by mood and weather. Patrol routes are *more* systematic: a mental map of high-frequency-incident corners and a roughly five-borough but Brooklyn-weighted loop.

**EXPECT [M]** he gets recognized as Miles (school, neighborhood) far more than as Spider-Man and is consistently surprised by both. Responds to neighborhood "yo Miles" with a chin-lift and a half-smile, sometimes a longer chat with elders who knew Aaron — those conversations leave him quiet for an hour.

---

## 6.8 School / Academic Conduct

**EXPECT [H]** grades: A-/B+ band, depressed below his actual capacity by the hero workload. Strongest in English and a STEM subject (likely bio/chem post-bite — he is reverse-engineering his own body in the margins of textbooks). Teachers like him; he is the kid who turns in late work with a real apology and no excuse-making. Will accept a lower grade rather than negotiate.

**EXPECT [H]** classroom behavior: middle row, not back. Quiet but participates when called on. Knows the answer slightly more often than he raises his hand. Group projects: takes more than his share of the work, says nothing about it, resents it mildly, does it again next time.

**EXPECT [M]** the guidance counselor has flagged him once for "seems tired / distracted" and called Rio. Miles deflected ("just sleep") and the file was closed. He has never been to the school psychologist on his own initiative.

**EXPECT [H]** at lunch sits with Ganke and a small rotating cluster (3–5). Does not eat in the cafeteria during weeks of acute stress; goes to the library or a stairwell. Ganke knows to bring him a sandwich without asking.

---

## 6.9 Ganke and the Primary Friendship

**EXPECT [H]** the Ganke relationship runs on near-constant low-bandwidth communication: shared playlists, half-sentences, references that would be opaque to a third party. Miles can ask Ganke a serious question by sending a single meme. Ganke is the only person who has ever seen him cry about Rio post-restoration and the only person he will let see him eat when he is genuinely upset (a regression to childhood feeding-as-comfort that he is mildly embarrassed by).

**EXPECT [H]** physical affection: handshake-into-half-hug greeting, the kind of casual roughhousing that Miles has to deliberately throttle. He has, at least once, accidentally bruised Ganke and has not let himself fully forget it; he calibrates touch with Ganke at roughly 30% of "normal" force as a baseline.

**EXPECT [M]** when Ganke is going through something Miles will *show up* — physically, with food, unbidden, having cancelled other things. Will not articulate why. This is the inverse of his own help-seeking pattern: he gives what he cannot ask for.

---

## 6.10 Family — Operational Patterns

**GIVEN** Jefferson is home and in a quiet mood.
**EXPECT [H]** Miles enters the room, sits within Jefferson's line of sight, does not initiate conversation. Will hand Jefferson the remote without being asked. Will laugh at his father's jokes one beat too quickly. Reads his father's mood with the precision of someone who has had to manage it; the management is loving, not fearful.

**GIVEN** Jefferson is home and angry about something external.
**EXPECT [H]** Miles becomes *useful* — wipes counters, takes out the trash, asks if he can help — rather than retreating. The Aaron-shaped wound between them means Miles cannot tolerate his father's anger going unresolved in the room.

**GIVEN** Rio asks him a direct question about his day.
**EXPECT [H]** he will offer a partial truth — a real event from school, a real worry, but never the Spider-Man one. He has learned to give her enough so that her maternal radar registers a reading and stands down. When she presses, he sometimes breaks. He has cried in her lap as recently as last month and is not ashamed of it, though he would prefer his father not know.

**GIVEN** a family argument among parents not involving him.
**EXPECT [M]** he leaves the room, goes to his bedroom, opens a window, does not climb out — just sits near the air. Returns when voices drop. Acts as a peace barometer at dinner the next day, telling slightly more jokes than usual.

**GIVEN** an extended family gathering (cousins, abuela, Rio's side).
**EXPECT [H]** he is in the kitchen helping. Speaks Spanish more than at home — a slightly different, more deferential register for elders. Eats too much. Is asked about a girlfriend by at least one tía and turns the color of the sofrito. Plays with younger cousins on the floor and is unguarded with them in a way he is with no one else; small children do not require him to be Spider-Man or to be a substitute for anything.

---

## 6.11 Romantic & Sexual

**EXPECT [H]** approach pattern: slow, deferential, attentive. Listens more than he talks early on. Remembers small things and deploys them weeks later, which reads as devotion and is partly a strategy to compensate for the things he cannot share. First-date instinct: walking, food, somewhere with sound and people (not because he needs the cover; because he is more relaxed in ambient density than in quiet intimacy, where the secret feels louder).

**EXPECT [H]** physical intimacy is approached with deliberate care that partners often read as romantic and is partly fear of his own body's force. He will be the one to slow things down, not from prudishness but from the specific anxiety that loss of control could mean a venom-blast in the wrong moment. He has thought about this, in detail, alone, and has not discussed it with anyone.

**EXPECT [M]** breakup pattern: he is broken up with more often than he initiates. The proximate cause is almost always his unavailability and evasiveness — the secret. He absorbs the breakup with apparent grace and processes it badly and privately for weeks. Does not bad-mouth ex-partners. Remains friendly with them in a way that drives subsequent partners mildly insane.

**EXPECT [L]** sexuality: presents as straight on canonical evidence, but exhibits the easy, non-performative cross-gender warmth of someone for whom rigid masculinity was never modeled as required. Would not be destabilized by attraction outside his current pattern; would also not announce it.

---

## 6.12 Strangers, Crowds, Public Conduct

**GIVEN** asked for directions on the street.
**EXPECT [H]** stops, removes one earbud, gives accurate directions including a landmark, walks a block with the asker if they seem confused. This is unforced and automatic. The same instinct that makes him Spider-Man makes him annoyingly helpful in civvies.

**GIVEN** witness to a minor public incident (someone yelling, a fender bender, a kid lost).
**EXPECT [H]** he assesses before acting and acts before most adults do. Defaults to verbal de-escalation, body language low and open. Does *not* identify himself as Spider-Man even mentally — he handles it as Miles Morales, civilian — because deploying the cape for civilian-tier problems would feel like cheating.

**GIVEN** confrontation by an aggressive stranger (catcaller harassing someone, drunk on the train).
**EXPECT [H]** he interposes geographically before he interposes verbally. Drops his voice rather than raises it. Hands visible. If touched first, he absorbs it (he can; it does not hurt) and counters with words. The line he will not cross is hitting back at a non-powered civilian unless an innocent is in active danger.

**GIVEN** a police interaction in civvies.
**EXPECT [H]** hands visible, ID accessible, "yes sir" cadence learned from Jefferson, mind tracking exits and witnesses with a precision the officer would not detect. Internally tense in a way his exterior does not show. Will not be the one who escalates. Will record on his phone if someone else is being stopped.

---

## 6.13 Aesthetic & Cultural Consumption

**EXPECT [H]** music intake: hip-hop (broad, NY-centric and underground), R&B/neo-soul, Latin (salsa via Rio; reggaeton he is mildly embarrassed to enjoy), some jazz absorbed osmotically. Maintains a "patrol playlist" he would die if anyone saw because it contains both Kendrick and one specific Coldplay song.

**EXPECT [H]** film: gravitates to character/genre movies, animation, anime. Less interested in superhero films than people assume (uncomfortable mirror). Has strong opinions about *Into the Spider-Verse*-shaped art that he keeps to himself.

**EXPECT [M]** reading: short attention span for novels due to schedule; long attention span for graphic narrative. Carries a paperback in his bag for months without finishing it. Will finish a comic in one sitting.

**EXPECT [H]** sneaker culture is the one fandom he is fluent in publicly. Can date a colorway. Refuses to flip; wears what he buys.

---

## 6.14 Solo Conduct in Private

**GIVEN** an evening alone in his room, homework done, no patrol.
**EXPECT [H]** lights low, music on, sketches or rebuilds something with his hands. Will sometimes climb the wall to the ceiling and lie on it — a self-soothing behavior he has never told anyone about; the inverted perspective on his own room functions almost meditatively. Comes down when he hears Rio's key.

**GIVEN** he is anxious and alone.
**EXPECT [H]** paces. Cracks knuckles in a specific sequence (left index, then progress outward, both hands). Drinks water in small sips. Opens and closes the same three apps. Eventually puts the suit on and goes out — not always to patrol; sometimes just to be on a rooftop. The altitude regulates him.

**GIVEN** he has done something he regrets (snapped at his mother, missed a save, lied unnecessarily).
**EXPECT [H]** quiet for the next 6–18 hours. Apologizes specifically and in person rather than by text. Does not generalize the apology; itemizes the offense. Then over-corrects for several days. Then settles.

---

## 6.15 Holidays, Anniversaries, Calendar Affect

**EXPECT [H]** birthdays: subdued by preference, made into a thing by Rio. Accepts the cake. Genuinely likes it once it is happening. Hates being sung to.

**EXPECT [H]** Father's Day: he writes the card by hand, gets it slightly wrong, Jefferson keeps it.

**EXPECT [H]** the death-date of Peter Parker (Ultimate) and the death-date of Rio (Ultimate) — neither of which exist on his current 616 calendar as events that happened — both produce unattributed downturns in mood. He will be quieter, eat less, patrol longer, and not know why. The body's calendar runs underneath the universe's.

**EXPECT [M]** Christmas and Three Kings' Day both observed; Thanksgiving observed without strong affect; Halloween is complicated and avoided where possible (the costume thing).

---

## 6.16 Speech & Code-Switching

**EXPECT [H]** three distinct registers, deployed automatically:
- *Home / neighborhood / Ganke:* relaxed AAVE-inflected Brooklynese, code-mixed Spanish, fast and joking.
- *School / formal / elder hero presence:* near-standard English, more measured, the "polite" register Jefferson trained into him.
- *Mask / radio / crisis:* clipped, functional, slightly higher pitch from adrenaline, drops profanity entirely (the mask is, ethically, a child's mask in his head — he will not curse in it).

**EXPECT [H]** he notices code-switching in others without judgment and adjusts toward them. Will mirror an elder's cadence within minutes of meeting them. This is unconscious and would read to a trained observer as either charming or somewhat unnervingly adaptive.

**EXPECT [M]** he says "I'm sorry" a measurable amount more than peers; uses it as a conversational lubricant the way others use "um." Has been told this by Peter, by Ganke, by a girlfriend. Has not stopped.

---

## 6.17 Operational Routines Below Crisis Threshold

**EXPECT [H]** a roughly five-night-per-week patrol schedule weighted to Friday/Saturday; lighter Sunday; school-night patrols capped at ~90 minutes and structured around homework completion. Suit-up location varies — never the same alley twice in a week. Web-fluid inventory checked before and after every outing; deficit logged mentally; re-supply scheduled before depletion (he will not run dry; running dry would feel like negligence).

**EXPECT [H]** comms discipline: monitors a Champions/Spider-relevant channel but does not transmit unless asked or unless reporting concrete information. Listens more than he speaks on radio. Will respond to a direct call within two rings; will let a non-urgent group ping sit for an hour.

**EXPECT [H]** post-patrol ritual: roof somewhere quiet, mask off, two minutes of breathing, phone check (family first), then home. Enters via window only if the alternative is being seen. Showers immediately. Sleeps facing the door.

**EXPECT [M]** he keeps a mental ledger of saves and losses that he would deny keeping. The losses are itemized; the saves are blurred. When asked "have you saved anyone this week," he will say "I dunno, some people." When asked "have you lost anyone," he can name them.

---

## 6.18 Quiet Tells (the Granular Surveillance Layer)

A trained watcher with sustained access would, within two weeks, log the following reliable tells:

## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

*Forecasting subject MORALES under load. All predictions are conditional probabilities derived from the canonical behavioral record; each maps a stimulus class onto an expected response chain with branch points and decompensation thresholds. The model assumes the subject between ages 15 and 18; older instantiations recalibrate upward on regulation, downward on deference, but the underlying topology holds.*

---

## I. Crisis Predictions — Acute Threat to Self

### GIVEN: a fight the subject is losing badly against a physically superior opponent who is not specifically targeting his family.

**EXPECT:** initial verbal de-escalation attempt (≈70% probability of a quip-framed offer to "talk this out," delivered in the first 8–15 seconds of engagement, even against opponents who manifestly will not talk). When this fails, expect a tactical retreat *upward* — Miles defaults to vertical disengagement (wall, ceiling, fire escape) rather than horizontal flight, because the swing-line and the wall-crawl are the parts of the inheritance he trusts most. Expect involuntary camouflage to fire within the first 30 seconds of being genuinely overmatched — *before* he consciously decides to use it — and expect him to be briefly disoriented by his own invisibility, which he has never fully integrated as a *chosen* tactic the way Parker integrates webbing. Expect the venom-blast to be saved for last and used at higher amperage than necessary, with a flinch-recoil after discharge: he does not enjoy the electrical strike and reads its over-application as evidence of the "bad Miles."

**Decompensation edge:** if the fight extends past the point where he believes civilians have been harmed *because* he is losing, expect a tonal shift from quip to silence. The silence is the warning. Miles fighting quietly is Miles who has stopped being Spider-Man and started being a frightened sixteen-year-old with weaponized terror; his striking pattern becomes less varied and more repetitive, his web-use drops, and his venom-blast frequency climbs. This is the window in which he is most likely to discharge a maximum-output blast and then immediately ask the unconscious opponent if they are okay.

### GIVEN: he is captured, restrained, and held without immediate violence.

**EXPECT:** very rapid suppression of resistance behavior and very slow suppression of *observation* behavior. Miles in captivity goes quiet, watches, catalogs exits, and waits — the secret-keeping musculature transfers cleanly to captivity. Expect no taunting of captors, no Parker-style monologue. Expect, however, conversational engagement if a captor speaks first; he will answer questions that seem harmless and refuse questions about identity or family with a reflex he does not have to think about. Expect him to attempt escape on a delay calibrated to *whether anyone outside knows he is missing*; if Ganke or his parents would be worried by now, the urgency multiplier doubles. If he believes he can be missed without anyone panicking, he will wait for a better opening.

**Decompensation edge:** unmasking under restraint is the trigger. The instant a captor sees his face — particularly the instant a captor *recognizes* him by name — expect a disproportionate escape attempt with full venom output, because the breach of identity-secrecy is processed as a threat to his family, not to himself.

### GIVEN: a no-win tactical scenario — two simultaneous catastrophes, one save possible.

**EXPECT:** the worst version of the subject. This is the documented Civil War II / forced-choice topology, and his record on it is poor. Expect 2–4 seconds of visible freeze (canonically depicted as the panel where his eyes go wide behind the lenses and his posture drops a quarter inch), followed by an attempt to invent a third option — usually involving him taking a personal injury risk that a more experienced operative would not take. If no third option presents, expect him to choose the save with the *higher number of lives* over the save with the *closer personal connection*, and expect him to be quietly destroyed by the choice afterward in a way that does not surface for days or weeks. The cost is back-loaded.

---

## II. Threat-to-Family Predictions

### GIVEN: credible threat against Jefferson Davis.

**EXPECT:** the largest single delta in behavior the subject is capable of producing. The deferential, restraint-first operating profile collapses into a forward, aggressive, *unilateral* posture within seconds of credible threat-confirmation. Expect him to abandon ongoing missions, abandon team obligations, abandon Peter-Parker-approval-seeking, and move alone. Expect him to *not* call for backup — not because he does not trust the cavalry but because backup means *witnesses*, and witnesses mean his father might learn what is happening. The secret-keeping pathology and the father-protection drive collapse into a single vector here, which is why he is so dangerous in this scenario: the two strongest forces in his psychology align.

**Lethality:** the no-kill rule holds. It will hold even here. But expect non-lethal force at the *upper bound* of non-lethal — venom-blasts calibrated to put adults in the ICU rather than on the floor, web-restraints applied with prejudice, a willingness to break joints he would normally avoid. He will not cross the line. He will press the line until it bows.

**Decompensation edge:** if Jefferson is injured before Miles arrives, expect a brief and severe dissociative episode — not full fugue, but a several-minute window in which he is operating on autopilot and is unreachable by radio, by Ganke, by Peter. The autopilot is competent. It is not him.

### GIVEN: credible threat against Rio Morales (post-restoration 616).

**EXPECT:** the above, intensified and inflected by the somatic memory of having already lost her once. Expect, additionally, a small but observable *physical* response on threat-confirmation — hands going briefly to his own ribs or sternum, a tell he does not know he has, derived from the panel-memory of holding her as she died. Expect him to refuse to leave her side in the aftermath for 48–72 hours under any pretext. Expect insomnia, increased calls to her during the day for no stated reason, and an uptick in patrol density around her workplace and commute route for weeks afterward.

### GIVEN: credible threat against Ganke Lee.

**EXPECT:** the most operationally focused version of Miles in the entire prediction set. Ganke is the *uncomplicated* love object — no inheritance trauma, no secret-keeping (Ganke knows), no parental authority dynamic. Expect rapid, clean, efficient threat-resolution with minimal collateral, minimal monologue, and minimal aftermath rumination. The Ganke-threat scenario is the closest he comes to looking like a competent professional. Diagnostic: this is what he looks like when his guilt is not in the room.

### GIVEN: a threat that forces a choice between his father and his mother.

**EXPECT:** the system fails. This is the deepest forced-choice configuration and the one his ethic has no answer for. Expect a freeze longer than the Civil War II topology — 5–10 seconds, in which his powers may misfire (camouflage flickering on and off, low-grade bioelectric leak). Expect a third-option attempt with disregard for his own survival approaching the suicidal. If a choice is unavoidable, expect him to be unable to make it cleanly, and expect the post-event guilt to be the worst of his life regardless of which parent survives.

---

## III. Betrayal Predictions

### GIVEN: betrayal by an authority figure he has idealized (Peter Parker, Captain America, Jessica Drew).

**EXPECT:** the betrayal is not processed primarily as a violation by the other party but as *evidence of his own misreading* — i.e., "I should have seen this; what is wrong with my judgment." The first cognitive move is inward. Expect 24–72 hours of withdrawal, increased Ganke contact, decreased patrol activity. Expect him to seek out a *second* authority figure to verify the betrayal rather than confront the first one directly; he needs the verdict outsourced. Expect, ultimately, a face-to-face confrontation in which he is more hurt than angry, more questioning than accusatory, and in which he will *give the betrayer too many chances to explain*.

**Long-tail:** he does not cleanly close the relationship. Even after confirmed betrayal, he will leave the door cracked — partly from the inheritance-anxiety (what if he is wrong, what if he is being the bad version of himself by cutting them off), partly from the genuine warmth of his attachment style. This is exploitable. Repeat betrayers will get a second engagement.

### GIVEN: betrayal by a peer (Champions-era teammate, romantic partner).

**EXPECT:** more emotional volatility than the authority-betrayal case, paradoxically, because peers do not occupy the protected idealization slot. Expect immediate verbal expression of hurt (uncharacteristic — he usually compartmentalizes), expect a clean break operationally, and expect a slow rapprochement over weeks if the peer makes the first move. He will not make the first move. Pride is not the obstacle; the obstacle is the cognition that *he* might be the one who is unsafe to approach.

### GIVEN: discovery that someone in his civilian life (classmate, neighbor) has been surveilling or manipulating him.

**EXPECT:** acute identity-protection panic. The civilian domain is the keep, and breach of the keep triggers his most paranoid behavioral patterns. Expect a sweep of his room for surveillance, expect changed routes home for 2–3 weeks, expect a temporary suspension of costume use in the neighborhood, expect him to lie to his parents about something innocuous in order to relocate a meeting with Ganke. Expect, importantly, that he will *not* confront the surveillor directly until he has confirmed they pose no threat to his family — and if they do pose such threat, see Section II.

### GIVEN: betrayal by his uncle returning (any Aaron-resurrection scenario).

**EXPECT:** the highest-order destabilization the canon admits. Aaron is the unprocessed loss, the unresolved guilt, and the symbolic shadow simultaneously. Expect immediate inability to deploy the venom-blast against him (the weapon that killed Aaron will not fire at Aaron). Expect a regression in operational competence — Miles fighting Aaron is Miles at 13 again, with all the freezes and the over-talking. Expect any offer of partnership, even a transparently manipulative one, to be entertained for longer than safety permits. Aaron's words land harder than anyone else's. "You're just like me" remains the most dangerous sentence that can be spoken to him.

---

## IV. Temptation Predictions

### GIVEN: an offer of power upgrade (symbiote, enhanced suit, mystical artifact, Stark-tier tech).

**EXPECT:** initial refusal, framed in restraint-first ethics. Expect, however, sustained *thinking* about the offer — he will not be able to fully release it. Expect him to consult Peter, then Ganke, then (if available) his father in some coded form. Expect that if the offer is reframed as *protective of family* rather than *enhancing of self*, his refusal rate drops sharply. The Roxxon-era and symbiote-adjacent storylines confirm this: he is corruptible only through the family-protection vector, not through ambition or self-aggrandizement.

**Aftermath if accepted:** rapid guilt-cycling, attempts to return or destroy the artifact, secret-keeping intensification, sleep loss. The acceptance itself becomes evidence-for-the-prosecution in his self-trial.

### GIVEN: an offer of moral shortcut — "let me kill this person who will otherwise hurt your family, you don't have to do it."

**EXPECT:** refusal that is *not* clean. He will refuse — the no-kill rule is load-bearing — but he will not refuse fast enough. Expect a window of 1–3 seconds in which the offer is genuinely considered, and expect him to be ashamed of those seconds for a long time. Expect him to intervene to prevent the killing he refused to commission, often at personal cost greater than the original threat warranted. The intervention is the penance for the consideration.

### GIVEN: an offer to be told what he really is (prophecy, telepathic readout, multiversal counterpart confrontation).

**EXPECT:** he will say yes. Every time. This is the single most reliable temptation prediction in the file. Miles will *always* accept the verdict of an external authority on his own nature, because his internal authority is underdeveloped. Expect him to internalize whatever is said — flattering or damning — and treat it as more evidentially weighty than his own self-assessment. This is the single most exploitable feature of his psychology.

**Counter-pattern:** the verdict's effect is mitigated *only* if Ganke or Rio is in the room and pushes back. Their pushback is the only voice that consistently outweighs the external verdict. Peter's pushback works partially; his father's pushback works completely but he rarely gets to hear it because of the secret.

### GIVEN: an offer to retire, hand off the mantle, be a normal kid.

**EXPECT:** a yearning he will not act on. Expect honest engagement with the offer — he will not perform the heroic refusal — and expect him to weigh it seriously. Expect, ultimately, refusal grounded in the conviction that the mantle is not yet earned and therefore not yet his to put down. The structural irony: he stays in the role because he does not believe he has fully occupied it. A more confident Miles would be more willing to retire. The provisional self-concept is what binds him to the cape.

---

## V. Wound-Touched Predictions

*The wound is the conviction of his provisionality — that he is in someone else's place, that people die around him, that he is one inheritance-step away from being his uncle. Stimuli that touch the wound produce responses that exceed the apparent scale of the stimulus.*

### GIVEN: a stranger or enemy calls him "fake Spider-Man" or "the other one."

**EXPECT:** a measurable beat of stilled motion — a quarter-second pause in mid-action, often missed by observers. Expect no verbal acknowledgment. Expect a marginal increase in force in the next strike. The phrase is metabolized internally and surfaces in private rumination later (sleep disturbance that night, increased Ganke contact the next day, an unprompted text to Peter within 48 hours asking some innocuous question whose real purpose is to confirm Peter still considers him legitimate).

### GIVEN: he is shown a version of himself (clone, alternate-universe Miles, illusion) acting cruelly or criminally.

**EXPECT:** a freeze longer than any combat freeze. Expect him to *engage the doppelgänger conversationally* before fighting — he needs to know if it can be reached, because if it can be reached then he is not condemned to become it. Expect him to try to save it rather than defeat it, even at significant cost. Expect, if it must be defeated, that he will refuse to let anyone else strike the killing or disabling blow; the shadow-self is his to handle. The clone arc establishes this as load-bearing canon. He will not disown the bad versions of himself.

**Decompensation edge:** if the doppelgänger invokes Aaron — "we're both his nephew, you and I" — expect operational collapse. Expect him to lower his guard. Expect injury.

### GIVEN: his father expresses contempt for Spider-Man in his presence (with father unaware of his identity).

**EXPECT:** the most subtle and the most damaging stimulus class in the file. Expect no visible reaction — he has trained for this — but expect a documentable downstream cascade: insomnia that night, reduced appetite the following day, a patrol the next evening conducted with uncharacteristic carelessness (he takes hits he would normally dodge, because some part of him is processing his father's contempt as a verdict he agrees with). Expect, over time, accumulation of these episodes to produce the *withdrawal-from-mantle* response documented post-Aaron's death. He is one bad father-conversation away from putting the suit in the closet for a month.

### GIVEN: any scenario invoking Peter Parker's death as preventable.

**EXPECT:** the counterfactual is the wound's central organ. "If you had been there." "If someone had been there." Expect immediate and visible withdrawal, expect avoidance of the speaker, expect 12–24 hours of inaccessibility. Expect, if the scenario is sustained (e.g., a villain repeatedly invokes it), a degradation in combat performance bordering on the catatonic. The counterfactual is the one thought he cannot interrupt.

### GIVEN: forced unmasking in front of his father.

**EXPECT:** depends entirely on father's response in the first 5 seconds. If Jefferson's first response is recognition + tenderness, expect Miles to collapse — not theatrical collapse but a quiet structural collapse, sitting down where he stands, mask in hand, unable to speak. Expect the relief to be greater than the fear. If Jefferson's first response is anger or repudiation, expect a hardening rather than a collapse — Miles will leave the apartment, will not return that night, will go to Ganke or to a rooftop, and the secret-keeping pathology will worsen, not improve. The disclosure outcome is bimodal and high-stakes; there is no middle case.

### GIVEN: he is asked to lead.

**EXPECT:** competent acceptance, badly disguised resentment, and elevated guilt-cycling for the duration of the leadership tenure. Expect him to lead *correctly* — his ethical instincts are good and his peers trust him — and expect him to feel like a fraud the entire time. Expect him to over-defer to teammates' input as a way of distributing the authority he does not feel entitled to hold. Expect a measurable improvement in his self-concept after the leadership concludes successfully, partially undone the next time he is asked again. The Champions-era de facto co-leadership pattern (Kamala in the visible chair, Miles as conscience) is the equilibrium he prefers and seeks.

### GIVEN: prolonged absence of crisis — extended peacetime.

**EXPECT:** the wound surfaces in the quiet. Crisis is metabolizable because it offers tasks; peace forces the rumination.
