Expect increased patrol density during peaceful periods (manufacturing crisis to manage), expect schoolwork avoidance, expect uncharacteristic short temper with Ganke that he apologizes for immediately. The "waiting for the other shoe" pathology produces poor functioning under good conditions. He is, paradoxically, more stable in catastrophe than in calm.

---

## VI. Decompensation Topology — Synthesis

The subject does not decompensate the way most high-load operatives do. There is no break, no fugue, no flip into a different person. The failure mode is *attritional*: he keeps functioning while the structural beams quietly bow. The signs, in order of appearance:

1. **Increased deference** — asking Peter or Cap questions he would normally answer himself.
2. **Quiet patrols** — the quips stop. The monologue stops. He works in silence.
3. **Power leakage** — camouflage flickering at rest, small involuntary bio-electric discharges when startled.
4. **Sleep loss, reported only to Ganke.**
5. **Father-avoidance** — coded as schedule, actually pathological.
6. **Mission-drift** — staying out longer than necessary, taking patrols that aren't his.
7. **The closet phase** — suit comes off. Days, weeks, in one canonical case over a year.

The closet phase is the floor. He has been there before. He returns from it not through self-permission but through external need: someone has to do this, no one else will, *I should have been there.* The cognition that put him in the suit at fourteen is the cognition that puts him back in it every time he tries to take it off. This is the operating engine. It is also the wound. They are the same structure viewed from different angles, and any predictive model that treats them as separate variables will fail.

He will keep going. He will keep doubting. He will keep being unable to fully claim the name. And he will keep, against the weight of all of the above, doing the work — quietly, competently, in someone else's place, until enough time has passed that the place is, by accumulation rather than by decision, finally his own.


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# UATU DOSSIER — SUBJECT: MORALES, MILES GONZALO
## Section 6: Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

> *Purpose statement.* This compendium catalogues every documented and inferable means by which the subject can be reached, calmed, persuaded, provoked, predicted, or destabilized. It is written in the surveillance-file register because precision requires it, but its operational orientation is **protective**: a clear inventory of his levers is what allows those who love him to guard them and what allows him, eventually, to recognize and own them himself. Anyone using this document to harm him is using it against its purpose.

---

## I. Architecture of the Vulnerability Set

The subject's vulnerability profile is structurally unusual and must be read against three baseline facts established in prior sections:

1. **His attachment system is intact.** This means he has *real* hostages to fortune — a living father, a restored mother, a best friend who knows everything, a mentor-elder he loves. Conventional isolation-and-recruit pressure tactics (the standard Cluster-B-vulnerable adolescent playbook) **do not apply** and will misfire. He cannot be pried loose from his anchors because the anchors are healthy.
2. **His nervous system is wired to the outside world.** Anxiety in this subject is not a private interior event. It produces visible electrical discharge and visible optical disappearance. Therefore *anything that frightens him registers somatically, externally, and often involuntarily*. He cannot bluff his physiology.
3. **His self-concept is provisional.** He believes his legitimacy is borrowed. This is the master lever. Almost every effective destabilization vector in this file is, at root, an attack on the conditional permission slip he believes he carries.

The vulnerabilities below are organized by access vector. Within each, levers are graded:
- **(C) Calming / De-escalating** — used to bring him down, ground him, restore function.
- **(P) Persuasive** — used to move him to a position.
- **(X) Provocative / Destabilizing** — used to disrupt him.
- **(R) Predictive** — used to forecast what he will do.

---

## II. The Inheritance Lever (Master Vulnerability)

Everything else is downstream of this.

The subject took the name from a dead boy. He has never fully metabolized the fact that the name is now his. Any input that **frames him as substitute, placeholder, copy, or understudy** lands harder than it should, because it confirms a private hypothesis he is already running.

**(X) Provocation vectors that reliably land:**
- The bare phrase *"the real Spider-Man,"* delivered casually, by anyone, in any context. He will not protest. He will absorb it and continue. The damage is delayed and cumulative. J. Jonah Jameson editorials, civilian asides, and offhand remarks from other heroes have all been documented producing this effect.
- Comparison framed as deficit: *"Peter would have…"* Even when Peter himself is the speaker (and Peter has done this affectionately, not realizing), the subject's interior monologue treats it as verdict.
- Being told he does not belong in a space (the Spider-Verse "anomaly" framing; the Web of Life rejection). He absorbs categorical exclusions as ontological facts rather than political ones.
- *"You only have the name because he died."* This is the unspoken sentence under all of the above; stated directly, it produces near-total decompensation. Avoid.

**(P) Persuasive vectors that exploit the same lever, benignly:**
- Framing a request as *"this is something only you can do — not him, you, because of who you specifically are"* moves him reliably. He responds to being seen as singular rather than fungible. Peter has used this. Kamala has used this. It works because it inverts the wound.
- Granting permission. The subject is unusually movable by explicit benediction from elders he respects. The May Parker / Gwen Stacy blessing scene (*USM* #5–6) is the prototype: he wept, then committed. Captain America's word ("you're one of us") in Civil War II had the same lift. Anyone in a position to bless him can move him.

**(C) Calming vectors:**
- Reaffirmation that the name is now his, said plainly and without qualifier. He does not need elaboration; he needs the indicative mood.
- Physical presence of someone who knew him *before* the bite. Ganke's company alone is regulating because Ganke's frame of reference is pre-mantle.

**(R) Prediction:**
- Whenever a public legitimacy challenge occurs in the same week as a personal-life stressor, expect withdrawal from the costume for 48–96 hours, followed by overcorrective re-engagement (a deliberately "Spider-Man-ish" act: a high-visibility save, a quip, a swing-by photo op). The over-corrective re-engagement is itself a tell.

---

## III. The Family Lever

The subject's family is his moral universe. The internal hierarchy within that universe is precise and exploitable.

### III.a. Jefferson Davis (Father)

The single most consequential figure in the subject's psychology. The father is the source of the *original* moral frame ("you earned it"), the holder of the contempt-for-vigilantes position that long predated the bite, and the unwitting cause of the longest sustained secret in the subject's life.

- **(X)** Any threat to Jefferson reliably produces the subject's worst tactical decision-making. He will abandon objectives, ignore tactical doctrine, and engage targets he should evade. Adversaries who have figured this out (Roxxon among them) have used it.
- **(X)** *Truth-disclosure scenarios* — anyone in a position to reveal the subject's identity to his father without his consent constitutes a leverage point. Even in post-disclosure canon, the residue is: *did I tell him, or was I told on?* The latter retraumatizes.
- **(P)** Jefferson's expressed disappointment moves the subject more than any other verbal stimulus in his life. Jefferson's expressed approval is correspondingly the highest reinforcer.
- **(C)** Time with his father in a non-hero context — kitchen, car, walking, watching something — regulates him faster than meditation, sleep, or any other observed input. The therapeutic mechanism is *being seen as a son rather than a symbol*.
- **(R)** If Jefferson is in any way at risk, the subject is **not** where his patrol pattern would predict; he is at home, on the roof opposite the apartment, or shadowing Jefferson's route.

### III.b. Rio Morales (Mother)

The somatic memory of her death persists across the universe-shift. He carries her loss in his body even though current reality has restored her.

- **(X)** Anything that *re-enacts* the conditions of her death — collateral civilian casualties in a crossfire he is part of, a woman dying in his arms, a hospital scene with a maternal figure — produces a brief but profound dissociative window. He will appear functional and is not.
- **(X)** Direct threats to her override every other operational consideration, including the no-kill rule's psychological stability. He has never crossed it. He has come closest when she was in danger.
- **(C)** Her voice. Recorded, in person, on the phone. Rio's verbal style — diminutives, code-switching to Spanish under emotion, the specific cadence of her *mi'jo* — is a regulatory input his nervous system recognizes pre-cognitively.
- **(C)** Cooking with her or eating food she has made. The sensory channel is direct.
- **(R)** On the anniversary of her death (which his body keeps even when his calendar may not), expect: insomnia, decreased patrol efficiency, increased risk-acceptance, and an unscheduled visit home.

### III.c. Aaron Davis (Uncle, deceased)

The shadow figure. Dead but operationally present in every decision.

- **(X)** *"You're just like him."* The single most destabilizing five-word string that can be addressed to the subject. Source matters less than content. He has heard it from Aaron himself (dying), from clones, from prophetic visions, and from his own interior monologue. Each instance produces a cognitive lockup of measurable duration.
- **(X)** The Prowler iconography — the specific costume silhouette, Aaron's gauntlets, the modulated voice. Visual triggers. He has frozen in fights with subsequent Prowler-equipped figures (the Aaron Davis from another reality; the Hobie Brown handoff) because the silhouette pulls him backward.
- **(X)** Any framing that suggests his powers are *Aaron's gift* rather than *his own development* — i.e., that the spider was Aaron-adjacent, that the bite was in Aaron's apartment, that without Aaron there would be no Spider-Man — lands on the impostor wound and the shadow wound simultaneously.
- **(C)** Reminders that *he chose differently than Aaron did at every branch point*, delivered specifically rather than abstractly. Generic reassurance does not work; itemized contrast does.
- **(R)** When confronted with a Aaron-coded figure (uncle-aged Black male criminal with a younger relative in danger), expect: hesitation to use force, attempts to redeem rather than neutralize, and over-extension into the figure's domestic situation.

### III.d. Ganke Lee (Best Friend / Confidant)

Sole peer in possession of the full identity disclosure for the longest continuous period. The relationship is structurally load-bearing.

- **(X)** Threats to Ganke would produce the most predictable berserk-state the subject is capable of, because Ganke is the only person whose knowledge of him is fully voluntary and complete. Loss of Ganke would be loss of the only fully witnessed self.
- **(C)** Ganke's specific humor — pop-culture-saturated, lateral, low-stakes — operates on the subject as a co-regulator. A single Lego reference can lower his shoulders.
- **(R)** When the subject is in genuine internal crisis (not external mission crisis), the destination is Ganke's room. Always. Sequence: rooftop alone for 20–40 minutes, then Ganke's window.

---

## IV. The Mentor / Authority Lever

The subject defers. He has not yet developed the internal authority to overrule respected elders, and he treats their words as verdicts rather than opinions.

**Authoritative figures, ranked by effect:**
1. Peter Parker (616). Functions as older-brother substitute. Single most influential voice.
2. Captain America (Rogers specifically; not Sam Wilson, though that bond is warm). Functions as conscience-validator.
3. Jessica Drew. Earliest blessing-giver; respected.
4. Kamala Khan. Peer-authority; he defers to her leadership in the Champions even though he predates her in the role.
5. Gwen Stacy / Ghost-Spider. Cross-reality elder-sibling; trusted with personal disclosures.

**(P)** A request framed as *"I think you should"* from any of the above is treated as instruction. He will execute against his own better judgment. This is a documented liability. The Civil War II self-surrender to Rogers is the prototype.

**(X)** An *adversary impersonating* any of these figures has a disproportionate access window. He will check, but the checking is slower than his initial compliance impulse. Skrull-type infiltrations, deepfake comms, and illusion-based attacks targeting him should *always* test mentor-impersonation first.

**(X)** *Withdrawal of mentor approval* — Peter telling him he is disappointed; Cap telling him he was wrong — produces a multi-day destabilization. He does not rebound from these the way he rebounds from physical defeats.

**(C)** Peter's physical presence on a rooftop, no words required, settles him.

**(R)** When uncertain about a moral choice, he will seek out a mentor before deciding. He does not decide-and-confirm; he confirm-and-decides. This is predictable enough to be a tactical pattern: route him toward a decision by controlling which mentor is reachable.

---

## V. The Somatic / Neurological Lever

His body broadcasts. This is the most exploitable category for surveillance adversaries and the most important to guard.

### V.a. Bio-electric Discharge

- Fear, startle, and acute anger trigger involuntary venom-blast. *Anyone touching him at that moment is hit.* This has produced civilian injury (early *USM*) and is a chronic source of his secondary guilt.
- **(X)** Sustained low-level fear (claustrophobic environments, prolonged surveillance awareness, sensory deprivation) degrades his control and increases discharge probability into the involuntary range.
- **(X)** Forcing him into physical contact under stress — restraint, grappling holds, hostage-shield scenarios — risks discharge he does not want. Adversaries who *want* to be hit by it (Electro-class energy absorbers; certain Roxxon-engineered armor) can weaponize this against him by *provoking* the discharge to feed.
- **(C)** Grounded contact from a trusted figure (hand on shoulder, embrace) does not trigger discharge and actively dampens charge. This is a known calming technique used by his mother and by Peter. The somatic memory of safe touch is intact.

### V.b. Camouflage / Active Concealment

- Triggers on the avoidant pole of his stress response. When he wishes he were not there, his body grants the wish.
- **(X)** Public exposure scenarios — being unmasked, being filmed, being addressed by a large crowd — can produce flickering involuntary camouflage. A tell, visible to a trained observer.
- **(R)** If he is hiding *visually*, he is *also* hiding *emotionally*. The camouflage state is diagnostic of his interior. Conversely, if he is fully visible and still, he is regulated.

### V.c. Spider-Sense

- Muted relative to Parker's. He compensates with trained reflex.
- **(X)** This compensation degrades when fatigued or grieving. His reflexes are still good; his early-warning is not. Adversaries who can identify a grief window can land first strikes that would not land otherwise. The post-*USM* #200 period showed this clearly.

### V.d. Sleep Architecture

- Disrupted reliably by grief, by unresolved interpersonal conflict, and by recent moral-ambiguity exposure.
- **(X)** Sleep deprivation amplifies every other vulnerability in this document. After ~48 hours, the impostor cognition becomes near-continuous and his secret-keeping fails into either confession or dissociation.
- **(C)** A full sleep cycle in a safe environment restores baseline more efficiently than any other intervention.

---

## VI. The Moral-Identity Lever

His ethical framework is unusually rigid and unusually load-bearing. It is also therefore precisely targetable.

### VI.a. The No-Kill Rule

- **Not negotiable.** Not because of a code he has adopted but because he has constructed his entire self-concept on *not being Aaron, not being the clones, not being the Capitol-steps vision*. Crossing it would not be a tactical loss; it would be an ontological collapse.
- **(X)** Any scenario engineered to force a kill — trolley-problem setups, contaminated weapons, redirected attacks — is a maximum-severity attack on him. He will accept enormous personal injury to avoid it.
- **(X)** *Making him watch* a killing he could plausibly have prevented produces an extended guilt-and-rumination state.
- **(R)** Faced with a binary kill-or-let-die, he will attempt a third option even when none exists. He will sustain the attempt past the point of viability. This is exploitable as time-purchase.

### VI.b. The Save-Everyone Default

- He does not triage. He will go for the civilian over the objective, for the henchman bleeding out over the boss escaping, for the bystander over himself.
- **(X)** Multi-axis civilian threat scenarios paralyze him because he cannot prioritize. This was demonstrated in the early Roxxon sequences and in several Champions-era set pieces.
- **(P)** A request framed as *"saving X also saves Y, and you are the only one who can do both"* moves him faster than any other framing.

### VI.c. The Truth Imperative

- Despite being a chronic secret-keeper, he believes in truth-telling as a moral good. The contradiction is sustained but uncomfortable.
- **(X)** Being caught in a lie — even a justifiable one — produces disproportionate shame and a compensatory truth-spree that has, historically, exposed information he should have kept compartmentalized.
- **(P)** *"Be honest with me"* from a trusted figure pulls disclosures he should not make. This is exploitable.
- **(C)** Confession itself is regulating. Once he has told someone the worst thing, his function improves measurably.

---

## VII. The Forced-Choice Lever

The most dangerous category in his profile. His ethic is *save everyone*. Forced-choice scenarios produce the worst version of him because they require him to be the kind of person his ethic insists he must not be.

- **(X)** Two-hostage, one-rescuer scenarios. Documented to produce extended decisional paralysis, attempts at impossible triage, and post-event self-flagellation regardless of outcome.
- **(X)** Choosing between a mission and a person. He chooses the person. This is reliable enough to be a tactical pattern.
- **(X)** Choosing between two people he loves. Produces the *worst* operational outcomes of his career. He will attempt to save both, often delaying long enough to risk losing both.
- **(R)** When forced-choice is recognized as forced-choice, he will burn time looking for an exit. *Time-cost is the lever*: an adversary buys the seconds they need.

---

## VIII. The Impersonation / Identity-Confusion Lever

The clone arc demonstrated that adversaries can attack him with *himself*.

- **(X)** A clone, alternate-reality variant, or impersonator with his face produces categorical distress: he cannot reliably distinguish their actions from his own moral responsibility. He will accept liability for things they did.
- **(X)** *His own face on a body doing harm* is the visual stimulus that most reliably destabilizes him. Photos, footage, witnesses misidentifying — all degrade his self-concept faster than direct accusation.
- **(C)** Itemized differentiation by someone who knows him (Ganke, Peter, Rio) restores him. The technique is specific: *"That was not you; here is how I know."*

---

## IX. The Public Legitimacy Lever

Partially metabolized; still active.

- **(X)** Press coverage questioning his identity, his right to the name, his relationship to Parker. He reads it. He should not. Ganke filters when possible.
- **(X)** Civilian misrecognition — being called "the new one," "the Black one," "the kid one" — accumulates. He never responds. The cost is invisible and real.
- **(C)** Civilian recognition by name — *"thanks, Miles"* or *"thanks, Spider-Man"* directed unambiguously at him — visibly lifts him. He remembers these.
- **(R)** On the day of any major press cycle that mentions him by deficit comparison, expect reduced patrol confidence and increased mentor-seeking behavior.

---

## X. Routine, Geography, and Behavioral Tells (Predictive)

A surveillance file requires the granular pattern. The subject is routinized in ways he does not realize.

- **Patrol geometry.** Brooklyn-centric, with a strong attractor toward his parents' building. Even when responding to Manhattan calls, he routes via overhead lines of sight that pass within visual range of home. Map his swings over a month and the apartment is the gravitational center.
- **Time-of-day pattern.** Late-evening primary patrol, post-homework / post-dinner. He does not skip dinner unless an emergency overrides. Dinner skipping is itself a stress indicator.
- **Rooftop preferences.** Specific water-tower in his neighborhood used for decompression. Specific spot on a Brooklyn Bridge cable for thinking. He returns to these. They are surveillance-vulnerable.
- **Verbal tics under stress.** Increased *"uh,"* increased question-marks in declarative sentences, code-switching into Spanglish in extremis (his mother's register surfacing). When he begins a sentence with *"so, like — ,"* he is buying time to choose between truth and lie.
- **Physical tells under mask.** Shoulders rise toward the ears. Hand goes to the back of the neck. Foot taps. Camouflage flickers at the fingertips when he is suppressing a feeling.
- **Post-fight ritual.** Sits. Catches breath. Calls or texts Ganke. Then home, then shower, then sleep or homework. Deviation from this sequence is diagnostic.
- **Communications hygiene.** Adequate but adolescent. Encrypted comms via Ganke's setup; personal phone is normal civilian-grade and is the predictable vector.
- **Costume care.** He washes it. By hand. In the apartment. This is a surveillance window his enemies have not exploited and his allies should ensure remains unexploited.

---

## XI. Anti-Recruitment / Protection Notes

Because the orientation of this file is protective, the inverse register matters: **how to make him harder to leverage**.

1. **Disclose, disclose, disclose.** The single most protective intervention in his life is reducing the secret-load. Each person who knows is one less person who can be used against him. The Jefferson disclosure was the largest protective gain of his career. Future disclosures (a long-term partner, a chosen extended circle) should be supported, not discouraged.
2. **Name the impostor pattern aloud.** When he says *"I'm not really —,"* the response should be *"That is the pattern. You are doing it now."* External labeling of the cognition degrades its authority. Peter has begun doing this. It works.
3. **Refuse the comparison frame.** Allies should not, even affectionately, compare him to Parker. The comparison reinforces the lever even when the valence is positive.
4. **Protect the rooftop geometry.** His decompression spots should be quietly secured by allies. He will not ask.
5. **Build his ground-truth network.** Ganke alone is too narrow a base. Each additional fully-witnessing relationship reduces the leverage available against any one of them.
6. **Reinforce the differentiation from Aaron specifically and itemized-ly.** Generic *"you're a good kid"* does nothing. Specific *"Aaron would have done X; you did Y; here is why that matters"* is structural repair.
7. **Sleep. Food. Mother.** In that order, in any crisis. The somatic baseline is the precondition for every other intervention.
8. **Permission, given early and often, by people he respects.** The mantle was inherited under conditional terms in his own mind. The conditions can be lifted by the people he believes hold them — and the people he believes hold them are still alive and reachable. This is the single greatest protective resource in his life.

---

## XII. Summary: The Master Pattern

Every lever in this compendium reduces to one operational fact: **the subject treats his own legitimacy as revocable**. Inheritance, family, mentor, somatic, moral, identity-confusion, public — each category is a different surface on which that same revocability can be pressed.

The adversary who understands this presses the revocability and watches the subject revoke himself.

The ally who understands this works, patiently and over years, to issue the permission slip the subject has been waiting for — and to repeat it often enough, and from enough mouths, and in enough registers, that the subject finally hears it from his own.

He is not yet


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# 6. STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE — THE POSITIVE LEDGER

A full asset map. The intelligence value here is not "what he can do in a fight" (though that is included) but *why his capacities are durable*: where they come from, what maintains them, and what conditions would have to obtain for them to fail. Most subjects in the costumed population present asset profiles that are brittle — a single relationship, a single income stream, a single belief. The subject's profile is unusually *distributed*: human, material, somatic, cognitive, and moral assets that reinforce rather than substitute for one another.

---

## 6.1 SOMATIC / PHYSICAL ASSETS

**Baseline platform.** Adolescent male, mesomorphic build trending toward lean-strong (sub-Parker mass; higher power-to-weight ratio than is visually obvious). Documented capacity for sustained rooftop traversal across most of Manhattan and outer-borough Brooklyn without resupply or significant fatigue: implied aerobic and anaerobic capacities in the elite athlete range, pre-augmentation. Post-bite, the platform is overwritten.

**Augmented strength.** Initially below Parker, by late adolescence (Ahmed run) approaching parity. Operationally: lifts in the multi-ton range, single-arm catches of falling vehicles documented in *USM* and the Ahmed solo. Crucially, the strength is **proportionate and controllable** — there is no canon incident of an inadvertent crush injury to a civilian, which is itself an asset (see §6.5 on regulation).

**Reflex and agility.** Reflex envelope comparable to Parker's; agility profile slightly superior in confined-space combat owing to lower mass. He moves *small* — tucks, rolls, and threads gaps that Parker, with more mass, would arrest. This makes him an exceptional indoor/interior operator: subway cars, stairwells, apartment hallways, the cluttered geometries of Brooklyn brownstone interiors.

**Wall-adhesion.** Stable, controllable, does not fail under his own anxiety the way the two novel powers do. Functions as his reliable substrate — when everything else is going wrong, the walls still hold him. This matters psychologically: the most basic spider-ability is the one he can always trust.

**Venom-blast (bio-electric discharge).** Unique to him within the immediate Spider-lineage. Tactical envelope: ranges from low-amperage taser-equivalent (used for compliance, non-lethal takedown) to high-discharge area effect (vehicle disablement, robotic-target shutdown). Operationally invaluable because **it is a non-lethal force-multiplier that does not require ammunition, web-fluid resupply, or environmental leverage.** It is the only spider-power that can end a fight without contact, restraint, or impact. For a subject whose ethics forbid killing, this asset is structurally load-bearing — it is what makes the no-kill ethic *tactically sustainable* rather than aspirational.

**Camouflage / optical and low-EM concealment.** Also unique. Tactical envelope: full visual concealment against most baselines, defeats most consumer-grade surveillance, defeats *some* enhanced sensors. Combined with wall-adhesion this produces an infiltration capability no other principal Spider possesses. Reconnaissance, escape, observation, the ability to *leave* a situation rather than win it — the camouflage is the only Spider-power oriented toward non-engagement, and it shapes his entire operational style toward de-escalation by exit.

**Spider-sense analog.** Muted relative to Parker's but functional. The dampening is, paradoxically, an asset: he has been forced to develop *learned* situational awareness — head-on-a-swivel, sightline checks, exit-mapping — that an over-reliance on precognitive twitch would have atrophied. He scans rooms. He notes exits. He counts hostiles. The muted sense made him a *trained* operator rather than a reflex operator.

**Recovery and healing.** Sub-Wolverine, approximately Parker-comparable; broken ribs and concussions resolve in days to a week. No documented chronic injury, no accumulated CTE-equivalent despite repeated head impacts. Endocrine and sleep architecture remain age-normative when not under acute grief load.

**Endurance and metabolic load.** Eats voraciously (canonically — Ganke's running commentary on his appetite); the augmented metabolism is well-supplied by an intact family kitchen. This is a quiet but real asset: many enhanced subjects under-fuel and degrade under sustained operations. Miles is fed.

---

## 6.2 COGNITIVE & EDUCATIONAL ASSETS

**General intelligence.** Above-average to gifted. The Brooklyn Visions / charter-school lottery (*USM* #1) is a competitive academic placement, and he retained it under operational load that would have washed most students out. Sustained academic functioning through the *Ultimate* run and into 616 college-track stories is itself a resilience indicator: he can compartmentalize sufficiently to hold a 3.x GPA while bereaved, secret-keeping, and patrolling.

**Lateral / consequentialist cognition.** Thinks in second-order effects on others. In tactical scenarios this manifests as: *what happens to the people downstream of this choice* — civilian evacuation routing, hostage de-escalation, environmental risk assessment. He is the Spider who notices the bus full of people behind the villain.

**Speed of moral reasoning.** Faster than his speed of self-trust, which is an interesting asymmetry. He arrives at the right answer quickly and then second-guesses whether he is allowed to act on it. The first half of that loop is an asset; the second half is the wound. But the first half does the work — under genuine time pressure, where the second-guess is foreclosed, his moral reflex is reliably correct.

**Metacognitive honesty.** He knows what he does not know. He asks. He goes to Cap when he is uncertain about Cap (Civil War II); he goes to Peter when he is uncertain about the mantle; he goes to Jessica Drew when he is uncertain about being Spider-Woman-adjacent legitimacy. Most subjects of his age and power-level do not seek consultation. He treats himself as a junior employee of a profession he is learning. This is a developmental asset of enormous value: it means he *acquires expertise* rather than calcifying around early errors.

**Linguistic and cultural fluency.** Bilingual (Spanish via Rio; conversational, not literary). Code-switches across Black, Puerto Rican, charter-school-academic, and superhero-professional registers without strain. This is a tactical asset for fieldwork in New York's actual demographic geography — he can talk to a Brooklyn abuela in Spanish, a Visions classmate in academic English, a Harlem corner kid in vernacular, and Captain America in whatever register Captain America requires, and all four read him as *one of theirs*.

---

## 6.3 RELATIONAL & SOCIAL CAPITAL

This is the densest asset category in the file and the one that most distinguishes him from comparable subjects.

**Rio Morales (mother, restored post-*Secret Wars*).** Primary attunement figure. Source of warmth, code-switched humor, the household's emotional weather. Operationally: feeds him, notices when he is off, hugs without preamble. Her restoration after *USM* #200 is treated by the universe as a fact and by Miles's nervous system as a miracle he is failing to deserve; nonetheless, *she is there*, and her presence is the largest single resilience factor in his life.

**Jefferson Davis (father).** Reformed, principled, stern. Once a source of risk (his anti-vigilante stance kept the secret toxic for years); post-disclosure, a source of enormous strength. Their reconciliation arc — Jefferson's eventual learning, processing, and choosing to support Miles — produces the asset Miles needed most: *paternal permission*. The man whose moral authority Miles internalized as judge has rendered a favorable verdict. This is irreplaceable.

**Ganke Lee (best friend, roommate, confidant).** First disclosure recipient. Functions as: tech support (LEGO-builder cognition transfers usefully to logistics, gadget-thinking, and improvisation), emotional release valve (the only person Miles is *uncomplicatedly* funny with), reality-check (calls him on his bullshit). Ganke is also a *boundary holder* — he insists Miles eat, sleep, and do homework. The presence of a peer who treats the cape as a *part* of Miles's life rather than its totality is a major protective factor against the identity-engulfment that destroys older heroes.

**Peter Parker (616, mentor / older-brother figure).** Asymmetric on Miles's side (he idealizes), but the relationship itself is robust. Peter has demonstrated, repeatedly and across crossovers, that he will (a) show up, (b) tell Miles the truth, (c) refuse the pedestal, and (d) extend explicit legitimacy ("you're Spider-Man too, kid"). The pedestal is Miles's pathology; the relationship is an asset.

**Kamala Khan (Ms. Marvel) and Sam Alexander (Nova) — the Champions core.** Lateral peer relationships with other young heroes who share the generational ethic. Kamala in particular functions as a *leadership scaffold* — she takes the role he won't, freeing him to operate as conscience-and-de-escalator without the dysphoric weight of being the front-of-house. The Champions are his *professional* friendships in the way Ganke is his *personal* one: they speak his moral language without requiring translation.

**Jessica Drew, Gwen Stacy (Ultimate), May Parker.** Legacy-adjacent women who at various points granted the explicit permission he could not give himself. May Parker's blessing in particular operates as a quasi-sacramental asset: the person with the most standing to refuse him chose to accept him.

**Captain America (Steve Rogers).** Senior moral consultant. Miles's Civil War II approach to Rogers — asking, essentially, *am I dangerous?* — establishes Rogers as a figure Miles can bring his worst self-suspicions to and receive an adult response. The fact that Rogers takes him seriously rather than dismissing the question is the asset.

**The wider Spider-network (Spider-Verse / Web of Life contacts).** Reachable in extremis. Gwen Stacy (Spider-Gwen), Miguel O'Hara, Peter B. Parker, the broader cohort. Functionally: he has *colleagues* across realities. Most subjects do not.

**Romantic relationships (Katie Bishop, Barbara Sanchez, others).** None currently stable, but the *pattern* is an asset: he is capable of genuine affection, sustained partnership effort, and respectful disengagement. The failures are diagnostic of secret-keeping, not of relational capacity. The capacity itself is intact and will, on present trajectory, mature.

---

## 6.4 MATERIAL & INFRASTRUCTURAL ASSETS

**Housing.** Stable. Brooklyn family home (Morales household), college dormitory (during academic terms), implicit access to Avengers and Champions facilities as needed. No housing precarity. This is non-trivial: many comparable subjects operate from instability that compounds their psychological load.

**Family economics.** Working-class but stable. Father employed; mother employed (nursing). No documented food insecurity, no documented eviction risk. Charter-school placement reduced education costs. He has never had to choose between rent and patrol.

**Equipment.**
- *Costume.* Currently his own design (the black-and-red Ultimate-derived suit), not a Parker hand-me-down. The transition from the Parker-knockoff suit to his own design is a documented identity asset — he wears *his* iconography now.
- *Web-shooters.* Parker-design or Parker-adjacent, supplied/supported via the mentor relationship. Web-fluid resupply is solved infrastructure.
- *Phone, comms.* Standard. Ganke functions as informal mission control on multiple occasions.
- *Champions/Avengers logistics access.* Quinjet-class transport available when needed; med-bay access; intelligence support.

**Geographic mastery.** Brooklyn, Manhattan, Queens to operational depth. Knows subway timing, rooftop sightlines, alley routing, bridge approaches. The borough is *his* in the way Parker's Queens-Manhattan corridor is Parker's. This is reconnaissance capital accumulated over years of routine patrol.

**Institutional standing.** Avengers-affiliated, Champions co-founder, Spider-Family-recognized. He can request resources from S.H.I.E.L.D.-successor organizations, the Fantastic Four, Stark legacy infrastructure. He does not abuse this access — the under-use is itself an asset (he does not deplete the favor pool).

---

## 6.5 REGULATORY & DISCIPLINARY ASSETS

This category is unique to his profile and deserves separate accounting.

**Premature emotional discipline.** Because his powers fire on his autonomic state — venom-blast on adrenal spike, camouflage on flight response — he has been forced, since age 13, to develop above-age affect regulation. Most adolescents do not have to learn to stay calm because their bodies are not weapons. His body is. The result is a 17-year-old with the breath control, the de-escalation reflex, and the self-monitoring capacity of an experienced adult professional. This is an asset extracted from a constraint: the somatic coupling that is a vulnerability under acute stress is, in the *chronic* register, a discipline-forcing function that has built genuine equanimity.

**No-kill ethic as load-bearing structure.** Not a rule he holds; a rule that holds him. Because it is non-negotiable and identity-load-bearing, it functions as a *decision-shortener* — under time pressure he does not have to deliberate the most consequential class of decision. The bandwidth saved is available for everything else. Compare subjects who relitigate the lethal/non-lethal question per engagement: they are slower, more morally fatigued, and more vulnerable to manipulation by adversaries who frame the question. Miles is not vulnerable to that frame. The frame is closed.

**Substance abstinence.** Total, documented, age-appropriate but unusually rigid. The rigidity is itself an asset: he will not be compromised by the standard vulnerabilities (intoxication, dependency, blackmail-via-substance). His body remains a reliable instrument because he does not contaminate it.

**Sleep, nutrition, study.** Maintained under load. Ganke is part of this; Rio is part of this; his own conscientiousness is part of this. He is not running himself into the ground.

---

## 6.6 MORAL & IDEOLOGICAL ASSETS

**Coherent ethical framework.** Articulable, internally consistent, and tested. Core tenets: people are mostly worth saving; restraint is identity; power obligates; family is primary. These are not slogans — they have survived contact with Civil War II, with the clone arc, with Aaron's "you're just like me," with the prophetic-vision pressure-test. The framework holds.

**Capacity for ethical creativity.** The Champions ethic — *change without punching* — is not a refusal of the work but a redesign of it. He generates novel solutions in scenarios where the inherited template would prescribe force. This is rarer than it sounds and is downstream of the same lateral-cognition asset noted above.

**Capacity to tell the truth eventually.** Critical. The secret-keeping is a documented vulnerability, but the *eventual disclosure* — to his father, to romantic partners under appropriate conditions, to himself — is consistent across the canon. He does not die on the hill of the secret. The disclosures are slow, painful, and complete. Most subjects of his profile take the secret to the grave; he does not.

**Capacity to integrate shadow.** The clone arc is the most rigorous test of this and he passed it. Confronted with literal fragmented selves carrying his uncle's instincts, he chose responsibility over disavowal. He does not split the bad-Miles off and destroy it; he claims it. This is the integration-of-shadow asset in its developmentally mature form, achieved earlier than most adults manage it.

---

## 6.7 RESILIENCE FACTORS — WHY HE DOES NOT BREAK

The single most important entry in this section. Subjects with his trauma load (predecessor's death, uncle's death-in-his-arms, mother's death-in-his-arms, reality-shift survivor effects, prophetic accusation, fragmented-self confrontation, sustained secret-keeping under family contempt) typically present with PTSD, MDD, substance abuse, or characterological deformation by his current age. He does not. The resilience factors that explain this:

1. **Secure primary attachment, intact.** Both parents alive and warm (post-*Secret Wars*); the attachment system that was forming when the trauma hit was already organized around availability and attunement. The trauma was processed against a *secure* base, not a *fragile* one. This is the single largest factor.

2. **Peer scaffolding that pre-exists the cape.** Ganke is not a hero-friend; he is a Miles-friend who happens to also know about the cape. The friendship's center of gravity is outside the operational identity, which means the operational identity cannot consume it.

3. **Mentor availability without mentor dependence.** Peter is reachable but not required. Steve is consultable but not authoritative-over-him. Jessica is a peer-elder. The mentorship is distributed across multiple figures, which means no single mentor's failure or death can disorganize him.

4. **A profession with a no-kill rule that he believes in.** Forecloses the worst self-corrosion path available to costumed subjects.

5. **Somatic discipline forced by power-physiology.** The constraint that makes anxiety dangerous makes equanimity practiced.

6. **The integrated shadow.** He has *met* his worst version (the clones; the Ulysses vision) and survived the meeting with his self-concept intact-if-bruised. He is no longer maximally vulnerable to the "you are secretly bad" attack vector; he has already processed it.

7. **A grief that was completed and then partially undone.** The *USM* #200 sequence — losing Rio, holding her, obeying her last instruction, surviving the year after — is, in narrative-medicine terms, a *completed* acute grief process. The post-*Secret Wars* restoration is somatic gift, not regression to denial. He carries the grief experience as data while having the mother back as fact. The asymmetry is uncomfortable but it is, on net, an enormous resource: he has been to the other side of the worst thing and returned.

8. **Functional capacity preserved across every trauma.** He has never stopped going to school, never become unable to leave the apartment, never lost the capacity to make a joke. The functional floor has held under every loss. This is the empirical marker of resilience and it is consistently present in the file.

9. **The eventual-disclosure pattern.** He does not let the secrets ossify into character armor. The secrets get told. The relationships get repaired. The pattern is slow but reliable.

10. **A self-concept that is *underclaimed rather than fragile*.** This is subtle and important. A fragile self shatters under contradiction; an underclaimed self merely accepts the data and re-evaluates. Miles, told he is not the real Spider-Man, does not break — he investigates. Told he might kill Captain America, he does not break — he investigates. The underclaiming that is his wound is also his durability: there is no inflated self-image to defend, so attacks on his self-image do not find a brittle target.

---

## 6.8 NET ASSESSMENT

The asset profile is *broad, redundant, and mutually reinforcing*. Strength is supplied by both somatic augmentation and learned discipline; legitimacy is supplied by multiple mentors and peers; emotional regulation is supplied by both family attunement and power-physiology constraint; ethical coherence is supplied by a framework that has been tested and held; resilience is supplied by a secure base, a peer scaffold, and a track record of completed grief processes.

The vulnerabilities documented elsewhere in this file (impostor cognition, secret-keeping past tactical need, deference past developmental need, somatic broadcasting of anxiety) are *real* and *operationally consequential*, but they sit on top of an asset platform that is, in this analyst's judgment, the most durable in the entire principal-Spider lineage. Parker's platform is held up by guilt and a dwindling number of survivors. The subject's is held up by living parents, living friends, living peers, a living mentor, and a no-kill rule he believes in.

He is, in plain terms, **harder to destroy than he believes he is**. The central project of his maturation — which he has not yet completed and which this file expects him to complete within the next operational decade — is the alignment of his self-concept with the actual robustness of his platform: granting himself the permission *to be* what the evidence demonstrates he already *is*.


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# 6. FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION

## 6.1 General Architecture of Collapse

The subject does not break the way most costumed assets break. The standard catastrophic failure mode in this population — psychotic break, dissociative fugue, addictive collapse, vigilante drift toward lethality, suicide-by-villain — is not on his probability surface in any meaningful magnitude. His secure base prevents the kind of structural fracture that produces those outcomes. What he does instead is *fail by attenuation*: he degrades by continuing to function past the point where function should have stopped, and the degradation is registered first in the body and the powers, second in the relational field, and only third (and last) in operational performance. By the time anyone external to him can see he is breaking, he has been breaking for weeks.

The collapse profile is therefore *slow, somatic, secretive, and self-punishing*. He does not explode. He compresses. The decompensation is centripetal — withdrawal of self from contact, with the costume as the only remaining permitted outlet — and it terminates not in violence against others but in a kind of *operational martyrdom*: he takes a hit he could have avoided, or fails to call for backup he could have called for, or stays out three nights running until something hits him hard enough to force a stop. The pattern is observable across *USM* #22–28 (post-Aaron), #200 and subsequent (post-Rio), the *Civil War II* arc, and the clone arc of the Ahmed run, with consistent structural beats across all four.

## 6.2 The Escalation Path — Stage by Stage

### Stage 0 — Baseline Strain (chronically present)

Even in equilibrium the subject runs hotter than is healthy. The somatic-coupled powers mean his nervous system is rarely fully parasympathetic; the secret-keeping load means there is always information being held back from at least one person he loves; the impostor cognition means baseline self-evaluation runs at a deficit. This is his floor, not a warning sign. *Detection signature:* sleep at the lower end of adolescent norms (six hours, fragmented), Ganke's couch occupied more nights than the dorm bed, intermittent loss of appetite around exam-and-patrol overlap weeks, slightly elevated startle.

### Stage 1 — Mild Stress (acute event within manageable load)

Triggered by single-event bad nights: a civilian he could not reach in time, a fight that went longer than expected, a near-disclosure with his father, a Peter Parker comparison delivered by a stranger. *Observable shift:* humor sharpens and turns inward; the self-deprecating tics tighten in cadence; deference to anyone older in the room increases visibly; he asks more questions and offers fewer opinions. *Somatic:* mild involuntary flickering of camouflage when startled — a fingertip going translucent for a half-second before he notices and resolves it. Texts to Ganke become shorter; calls to his mother become longer and more frequent (a tell — he is checking that she is alive). Sleep drops another hour. *Risk at this stage:* negligible operationally. He is at this level constantly and operates well. The danger is that Stage 1 has become indistinguishable from baseline and his contacts have stopped registering it as elevation.

### Stage 2 — Moderate Stress (sustained load, accumulating)

Triggered by serial weeks of bad outcomes, an unresolved relational rupture, a public legitimacy attack, or any scenario in which he is positioned by an authority figure as comparable to a harmful person. *Cognitive:* rumination becomes the dominant cognitive activity; counterfactual loops ("if I had swung two seconds earlier") replace forward planning; decision latency increases on morally ambiguous calls while combat reflex remains intact. *Behavioral:* over-functioning. Patrol hours expand. He takes calls he should pass to other heroes. He starts answering for the rest of the Champions in conversations because deferring questions feels like exposing them. Homework completion degrades but is concealed; grades held up by raw cognitive surplus. *Somatic:* venom-blast involuntarily firing on contact when startled — the bodega owner who claps him on the shoulder, the teammate who hugs him from behind. He apologizes profusely. He stops letting people touch him from behind. Camouflage activates in elevators and crowded subway cars and he has to consciously suppress it. Sleep around four hours, with the remaining hours occupied by patrol or by lying awake running the rumination loops. *Relational:* Ganke is the first to register the change and is also the first to be lied to about it ("I'm fine, just finals"). Mother registers it second and is lied to with greater effort. Father is not engaged enough in the day-to-day to detect it unless something forces his attention. Peter Parker, if present, registers it instantly and is rebuffed gently. *Risk at this stage:* mounting. He will not yet take a bad hit, but he is one bad night from Stage 3.

### Stage 3 — Acute Decompensation (the visible failure)

Triggered by a catalyst event on top of accumulated Stage 2 load. The catalysts are stereotyped across canon: (a) death or grievous injury of someone he failed to protect; (b) being publicly accused of being like Aaron, like a clone, like the figure in the prophecy; (c) forced disclosure or near-disclosure to his father against his will; (d) a forced-choice scenario in which the *save everyone* ethic cannot be satisfied. *Cognitive:* the bifurcated self-concept collapses — the operational and the existential merge, and the existential wins. He genuinely believes, in this stage, that he is the impostor he has always suspected himself to be. The thought presents not as catastrophic but as relieving: *finally, the truth is confirmed*. This is the most dangerous moment in his decompensation curve because the relief makes the conclusion feel correct. *Behavioral:* one of two configurations:

- **Vanishing configuration.** Withdrawal from contact. Camouflage stops being involuntary and becomes preferred. He routes home along rooftops instead of streets to avoid being seen. He stops answering Ganke. He answers his mother in monosyllables. He sleeps on a water tower rather than in his bed because the bed implies a person who deserves it. He patrols alone, signal off, comms muted. This is the *post-Aaron* and *post-Rio* configuration and the dominant one.

- **Lashing-out configuration.** Rarer. The venom-blast becomes the first response rather than the last. He hits harder than the situation requires and is appalled by it after. He cannot stand to be touched. He picks fights he could have de-escalated, then loses sleep over having picked them. The shame loop from these episodes is severe enough that the configuration is self-limiting — he scares himself back into the vanishing mode within days.

*Somatic:* the involuntary power activation becomes constant. He cannot reliably stay visible in stressful conversation. His electric field becomes detectable to other enhanced parties as a low hum. Appetite collapses. Sleep collapses to two-to-three hours per cycle, frequently zero. *Relational:* Ganke escalates from concerned to alarmed and starts withholding the patrol-suit pieces he secretly maintains, or threatens to. Mother (when alive / in 616) starts asking direct questions. Father senses something and pushes; this push is the variable that determines whether Stage 3 resolves or progresses to Stage 4. *Operational:* combat performance still high but tactically narrowed. He takes hits he should have avoided. He does not call for backup. He starts treating injury as deserved rather than as data.

### Stage 4 — Crisis (the failure that forces external intervention)

He does not have a Stage 5. Stage 4 is the floor. The pattern at this stage is *not* breakdown into incapacity — it is breakdown into *over-capacity in a single direction*. He becomes a Spider-Man who does nothing but Spider-Man, twenty hours a day, until something stops him. The body fails before the will does. Stage 4 typically terminates in one of:

- **Forced-rest injury.** A hit hard enough to put him down for a week. He accepts this gratefully — the injury is permission to stop. This is the most common termination in the canon (concussions, broken ribs, the Venom encounters). *Detection signature:* he does not protest the bed-rest the way an undamaged operator would.
- **Forced disclosure.** Someone — Ganke, Peter, the mother, eventually the father — breaks through. The disclosure is the actual therapeutic event. He weeps. The weeping is disproportionate to the immediate trigger and proportionate to the accumulated months. *USM* canon repeats this beat: the tears are the discharge of Stages 2 and 3, not a response to the conversation in the room.
- **Operational withdrawal.** He quits. He puts the costume in a drawer and refuses it for months or longer. This happened after the Aaron event and was sustained for over a year. It is presented in canon as collapse but functions, in the file, as *self-administered medical leave*. He returns when he has metabolized enough to return; the return is always triggered by external need, never by internal readiness.

Crucially: there is no Stage in which he turns. There is no Stage in which he kills. There is no Stage in which he becomes Aaron. The clone arc was the canon's stress-test of this proposition and the proposition held — the "bad Miles" had to be externalized into separate bodies because the actual subject cannot generate that material from inside himself.

## 6.3 The Specific Decompensation Signatures

A surveillance file would catalogue the granular tells. The following are the high-confidence signatures, ordered by detectability:

**Somatic / power-coupled signatures.**
- *Fingertip flicker.* Earliest tell. The distal phalanges of the dominant (right) hand lose opacity for fractions of a second under acute stimulus. He has learned to keep that hand in a pocket or behind his back during difficult conversations.
- *Static discharge on contact.* The unintended shock to a friendly hand. Frequency rises monotonically with stress load and is the most reliable Stage 2 marker.
- *Low-amplitude electric hum.* Detectable only to enhanced sensors / enhanced individuals. Present at Stage 3 and indicates the bioelectric system is no longer fully damped.
- *Camouflage drift in mirrors.* He avoids mirrors at Stage 3. The reflection sometimes does not fully resolve and the dissonance produces a panic spike that itself triggers more camouflage.
- *Sleep posture.* Reverts to a tight curl, often on a ceiling or elevated surface rather than horizontal. The ceiling is a regression to the early-mantle period and reliably indicates Stage 3.

**Verbal / cognitive signatures.**
- *Apology inflation.* Baseline apology rate is already high; at Stage 2 it doubles; at Stage 3 he apologizes for being in rooms.
- *Reference to Peter Parker increases* under stress, not decreases. He invokes the predecessor as a yardstick more often when he feels less worthy.
- *Pronoun shift in self-narration.* In interior monologue (as depicted in canon), under Stage 3 he begins referring to Spider-Man in the third person — *Spider-Man should have been there*, not *I should have been there*. This is the linguistic signature of the existential/operational split widening.
- *Counterfactual saturation.* Sentences begin with *"if I had —"* more than half the time. He cannot finish a debrief without one.

**Behavioral / routine signatures.**
- *Route narrowing.* In Stage 2 his swing paths become repetitive — same rooftops, same vantage points, same bodega for after-patrol food. The narrowing is a self-soothing routine.
- *Route disappearance.* In Stage 3 the routes become unpredictable and aerial — he stops touching the ground for entire patrols. The street feels like exposure.
- *Phone latency.* Reply times to Ganke increase from minutes to hours to days across the stages. Reply times to his mother are protected and remain fast at the cost of everything else.
- *Costume care lapses.* He is normally fastidious — repairs the suit himself, keeps the mask clean. Under Stage 3 the suit accumulates damage he does not repair. The damage is, in effect, a worn record of the period he is not metabolizing.
- *Headphone use increases.* He retreats into music as a way of imposing a private audio environment on a world that is too loud. Specific tracks repeat. Volume rises.

**Relational signatures.**
- *Withdrawal from Ganke first.* Ganke is the closest to the system and therefore the first relationship sacrificed when the system is failing, because Ganke is the most likely to see and to name it.
- *Increased physical proximity to mother* (when alive / present), decreased verbal content. He sits in the kitchen while she cooks and says little. This is the regression to pre-verbal comfort-seeking and is one of the most reliable Stage 3 markers.
- *Avoidance of father.* The opposite valence: father represents the unresolved Aaron-disclosure axis and proximity to him under stress is intolerable. He invents reasons to be elsewhere.
- *Permission-seeking from elder heroes intensifies.* He will go out of his way to be seen by Captain America, by Jessica Drew, by Peter — looking for an external verdict that he is still acceptable.

## 6.4 The Conditions That Produce Collapse

Six condition-classes reliably move him up the stages. They are not equally weighted; the first two are existential, the rest catalytic.

1. **The Aaron-resonance condition.** Any framing — by an enemy, an authority figure, a precognition, a clone, a stranger on a podcast — that asserts moral or structural equivalence between him and his uncle. This is the single most potent destabilizer because his entire ethical architecture is built as a refutation of it, and the assertion forces him to re-litigate the refutation rather than rest on it. Aaron's dying line is the recurring intrusive thought and the catalyst that the canon returns to.

2. **The legitimacy condition.** Public, sustained denial of his right to the name. Not the trivial form (a J. Jonah Jameson editorial; he can metabolize this) but the credentialed form — another hero, Parker's actual family, or the metaphysics of the Web of Life itself telling him he does not belong. *Spider-Verse*'s framing of him as anomalous was a sustained Stage 2 event for him.

3. **The forced-choice condition.** Scenarios in which his *save everyone* ethic is mechanically impossible — two civilians, one of him, one rescue. He will perform competently and decompensate after. The decompensation is not proportional to the loss; it is proportional to the violation of the operating principle, which destabilizes the principle itself.

4. **The disclosure-pressure condition.** Any sustained pressure toward, or near-miss of, identity disclosure to his father against his readiness. His mother's last instruction is internalized as a moral injunction, and the pressure to violate it operates with the force of a parental command being countermanded by another parental command. He becomes briefly incoherent in these scenarios.

5. **The bereavement-anniversary condition.** Stress-load elevation in temporal proximity to the dates of Parker's death, Aaron's death, and his mother's death. He does not mark these consciously and would deny their effect, but the somatic and behavioral signatures elevate predictably in those windows. A surveillance file would calendar them.

6. **The authority-imposition condition.** Being formally placed in command. The Champions worked because Kamala led; he was the conscience. Any structure that puts him at the top of a chain elevates him into Stage 2 within days. He discharges the role competently and resents it the entire time.

## 6.5 What His Collapse Does Not Look Like

The file should be explicit on the negative space, because the misreadings of this subject would be costly.

- **He does not become his uncle.** The probability surface for antisocial drift is functionally zero. The fear of it is the prophylaxis against it.
- **He does not kill.** Not under prophecy, not under provocation, not in grief. The line is load-bearing for his identity and crossing it would not be a regression but a structural collapse from which the personality would not return as itself. The canon has tested this and the line has held.
- **He does not betray.** The secret-keeping is inward, not outward. He does not flip on his allies; he does not sell out a team; he does not become an asset to an opposing structure under duress. His failure mode is to absorb damage, not to redirect it.
- **He does not lose the mask in public.** The compartmentalization is robust enough to survive Stage 4. Identity exposure has been threatened many times in canon and has produced disclosure to specific trusted parties (mother, father, Ganke) — never to the field.
- **He does not develop a substance problem, a sexual-acting-out pattern, or a violence-seeking habit.** The superego that prevents these in baseline is *reinforced*, not weakened, by decompensation. He becomes more rigid as he degrades, not less.
- **He does not become catatonic, psychotic, or dissociatively absent.** Even at Stage 4 the lights are on. He is conscious of the collapse as it happens; he simply cannot stop it.

## 6.6 The Recovery Profile

Collapse is followed, in every documented instance, by *slow* recovery driven by external relational intervention rather than internal resolution. The reliable recovery vectors are:

- *Ganke's persistence.* The non-superpowered best friend who refuses to be successfully pushed away is the most reliable Stage 3-to-Stage 2 de-escalator in the entire file. The friendship's value is in Ganke's refusal to be impressed, frightened, or excluded.
- *Maternal contact.* A meal, a kitchen, a question asked without judgment. Pulls him out of Stage 3 in hours when it works.
- *Paternal forgiveness or acknowledgment.* The highest-amplitude intervention in the file. When Jefferson explicitly registers Miles as Spider-Man with acceptance, the effect is structural and durable. It is also the rarest intervention because the disclosure problem is itself one of the conditions producing collapse.
- *Peer-hero validation that does not idealize back.* Kamala Khan in particular — peer rather than mentor — produces a kind of horizontal legitimacy that the vertical relationships (Peter, Cap) cannot supply. Peter's value is high but Peter's pedestal status feeds the impostor cognition even as Peter tries to refuse it.
- *Operational success at a non-trivial save without witnesses.* He metabolizes anonymous saves better than public ones. The absence of an audience removes the legitimacy-judgment loop and lets the save register as evidence to himself.

The recovery is never complete. Each stage-cycle leaves residue. The subject at seventeen is carrying the unmetabolized remainder of every prior cycle — the Aaron remainder, the Rio remainder (somatic in 616, full in Ultimate memory), the Parker-substitution remainder, the prophecy remainder, the clone remainder. The remainder is the substrate of the impostor cognition and the impostor cognition is the engine of the next cycle. The pattern is not progressive in either direction. He is not getting worse. He is not, by any measure that would satisfy him, getting better. He is *holding*, which under his load is itself an extraordinary act of structural integrity, and the file should record it as such.


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP — SUBJECT: MORALES, MILES GONZALO
## Section 6: Trajectory & Forward Assessment

---

### 6.0 Framing the Question

The subject is, at time of writing, somewhere between sixteen and eighteen years of age depending on the diegetic counter one trusts; he has been operational as Spider-Man for roughly four published years (substantially longer in editorial time) and has compressed into that interval a quantity of structural loss and identity-pressure that most costumed subjects do not accumulate until their late twenties. The forward question is therefore unusually live: he is not a settled adult operator whose pattern can be extrapolated linearly. He is mid-formation. The decisions he makes in the next narrative cycle — concretely, the next three to five years of his subjective life — will determine which of several quite divergent endpoints he occupies at thirty.

This section maps those endpoints, the fork-points that select among them, and the conditions that load the dice toward growth or catastrophe.

---

### 6.1 The Default Trajectory (Mean-Reversion to Canon)

Absent any extraordinary input, the subject's trajectory is the one the canon has been describing in slow motion since 2011: an asymptotic, frustratingly incremental approach to *self-authorized* heroism. He will continue to do the work, continue to do it well, and continue to privately believe he is doing it on probation.

Concretely, the default ten-year forecast looks like this:

- **Years 1–2:** Completes secondary education; matriculates at a New York-area university (the 616 continuity has been seeding Empire State / Brooklyn Visions College trajectories). Continues Champions involvement at reduced operational tempo; continues solo patrol in Brooklyn and lower Manhattan with occasional cross-borough engagement. Romantic relationships continue to end on the disclosure axis until one does not.
- **Years 3–5:** First serious solo command experience, likely thrust upon him rather than sought (the Champions inheritance from Khan if she steps back, or a Spider-team formed around a crisis). He will accept it visibly reluctantly, execute it competently, and seek immediate handoff. He will be told, repeatedly, by elders, that he is ready; he will partially believe them.
- **Years 5–7:** Disclosure to father becomes complete and structurally stable. (It has been partially disclosed at multiple points; the question is whether it survives a *second* major loss without re-encrypting.) Romantic stability becomes possible only after this. Career identity outside the cape begins to crystallize — most likely in an applied-ethics direction (law, education, social work, science-policy); he is too morally serious for finance and too people-oriented for pure research.
- **Years 7–10:** Reaches the *operational* maturity of a senior Spider-figure. The *existential* maturity — the integrated belief that he is not a substitute — lags by several years and may never fully arrive. He will be, at thirty, what he is at seventeen: extraordinarily competent and quietly unconvinced.

This is the *boring* forecast. It is also the most likely one, because the subject's defenses are well-organized, his attachment system is intact, and his ethical floor is high. Boring is, for him, a victory condition.

---

### 6.2 The Growth Vectors

Within the default trajectory there are specific developmental movements that constitute *growth* rather than mere continuation. They are listed in order of difficulty for the subject.

**6.2.1 Granting himself permission to use the name without internal asterisk.** The simplest to state and the hardest to achieve. The behavioral marker is not verbal ("I am Spider-Man" he has said many times) but *somatic*: the moment his powers stop firing on identity-doubt cues. When he can be called "the wrong Spider-Man" by a hostile civilian and not have his camouflage flicker, the integration has occurred. Current status: not achieved. He still flinches.

**6.2.2 Disengagement from Peter Parker as moral guarantor.** The relationship is healthy in form and limiting in function. Peter is structurally incapable of giving Miles what Miles asks of him — sanction — because Peter himself does not believe sanction is his to give. The growth move is for Miles to stop asking. The behavioral marker is the first major operational decision he makes without mentally check-ing it against "what would Peter do." This is harder than it sounds because the check is largely unconscious.

**6.2.3 Reframing of Aaron.** Currently held in a binary: cautionary tale / family shame. Growth requires the more difficult third position: Aaron as a man who loved him imperfectly and damaged him deliberately, whose death was not Miles's fault but whose *life* shaped Miles in ways worth examining without flinching. The clone arc was a first pass at this and stalled at the disowning stage. A second pass is the developmental work of his twenties.

**6.2.4 Disclosure to Jefferson as ongoing practice, not single event.** The fantasy of *the* disclosure scene — one conversation, after which everything is known — is the wrong frame. What he needs is the *habit* of telling his father things in something like real time. The growth marker is the first time he calls his father from a rooftop, mid-patrol, to report a scare. He has never done this.

**6.2.5 Tolerating happiness.** The "waiting for the other shoe" pattern noted in §3 is, long-term, the most insidious obstacle to his wellbeing. The somatic memory of his mother's death — present despite the universe-shift, never therapized, rarely articulated — generates a chronic low-grade anhedonic ceiling. Growth here looks like the capacity to enjoy a Sunday dinner without scanning the perimeter. Therapy would help. He will not seek it.

**6.2.6 Allowing himself to be led without being subordinated.** He is comfortable as a soldier and uncomfortable as a captain; the mature position is *peer*, which he has never sustainably occupied. Kamala Khan is the most likely catalyst because she has the rare combination of clearly leading him while clearly regarding him as her equal. The Champions arrangement is his developmental gymnasium.

---

### 6.3 The Catastrophe Vectors

The subject's failure modes are not the standard costumed-subject failure modes (corruption by power, escalation into authoritarianism, public-image collapse into villainy). His ethical floor is too high and his attachment base too secure for those endpoints. The catastrophes available to him are narrower and quieter, and therefore harder to interdict.

**6.3.1 The Withdrawal Catastrophe.** Highest probability. After a sufficient additional loss — Ganke, Jefferson, a romantic partner, or, on a sufficiently bad day, a civilian he could plausibly have saved — the subject's documented withdrawal response (he has done this once already, for over a year post-Aaron) extends into permanence. He retires the cape, returns to civilian life, builds a life of quiet usefulness in a helping profession, and carries the abandoned mantle as a private wound for the rest of his life. This is not a *bad* life. It is, however, a catastrophe by his own values: he will spend it convinced he failed the people he stopped helping. The probability of this endpoint rises sharply with every additional loss in his core unit. Current estimate: roughly one-in-four over a ten-year window, rising to one-in-three if Jefferson is killed or seriously harmed in his operational vicinity.

**6.3.2 The Confirmation Catastrophe.** The subject's habit of treating external moral verdicts as evidence about his own nature (Aaron's deathbed line; Ulysses's vision; the Web-of-Life anomaly classification) opens a specific vulnerability: a sufficiently authoritative *false* verdict, delivered at a sufficiently raw moment, could be load-bearing. If a respected adult hero — Rogers, Carol Danvers, a 616 Parker on a bad day — were to tell him, in extremity, that he is a danger, he is at non-trivial risk of believing it and acting accordingly (self-imposed exile; voluntary depowering attempt; submission to oversight regimes he should resist). The Civil War II arc rehearsed this; he survived it because the verdicts were ambivalent. A clearer verdict from a more trusted source is a live risk.

**6.3.3 The Forced-Choice Catastrophe.** Noted in §5 as a pressure point. The save-everyone ethic, when defeated by physics, produces in him not adaptive triage but durable, structural guilt. A single high-profile incident in which he is forced to choose between two civilians (or worse, between a civilian and a teammate, or worst, between two people he loves) and visibly chooses, could install a permanent loss of operational confidence. His powers, coupled as they are to his anxiety, would compound this — every subsequent engagement would carry a higher baseline of involuntary discharge, which would in turn produce more incidents, which would in turn raise the baseline. Feedback loop. Mitigation requires therapy he will not seek or a mentor he will actually believe (rare).

**6.3.4 The Clone Catastrophe.** The clone arc is unfinished. The "bad Miles" entities exist in the canon as externalized fragments of his shadow self. Should one of them commit a sufficiently public atrocity using his face and powers, two failure modes open: (a) the *public-legitimacy* catastrophe (Spider-Man is now a murderer; he cannot disprove it without exposing the cloning, which exposes him), and (b) the *internal-legitimacy* catastrophe (he is forced to confront the fact that his genome and neurology, in slightly different developmental conditions, do produce killers — that Aaron was not entirely wrong). The second is the more dangerous. It would not turn him into a villain. It would turn him into a hero who believes he is a villain who is *getting away with it*. Functionally indistinguishable from the Withdrawal Catastrophe but more punishing.

**6.3.5 The Identity-Erosion Catastrophe (low probability, high severity).** Multiversal events have repeatedly classified him as anomalous, out-of-place, narratively unstable. A sufficiently aggressive cosmic actor — or a sufficiently bad outcome in a Spider-Verse-scale event — could literalize his impostor anxiety as ontological fact: the universe agreeing with him that he does not belong. He is poorly defended against this because his existing self-concept already half-believes it. Mitigation is almost entirely external (other heroes refusing the framing on his behalf).

**6.3.6 The Quiet Erosion (background catastrophe).** No single event, no dramatic break. Just twenty years of unprocessed grief, untreated anxiety, secret-keeping that calcifies into the only intimacy style he knows, and an asymptotic approach to self-acceptance that never crosses the line. He ends up at forty as a perfectly competent Spider-Man and a man whose interior life is a museum of unaddressed rooms. This is, in raw probability, the most likely *bad* outcome — and the hardest to interdict because it never presents as a crisis.

---

### 6.4 The Fork Points (Open Questions, in Order of Operational Importance)

**Fork 1: Does Jefferson get the full truth and survive it?** This is the master variable. Every other psychological vector in the subject's life routes through the unresolved father-axis. Disclosure followed by paternal acceptance is the single most growth-positive event available to him. Disclosure followed by paternal rejection — or, worse, paternal death before disclosure completes — would install a wound of a kind he has not previously sustained, because every prior loss has been *survivable* by reference to the surviving parent. There is no parent behind Jefferson.

**Fork 2: Does he find a therapist or therapy-equivalent?** Formal therapy is unlikely; he is a Black teenage boy with secret-keeping baked into the operational core of his identity, and the culture he is embedded in (both familial and superheroic) does not push him there. The therapy-equivalents available to him are: (a) sustained dialogue with another costumed subject who has done the work (very few candidates; Sam Wilson is the strongest), (b) a romantic partner who knows everything (requires Fork 1 to resolve favorably), or (c) a writing/journaling practice (consistent with his cognitive style, never depicted, plausible). Without one of these, the Quiet Erosion clock runs.

**Fork 3: Does the next major loss occur before or after he has integrated the previous ones?** Timing is everything. Another Rio-scale loss in the next two years lands on un-metabolized substrate and tilts toward the Withdrawal Catastrophe. The same loss in five to seven years, after some integration has occurred, would damage him without breaking him. He has no control over this fork. His writers do.

**Fork 4: Does he get a Spider-figure he is older than?** The subject has never been the senior partner in a Spider-relationship. The arrival of a younger spider-bitten adolescent for whom he is the Peter — for whom he is the dead/distant predecessor's living representative, the giver of permission rather than the seeker — would force the developmental movement that mentorship from above has failed to produce. This is the most efficient growth lever available and is increasingly likely given editorial trends.

**Fork 5: Does he kill?** The non-killing ethic is load-bearing for his self-concept (§5). A scenario that forces or appears to force him across this line — even ambiguously, even via a clone, even via an opponent who dies of their own actions in his presence — would be a foundational crisis. Aaron's death already prefigured this; he metabolized it by locating causation in Aaron's weapon malfunction. A cleaner incident would not afford that escape. Survival of this fork is possible but requires immediate, intensive relational support of a kind he is reluctant to ask for.
